TMW-01 乘车须知 / Travel Notice

那不是普通的列车。
This is no ordinary train.

从伊斯坦布尔到维也纳，它沿途穿越的每一寸土地，都不乏弥漫的硝烟与战火。
From Istanbul to Vienna, each land it passes through still carries the echoes of gunshots and explosions.

在战前，它曾是奢华的象征。在战时，它一票难求，人们将其视为逃离死亡的方舟……
Before the war, it was a symbol of luxury. Now it is an ark, a way to outrun death, and everyone is scrambling for a ticket.

无人知晓的是，列车会挑选死亡之夜停下。
They have no idea that when night falls and the train stops, death comes aboard too.

在夜里醒来的乘客们，先是听见哭声，然后听见哀嚎。而当他们朝声音的来源寻觅而去时……
On one such night, a group of passengers awoke to the sound of crying. They followed it. Then the crying turned to bawling, and the bawling to wailing, until they reached it—

他们看见了那节本不该存在的车厢，无数血红的眼睛在尽头的黑暗中交替明灭。
A door that wasn't there before. And there, in a carriage that never was, in that place that shouldn't even have existed, blood-red eyes blinked in the darkness.

乘客们还未来得及发出尖叫，便被扯入黑暗，成为那永无止境的哭声和哀嚎的一部分。
Before they could utter a scream, they were pulled into the darkness, doomed to join the wailing of the dead and dying in their accursed chorus.

很快，夜晚会淹没最后的呼救。
As the night fell and the last slivers of light gave in to the darkness, their cries faded ...

鲜血遍地流淌，沉睡于黑夜中的怪物们悄然苏醒，静静吞咽那甘甜的热血。
And the blood of those sorry passengers trickled, sweet and warm, into the throats of the red-eyed monsters.

直到最后一滴鲜血也被吸尽，列车长终于现身。她在尸体间踱步，如仆从清点主人饱餐后的狼藉。
Only when that last drop had been swallowed up did the conductress appear. Walking amidst the shredded flesh, counting off each passenger the way a butler might inspect a mess left behind from his master's feast.

“……二百三十一、二百三十二。仪式已完成，本次旅程圆满结束。”
"... 231, 232. The ceremony is complete, and this journey has come to an end."

“欢迎再次乘坐我们的列车……”
"We hope you had a pleasant trip, and we look forward to seeing you again aboard ..."

“多瑙黎明号！”
"The 'Danube Dawn'!"

戴毡帽的男孩：“多瑙黎明号”……
Hatted Boy: The "Danube Dawn" ...

又喃喃念了一遍，男孩才恋恋不舍地合上笔记本，将它还给身旁的女性。
The boy mutters the words one last time, then closes his notebook and hands it back to the woman beside him.

戴毡帽的男孩：好久都没读到有关血食怪的新传说了，自从战争开始……谢谢您，好心的女士！
Hatted Boy: Ha! I haven't been able to read a vampire story since the war started. Thank you, kindly ma'am!

？？？：这只是我收集的素材之一。怎么样，还算有趣吗？
???: It's just one of many stories in my collection. I suppose it's interesting enough, then?

戴毡帽的男孩：当然！而且我还知道，一会儿要进站的列车就叫“多瑙黎明号”！
Hatted Boy: You suppose?! It's amazing! And the next train coming into the station is called the "Danube Dawn" too, you know!

戴毡帽的男孩：也就是说，它是血食怪盘踞的秘密基地，对不对？
Hatted Boy: Hah. So it's the same train, isn't it? The vampires' secret base!

？？？：看来你还没弄清传说和真实之间的分界线。
???: Ha, the folly of youth. Not yet able to discern fiction from reality.

戴毡帽的男孩：嗯……我认为很多时候，这条分界线也未必存在，很多传说都诞生于真实……您觉得呢，女士？
Hatted Boy: Well, it's not like these stories just spring up out of nowhere. I've heard all kinds of them that really happened. At least, I think so. What do you think, ma'am?

男孩朝女人眨了眨红色的眼眸，随后将帽檐压得更低了一些。
He blinks his shadowed eyes at the woman, then lowers the brim of his hat.

？？？：我的想法不重要，我只负责记录。倒是你……看来似乎有些特别的故事。
???: What I think is of little matter. I simply write what I see, and I see an intriguing story in you.

？？？：能告诉我你的名字吗？
???: May I have your name?

野树莓：我叫野树莓！很高兴认识你，女士。
Rubuska: Rubuska! My name's Rubuska. Pleasure to meet you, ma'am!

？？？：野树莓……是个有趣的名字，我记住了。我偶尔会记录一些故事，或许你能为我提供一些素材。
???: Rubuska ... An interesting name. I'll be sure to make a record of it. As I said, I'm a collector of stories, and you may just have something worth adding to my collection.

女士翻开自己手中的笔记本，闪亮的钢笔在新一页写下一小行字。
She opens her notebook, her shining pen tracing a line across the page.

野树莓：我的荣幸！不过您即将登上“多瑙黎明号”，而我只是在这里歇脚而已，恐怕我们之后不太可能会有交集了。
Rubuska: I'd love to, ma'am! But you're about to board the train, aren't you? I'm only here for a visit, so it's pretty much impossible I'll ever see you again.

？？？：这可不一定。
???: I wouldn't be so sure.

女士漫不经心地转动着指间的钢笔，从书页里抬起头。
She spins the pen idly between her fingers and looks up.

？？？：一个传奇的故事，往往是由“不可能”开始的。
???: Many a great tale started with the "impossible."

乘客Ⅰ：“血食怪”？哈哈，老掉牙的故事啦。
Passenger I: Vampires on a train, eh? Hahahaha, that old tale.

旁边传来一声感慨，显然不只一人成为了“多瑙黎明号”故事的听众。
The comment drifts lazily out from another passenger. It seems the tale has a few more listeners than expected.

野树莓：老掉牙？老爷爷，您以前听过这个故事？
Rubuska: Old tale? You've heard the story before, sir?

乘客Ⅰ：类似的故事没有几百也有上千啦。血食怪吃人、狼人吃人、野兽吃人……
Passenger I: No, no, not precisely, but many like it. Vampires, werewolves, wild beasts, and monsters.

乘客Ⅰ：说到底，本质都是人吃人罢了，还非要安上一个名头。这些写故事的人呀，就喜欢这么弯弯绕绕。
Passenger I: It's always the same story about the powerful consuming the common folk. Heh, storytellers have always been good at making their points one way or another.

野树莓：唔，我觉得还是不太一样……您觉得呢，女士……？
Rubuska: Uhh, that doesn't seem like the same thing to me. What do you think, ma'am?

野树莓转过头去，那位带来故事的女士却已经消失了。
Rubuska turns to look, but the woman who told the story has vanished.

乘客Ⅰ：哈哈，看来你还是相信血食怪的年纪。
Passenger I: Hahahahaha! You're young. You'll grow out of these tall tales soon enough.

野树莓：难道您不相信血食怪是真实存在的吗？
Rubuska: You really don't think vampires are real?

乘客Ⅰ：一趟列车在驶向终点之前，车上的人都死光了——在这样的故事里，有没有血食怪很重要吗？
Passenger I: Ah, I'm much too old to believe in that kind of rubbish. I don't see why it's necessary to even put vampires in that one anyway.

老人长长地吐出一口烟圈。他弯下身，揉着断腿和假肢之间那仿佛还在疼痛的残缺接口。
The old man exhales a long ring of smoke. He bends down, rubbing the raw seam where his prosthetic meets his severed leg.

野树莓：很重要。
Rubuska: Of course it's necessary.

男孩认真地点了点头，面向火车进站的方向。
The boy nods gravely, turning toward the direction of the oncoming train.

野树莓：在一个大家都会迎来死亡的故事里，血食怪可能是带来死亡的角色，但也可能会带来新生。
Rubuska: Think about it—the story's about death, right? And vampires kill, sure, but they also give eternal life.

野树莓：或许会有死人因为被血食怪咬了而再度苏醒。在那时如果没有血食怪的话，死亡就成了板上钉钉的事。
Rubuska: So, say one of the passengers is killed. The vampire can just bite them on the neck, and just like that, they're alive again! Take out the vampires, and now death is a one-way trip—the end of the line!

野树莓：总之，我不喜欢没有意外的、一眼望到底的故事——那可太没意思了！
Rubuska: It's way more exciting to have some twists and turns. I mean, where's the fun in a story you can predict from the very beginning?

乘客Ⅰ：噢……那你恐怕要失望了，孩子。现在到处是这样的故事。
Passenger I: Ah. You're in for a disappointment looking at things like that. The world is filled with predictable endings, usually predictably tragic.

老人指间夹着半截燃尽的烟头，轻轻点向车站一隅。
The old man, a half-burned cigarette between his fingers, gestures toward a corner of the station,

几道模糊的身影缩在角落，衣衫陈旧，脸颊也被冻得通红。
where a mass of figures huddle together, clothes worn, cheeks red with frost.

他们静静地盯着前方的铁轨，目光沉默而执拗，仿佛要从冰冷的铁轨中刨出一条活路。
Silent and stubborn, they've fixed their gaze on the frozen tracks ahead of them.

乘客Ⅰ：就像这些可怜虫，已经在这里守了好些天了。
Passenger I: Just look at those poor folk over there. They've been waiting here for days.

乘客Ⅰ：你觉得他们有钱买这样昂贵的车票吗？不过是饿着肚子，又吃不住炮火，来这里赌运气罢了。
Passenger I: How do you think their story will end? Do you think they have tickets in their pockets? Hmph, of course not. But they're hungry and afraid to face the gunfire, so they come here to try their luck.

乘客Ⅰ：可惜，这世上哪有这么多奇迹。
Passenger I: *sigh* But miracles are few and far between in this world.

男孩摸了摸自己空空如也的肚子，咀嚼着老人话语背后的深意，慢慢眨了眨眼睛。
The boy pats his empty stomach, chewing on the meaning behind the old man's words.

野树莓：赌运气？听起来很有趣……什么运气？
Rubuska: Try their luck? What sort of luck are you talking about exactly?

乘客Ⅰ：你不也一样吗？小家伙。
Passenger I: I'm sure you're well aware already.

老人意味深长地丢下一句，那双见惯风霜的眼睛静静地望着车站的深处，像是在等待一场即将揭幕的戏剧。
His weathered eyes gaze out over the station, as if awaiting a drama soon to unfold.

野树莓：老爷爷，您快把我说糊涂啦，我们不是在这里听故事的吗？
Rubuska: Hah, ah, you're confusing me, sir. Weren't we just talking about stories?

男孩弯下腰，拍拍自己膝盖上的灰尘，借着动作，他的目光在车站里缓慢移动的人群中逡巡着。
The boy bends to brush the dust from his knees. As he does, the crowd begins to move.

恰逢站台整点的钟声响起，站务员的声音从风雪中飘来。
At that moment, the station bell tolls, and a voice rings out over the din.

站务员：列车还有二十分钟即将进站。请大家排好队，注意自己的车票和行李……
Station Staff: The next train will arrive in twenty minutes. Please line up, taking care to bring all your belongings, and prepare your tickets for inspection.

平民Ⅰ：车就要来了……“多瑙黎明号”……
Civilian I: It's coming—The "Danube Dawn."

平民Ⅱ：一定要抓住机会……
Civilian II: This is my chance.

人们纷纷起身，向乘车处涌去。
The crowd rises and surges toward the boarding gate.

野树莓：我想我现在该走了，我的意思是……我的车就要来了，愿神保佑你，老爷爷！哪个神都保佑你！
Rubuska: Well, I better get going now. I mean, my train is here. God bless you, sir! Whichever god that is!

他朝老人挥挥手，随后也没入人群，像一滴水没入大海。
He waves to the old man before slipping into the crowd like a drop falling into the sea.

无人在意这小小的身影，人们现在只关心车票、远方的家人、即将进站的列车……
No one notices his movement; all they care about are tickets, loved ones far away, and the train about to arrive,

……以及手头棘手的工作。
along with a troublesome mission.

塞梅尔维斯：“多瑙黎明号”，一九一二年十一月三十日，靠站于……
Semmelweis: November 30th, 1912, the "Danube Dawn" is arriving at ...

塞梅尔维斯：血食怪……感染……
Semmelweis: Vampires ... Infection ...

塞梅尔维斯：重塑之手……
Semmelweis: Manus Vindictae ...

调查员的目光停在那个熟悉的单词上。
The investigator lingers on the name.

塞梅尔维斯：……第五次“暴雨”后的首次外勤任务，竟然就要跟重塑之手打交道。
Semmelweis: Didn't expect I'd be dealing with Manus Vindictae for my first field mission after the 5th "Storm."

塞梅尔维斯：根据已有情报推断，重塑之手安插的血食怪很有可能会登上这趟列车……
Semmelweis: According to current intelligence, the vampire working with the Manus is set to board this train.

塞梅尔维斯：我还期待着和新队友们一同合作，尽早达成目标收工。
Semmelweis: I was hoping I'd be able to finish this job with my new teammates. Get this done quickly.

塞梅尔维斯：现在看来，恐怕不会那么轻松了。
Semmelweis: It looks like this won't be so easy.

调查员叹了口气，拿出外衣口袋内的通讯器。
She sighs and draws a communicator from her coat pocket.

塞梅尔维斯：下多瑙河七十七行动小队，傍晚六点二十分，车站会合……
Semmelweis: Istros Operation Squad 77; rendezvous: train station; time: 18:20 hours ...

塞梅尔维斯：还是没有回音。我可没听说过“暴雨”会影响人对时间观念的认知。
Semmelweis: Still no answer. I never realized the "Storm" could affect people's punctuality, too.

塞梅尔维斯：……
Semmelweis: ...

塞梅尔维斯：好吧，最多等到列车发车……嗯？
Semmelweis: Fine, if the train arrives and they're still not here, then—Hm?

进入车站的人越来越多。他们涌入站台，紧挨着彼此，人数远远超过了一趟列车能够承载的数量。
More and more people stream into the station. The platform heaves with bodies, far beyond the capacity of a single train.

乘客Ⅲ：见鬼，别挤了！你们买得起车票吗？！
Passenger III: Don't push, damn it! Do you even have a ticket?

乘客Ⅳ：车还没进站呢，该死的……
Passenger IV: For crying out loud, the train isn't even here yet!

抱怨声不断响起，焦虑和不安开始蔓延。一时间，车站本就脆弱的秩序荡然无存。
Complaints rise, anxiety spreads. The fragile order of the station collapses.

焦灼的拉锯之中，一声惊叫终于打破了这岌岌可危的平衡。
A scream pierces out above the din.

傲慢的乘客：不，我的车票……！
Arrogant Passenger: No, my ticket!

站务员：先生，请把车票还给那位女士！
Station Staff: Sir, please give that ticket back to that lady.

疯狂的乘客：这就是我的车票！先让我上去！
Maniacal Civilian: What are you talking about? This is my ticket!

傲慢的乘客：你的车票？这么多双眼睛都看着呢，你刚才是怎么从我手里抢走票的！
Arrogant Passenger: Your ticket? You just snatched it from my hand! Everyone just saw it!

指责和劝导都没能对男人造成丝毫动摇。
The man remains unaffected by her scolding.

站务员：我们都有机会离开，先生！这趟列车不会是最后一班，请冷静下来，好吗？
Station Staff: Sir, there will be other trains. Everyone will have the chance to leave. I need you to calm down, understand?

站务员：车票都做了特殊处理，您没法用这张票上车——
Station Staff: Our tickets have been specially processed to prevent misuse, so you won't be able to use that ticket.

疯狂的乘客：下一班，谁能保证有下一班？！听着，我有第一手消息，今晚过后谁都别想走了！
Maniacal Civilian: Other trains? Hey, everyone! Listen to me! I have firsthand information that this is the last train out of here! It's now or never! No one's leaving here after tonight!

站务员：先生……请冷静！
Station Staff: Sir ... SIR!

嘶吼声与孩童的哭喊声交织在白茫茫的蒸汽中，迅速吞没了无用的劝解。
Shouts and children's cries intertwine with whistles and pops of steam, drowning out all persuasion.

疯狂的乘客：你们不知道外面已经烧成什么样子了……谁能保证我们明天还活着……
Maniacal Civilian: You don't know what it's like out there. We could all be dead by tomorrow!

傲慢的乘客：呵，冠冕堂皇的借口罢了！请把票还给我，再来发表你的英雄宣言——
Arrogant Passenger: Oh, enough of your blithering excuses! Give me my ticket back now! You can save your heroic speech for—

傲慢的乘客：啊！！
Arrogant Passenger: AHH!

话音未落，男人猛地将她拽了过去。
Before she finishes, he yanks her toward him.

拥有车票的乘客们发出惊叫，束手无策的平民们沉默着，麻木的眼神都落在他的身上。
Passengers with tickets scream. The ticketless stand silent, numb eyes locked on him.

站务员：先生！请不要冲动……
Station Staff: Sir! Please, drop the weapon.

疯狂的乘客：别拦着我。不然我会一枪崩了她，再崩了你们。
Maniacal Civilian: Let me in. I'll shoot her. I'll shoot you. I'll shoot everyone!

他用手钳住女士的脖颈，缓缓后退，将她从明黄的灯下一点点拽入他身后的暗影中。
He clamps her throat and backs away, dragging her from the yellow lamplight into the shadow behind.

疯狂的乘客：你以为我会乖乖听话，遵守你们的狗屁规则，坐在家里等着炮弹炸穿我的脑子？
Maniacal Civilian: You really think I'm just going to be a good little sheep and go back home to wait for a bomb to fall on my head?

他哑然失笑，眼底涌起一抹血色。
A hollow laugh escapes him, blood rising in his eyes.

疯狂的乘客：不不不……我活不了，你们也别想活——
Maniacal Civilian: No, no, no. If I don't get to make it out of here, then no one else will.

一声朝天的枪响划破沉沉的暮色，人群瞬间安静下来。
A gunshot splits the air. Silence falls over the crowd.

车站守军：喂——混球，把你的手从那位女士身上拿开！
Platform Guard: Hold it, you bastard! Get your hands off that lady!

几名士兵从不远处赶来，枪口毫不迟疑地对准了肇事的乘客。
Guards rush forward, training their rifles on the troublemaker.

车站守军：别逼我们采取“必要的强制措施”。
Platform Guard: Don't make us end this the hard way.

疯狂的乘客：呵呵……
Maniacal Civilian: Heh ...

疯狂的乘客：男人讥讽地看着眼前黑洞洞的枪口，像是在欣赏一个拙劣的笑话。
Maniacal Civilian: He sneers at the dark muzzles.

疯狂的乘客：就是这样，自相残杀、互相掠夺，就像你们在战场上做的那样。
Maniacal Civilian: Aren't you soldiers busy enough killing each other? You have to come and start roughing us up too?

瞳孔收缩，扣住扳机的手指缓缓收紧。
His pupils shrink. His finger tightens on the trigger.

疯狂的乘客：那么，要不要试试看——我们谁的子弹比较快？
Maniacal Civilian: Alright, then try me. Let's see who can pull the trigger first?

混乱中，惊魂未定的“人质”被驻军拽了回来。
In the chaos, the shaken "hostage" is pulled back by the platform guards.

车站守军：您没事吧，女士？
Platform Guard: Are you alright, ma'am?

傲慢的乘客：我好得很。但我的票……票还在他手上！
Arrogant Passenger: I'm fine, but my ticket ... He still has my ticket!

她指向前方的肇事者。此刻他像一头失控的野兽冲撞出去。
She points toward the culprit ahead, who now charges like a mad bull.

疯狂的乘客：别拦着我，滚开！
Maniacal Civilian: Out of my way!

他终于摆脱了身后的驻军，向着前方雾气弥漫的铁轨跑去。
He finally shakes off the guards and bolts toward the misty tracks.

疯狂的乘客：布达佩斯！只有那儿是安全的……
Maniacal Civilian: Budapest! That's the only safe place.

疯狂的乘客：啊——！！
Maniacal Civilian: Ah!

世界忽然倾斜。
The world tilts.

男人脚底一空，不慎从月台坠落。
The ground gives way beneath him. He slips from the platform.

傲慢的乘客：噢，我的上帝……
Arrogant Passenger: Good Lord!

站务员：先生，请立刻上来！火车马上就要进站了！
Station Staff: Sir, take my hand. The train's coming.

哭声、尖叫声和口哨声此起彼伏，几乎淹没了远处列车的汽笛声。
Cries, screams, and whistles rise in chorus, nearly drowning the train's steam whistle in the distance.

疯狂的乘客：……
Maniacal Civilian: ...

男人迷茫地站在铁轨中央。他流了很多血，又摔伤了一条腿。
The man stands dazed in the center of the tracks. His legs are bent at obtuse angles, broken and bleeding.

可他似乎感觉不到痛。
But he smiles.

喧哗声中，一道漆黑的烟柱随着鸣笛声出现在暮色之下。
A thick black column of smoke cuts into the dusky sky, rising along with a loud whistle.

平民Ⅰ：是列车……“多瑙黎明号”来了！
Civilian I: It's the train. It's the "Danube Dawn"!

年复一年，战争的阴影盘踞在这片土地上，如影随形，挥之不去。
Year after year, the shadow of war clings to this land, relentless, unshakable.

就在这片破碎土地的尽头，“多瑙黎明号”缓缓驶来，如同暴风雪中唯一幸存的孤舟。
But still, the "Danube Dawn" makes its journey, like a dutiful soldier marching alone through rain, sleet, and storm.

她就在那里，带着自由与生的希望。
She arrives bearing hope for freedom and for life.

疯狂的乘客：“多瑙黎明”……布达佩斯……
Maniacal Civilian: The "Danube Dawn" ... Budapest ...

他终于记起自己该做什么，于是踉跄着奔向车头。
At last, he remembers what he must do and stumbles toward the engine.

站务员：不，先生，不——！！
Station Staff: No, sir! No—!

疯狂的乘客：我来了……母亲、父亲，玛丽娜……
Maniacal Civilian: I made it. Mother, Father, Malina ...

列车吞吐着烟雾逐渐逼近，车灯在暮色中晕开一圈又一圈昏黄的光。
The train exhales smoke as it nears, headlights spilling dim yellow circles into the twilight.

男人艰难地向前挪步，将他那伤痕累累的、总是笼罩在哭声与枪炮声中的故土抛在背后。
The man limps forward along the tracks.

疯狂的乘客：票，我有票……让我上车……让我上车！
Maniacal Civilian: Here's my ticket. Let me in. Let me in!

男人高声呐喊，举起左手，用力挥动着那张薄薄的车票。
He cries out, waving the thin ticket in the air.

这是他挣扎至今唯一的凭证，也是他通向新生的唯一钥匙。
He waves it like a protective charm, like the key to life were in his hand.

疯狂的乘客：我有票——！！
Maniacal Civilian: I have a ticket—!

列车呼啸而过。铁轮碾过他的血肉，像碾死一只误入轨道的蚂蚁。
The train thunders as it grinds to a stop—too late. Momentum and weight carried on iron wheels pulverize his flesh,

轰鸣声持续不断，震颤穿透地面，将愤怒、疯狂、恐惧——他的一切都压入冰冷的铁轨。
crushing rage, madness, and fear—everything—into the cold steel.

而那张染血的车票，此刻也悄然从他的指缝间滑落，被列车带起的风拖曳向远方。
The bloodstained ticket slips from his fingers, carried up and far away.

车门开启，头戴眼罩的乘务员着急忙慌地跑了下来。
The train door opens, and a stewardess with an eyepatch rushes out in a panic.

乘务员女孩：怎么会这样……
Train Stewardess: Oh my ...

乘务员女孩：请大家保持冷静，我们需要先确认一下事故情况……
Train Stewardess: Everyone, please remain calm. We need to inspect the scene.

平民Ⅰ：让我上车吧……小姐，看在上帝的份儿上，我不想死在这里……
Civilian I: Please let me in, miss! For the love of all that's good, don't let us die out here.

平民Ⅱ：这是最后一趟车了，对不对？发发善心吧……
Civilian II: This is the last train, isn't it? Please, you have to help us.

强烈的求生本能驱使着人们如潮水般涌上，将车门围得水泄不通。
The crowd surges forward toward the opening doors. The gore and horror that only just occurred is forgotten in their desperation.

焦灼的目光和声声恳求汇成海洋。
A roiling mass of faces filled with stark fear and determination and bodies jostling for position.

而那张雪片儿般飞走的车票，在无人在意的地方，悄无声息地飘到了另一人眼前。
Meanwhile, the ticket drifts unseen, landing silently before another.

塞梅尔维斯：……？
Semmelweis: ...?

调查员下意识伸出手，指尖即将触到染血的纸张时，眼前忽然降下了漆黑的帷幕。
Yet as Semmelweis reaches out to it, she's met by a shadowy apparition.

下一秒，飘在半空中的车票早已失去踪影，仿佛从未存在过。
Before she can react, the shadow and the ticket are gone, vanishing into thin air.

塞梅尔维斯：……影子？
Semmelweis: A shadow?

塞梅尔维斯：似乎是某种神秘术……
Semmelweis: It could be some kind of arcane skill.

调查员默不作声地扫过眼前拥堵的人潮，寻找着“影子”的来源。
The investigator scans the crowd in silence, searching for the source of this "shadow."

严肃的女士：安娜贝尔，威廉——快跟上来。这里很容易走散。
Solemn Lady: Annabelle, William, come along. We wouldn't want to get lost now, would we?

小女孩：等等我，多萝西女士……
Girl: Wait for me, Ms. Dorothy.

不是这里。
Not here.

乐天派的绅士：10型蒸汽机！这匹铁马跑起来，连阿尔卑斯山的风都追不上！
Convivial Gentleman: A Class 10 steam engine! When this beauty gets goin', it'll run faster 'n the wind blows over the Alps!

乐天派的绅士：复合式汽缸懂么？就像老裁缝的顶针套顶针，蒸汽要转两道弯才舍得吐气……
Convivial Gentleman: Has a compound engine, you understand? Steam's got to go through two stages 'fore it gets pumped out the top.

也不是这里。
Not here, either.

人潮依旧。调查员摇摇头，提起行李箱正准备登车时，耳畔忽然传来声音。
Finding no further clues, her pressing mission returns to the forefront of her mind. She picks up her suitcase and joins the madly churning queue.

野树莓：当人们都在拼命往前赶时，站着一动不动可是很危险的。
Rubuska: Crowd's starting to rush—not safe to stand around.

野树莓：麻烦让一让，女士。
Rubuska: Excuse me, coming through.

擦肩而过的间隙，调查员敏锐地捕捉到了男孩手中攥着的那张染血车票。
In the brief moment they pass each other, the investigator spots the bloodstained ticket clenched in the boy's hand.

塞梅尔维斯：请稍等一下。
Semmelweis: Please, wait.

对方似乎没有听见她的发话，像急匆匆要赶着上车一般，加快了步伐。
He seems not to hear her call, hurrying on as if rushing to board, quickening his pace.

调查员伸手试图拦下，男孩却灵敏地矮下身子，她只来得及碰到那顶深色的毡帽。
The investigator attempts to stop him, but the boy ducks; her reaching fingers brush across the top of the dark felt hat.

塞梅尔维斯：……？
Semmelweis: ...?

野树莓：糟了！我的帽子……
Rubuska: Hey, my hat!

毡帽被挤落，一张女孩的脸被迫从阴影中剥离出来。
The felt hat falls away, revealing a girl's face.

浅色的长发挣脱了帽子的束缚，飘散在风中。
Her hair spills free, drifting in the wind.

苍白的皮肤，红色的眼眸，以及一对尖牙——再标准不过的血食怪长相。
Pale skin, red eyes, and fangs—she's the spitting image of a vampire.

塞梅尔维斯：红色的眼睛……
Semmelweis: Red eyes ...

女孩匆匆低下头，阻绝了调查员探究的目光。
The girl bows her head, cutting off the investigator's sight.

野树莓：啧，真倒霉。
Rubuska: Tsk. You're kidding.

野树莓：那顶帽子才陪了我三天……
Rubuska: I only got that hat three days ago.

趁着调查员发愣的间隙，她灵巧地往人潮中一跃——
Seizing the pause, she leaps into the throng.

转眼之间，像落入芦苇丛中的蜻蜓，她就这样消失在了人群里。
In an instant, like a dragonfly into reeds, she disappears into the crowd.

调查员上前两步，捡起地上一顶平平无奇的……帽子。
The investigator steps forward to grab her sole piece of evidence—a hat, plain and unremarkable.

塞梅尔维斯：……
Semmelweis: ...

塞梅尔维斯：努力想伪装成普通人的血食怪吗……这样标准的血食怪样貌，她应该被收集进基金会资料室那些厚厚的图鉴上。
Semmelweis: A vampire disguised as a normal person. Though far from perfectly. They could add her picture to the Big Book of Vampire Faces back at headquarters.

她跑得那么快，快到来不及把自己的帽子给拿走。
If nothing else, it tells her the girl values a clean getaway over her disguise.

TMW-02 羊肠线 / Catgut

意外留下的余波仍在车站回荡，争吵与惊叫声此起彼伏。
The full weight of the earlier travesty finally hits the crowd, as shrieks and shouts of horror divert the attention of even the most desperate.

瘦小的身影穿行在这片混乱之中，灵活而谨慎地避开纷争。
With one exception—a small and slight figure that darts between the gawking crowd.

野树莓：呼，那个缠人的家伙没有跟上来……就在这里上车好了。
Rubuska: Phew. Didn't follow me. Alright, guess I'll just board here.

她长出了一口气，扶在膝盖上的手却开始颤抖起来。
She exhales, though her hands tremble on her knees.

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

胃部的空虚开始扩大，转为渴望，转为疼痛，让她开始有些头晕眼花。
The adrenaline fades, and rising against it comes the ache of overlong hunger. Her head feels like a weightless balloon.

野树莓：……忍住，野树莓，忍住。车上一定会有好吃的……
Rubuska: A little longer yet, Rubuska. There'll be food for days on the train.

野树莓：当务之急是先上车……
Rubuska: All you have to do now is get on.

她安抚着自己的肚子，缓慢地直起身来。
She presses her belly, slowly straightening.

如同一位悠闲地等待检票上车的乘客，她手插裤袋，汇入队列之中，漫不经心地看向前方正面露难色的小乘务员。
She slips her hands into her pockets, blending into the line, and glances at the flustered young stewardess.

车门前方，乘务员摊开双手，安抚、劝解着四周情绪激动的乘客。
At the train door, the stewardess spreads her arm, pleading with the agitated crowd.

乘务员女孩：请、请您稍候一会儿，乘务组正在核实身份……
Train Stewardess: Please wait a moment while our attendant confirms your identity.

傲慢的乘客：抱歉，我现在必须上车——立刻、马上。
Arrogant Passenger: I've waited quite enough, thank you very much. Let me aboard this instant.

傲慢的乘客：想必你们也看见了，那些平民是怎么惹出骚乱的……这样的噩梦没人想经历第二次。
Arrogant Passenger: You saw the chaos those peasants raised—a living nightmare, I tell you. And I certainly don't wish to experience it again.

乘务员女孩：我完全理解您的心情，索尼娅女士。可是列车有规定，请您再等等……
Train Stewardess: I-I understand your concern, Madam Sonya, but we must follow the train's regulations. Now, if you'd just wait a moment longer—

眼前的情境显然超出了乘务员日常处理事务的复杂程度。她涨红了脸，不知所措地挡在乘客与车厢门中间。
Her face burns red as she stands helpless between passengers and carriage.

索尼娅：恕我直言，你的眼罩是遮住了全部两只眼睛吗？
Sonya: Hmph! Have you lost your other eye, too?

索尼娅：所有人都瞧见了，我的票被那个无礼的家伙抢了过去，现在还给弄没了。
Sonya: My ticket was snatched by that belligerent fellow who tumbled onto the tracks. Everyone can attest to the fact.

索尼娅：不必要的程序请立刻省去。否则我将立即给铁路局写信，详细叙述今天发生的一切。我相信他们会对这起小小的“意外”很感兴趣……
Sonya: Now I beg you to skip all this unnecessary rubbish, else I will be forced to write to the railway administration! I'm sure they'll be very much interested to hear about this little "incident."

乘务员女孩：女士，您先等一下好吗？我需要请示我的上级——
Train Stewardess: Please, madam, if you'd just wait for another moment, I'll go and ask my superior.

乘务员单手便将激动的乘客拦在车门外。
Despite their difference in size and in station, the little stewardess is able to hold back the agitated woman with a single hand.

索尼娅：噢！你这粗鲁的丫头……！
Sonya: Hmph! What a crass little girl you are!

？？？：艾玛。
???: Aima.

车厢中传来了厚重的女声。
From within comes a woman's voice, deep and grave in its authority.

？？？：我来解释吧。
???: I'll take care of this.

身着制服的女人走到车门前，身躯在地上投下一片巨大的阴影。
The uniformed woman with a patchwork face approaches the door, a long shadow stretching out behind her.

野树莓：嗯，那是……？
Rubuska: Wh-Who's that?

嗅到危险气息的女孩下意识往后躲了两步。

索尼娅：不必浪费时间，谁来解释都一样……啊！你、你是？

？？？：为您解决问题的人。
???: The solution to your problem.

Sonya: Stitches ... Scars ... Oh! You're that conductress everyone has been talking about.

索尼娅：咳，我的票被人……
Sonya: Ahem, as I explained, eh, my ticket has been—

原本尖锐的声音渐渐低了下去，竟带上了一丝紧张。
Her shrill tone softens, now touched with nervousness.

告死鸟：刚才的情况我已经了解了。请放心，女士。
Corvus: I've been made aware of this situation. These tickets are made with an arcane process.

告死鸟：车票都经过了神秘术的特殊处理，无需担心被人冒用。

告死鸟：而且，这类事件很常见，我们几乎每天都会处理。
Corvus: Attempts at ticket theft are a familiar thing.

她面无表情，眼神已瞥向那最不起眼的角落之中。
Expressionless, the woman glances into the most unremarkable corner.

告死鸟：从未有过遗漏。
Corvus: But we have never lost a single ticket.

野树莓：——！！
Rubuska: ...!

女孩对于危机的嗅觉向来灵敏。她当即转身，可刚打算迈出脚步——
The girl's instinct for danger has never failed her. She turns at once, ready to move ...

野树莓：哎哟！
Rubuska: Ow!

右脚仿佛被灌了铅，将失衡的女孩拽倒在地。
Her right foot feels weighed down, and she is all at once pulled to the ground.

微弱的电流悄然游走在女孩脚下，仿佛有意识一般将她困在原地。

脑海中不期然闪过一个画面。
A thought flashes through her mind.

野树莓：……！
Rubuska: ...!

告死鸟：车票上的神秘术会指引我们找到它，它离我们很近。
Corvus: The arcane processing on the ticket will lead us to its location. It's close.

野树莓：冷静，冷静……野树莓。这没什么大不了的。

Rubuska: Do what you always do. It's worked so far.

Her tone falls like a sledgehammer, pinning her into place.

女孩身体一轻，衣领忽然勒住了脖子。
Her body lifts as her collar cinches tight around her throat.

她被列车长轻松拎起，脚尖离地，瘦小的身躯在半空中轻轻飘荡。
The conductress hoists her up with a disturbing ease.

野树莓：……？
Rubuska: ...?

她难以置信地看着自己晃来晃去的鞋尖，一时间连情绪都迟到了半拍。

Corvus: That mouth has a habit of running off. Should I sew it up for you?

列车长指尖隐约泛出发光的符文。女孩只能紧闭上嘴，不再言语。
Faint runes shimmer at the tips of the conductress's fingers. The girl wisely clamps her mouth shut.

野树莓：……哼。
Rubuska: Hmph.

The stewardess searches the instructed pocket. As she does, she leans in close to whisper in the girl's ear.

艾玛：别害怕。列车长不会真的伤害你，我们只想把车票还给它的主人。
Aima: Don't worry, the conductress won't hurt you. We just want to retrieve the ticket.

艾玛：找到啦！索尼娅女士，请确认一下，这是您的车票吗？
Aima: Found it. Madam Sonya, please take a look. Is this your ticket?

乘务员朝车厢里招招手。焦急的乘客女士快步走来，接过那张染血的车票。
She gestures to the carriage. A frantic passenger hurries forward and takes the bloodstained ticket.

索尼娅：啊，没错！就是它，我那多灾多难的车票！
Sonya: Oh, yes. This is it. Oh, thank goodness you've found it!

她将车票捧在手心，像一个祈祷的女孩。
The woman cradles it in her palms like a prayer.

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

女孩泄气般安静下来，如同一块悬挂在树梢随风摆动的破布。
The girl falls limp, like a rag caught in the wind.

几枚硬币，一个药瓶，几片破布条和一支笛子。这就是她的全部了。
A few coins, a bottle, some strips of cloth, and a flute. All the possessions to her name.

她不愿意数这是第几次了——捡到好运，却又很快弄丢了它。
Her luck has run thin—not that she had much to begin with.

野树莓：我只是……太饿了，实在太饿了。我没有想伤害任何人……
Rubuska: I'm just hungry. So hungry. I never meant to hurt anyone.

野树莓：有钱人总有上车的法子，我只是想吃顿饱饭……
Rubuska: Rich people always find a way to get onto these trains. I just thought that maybe I could get on to have a meal.

最后一点委屈被她咽下肚子，她知道这并没有用。
She swallows her last protest.

野树莓：好了，票也还了。放我下来，我自己会滚得远远的……
Rubuska: You've got your ticket back. So, how about letting me down? I'll see myself off.

？？？：看来，你又给我惹麻烦了。
???: There you are. What sort of trouble have you gotten up to this time?

心灰意冷之际，一个不曾料想到的“陌生人”来替她解了围。
A familiar, if unexpected, savior emerges from the crowd.

深发深眸的调查员信步而来，目光掠过被拎在半空中的女孩，毫无波澜。
The dark-haired, dark-eyed investigator strides forward, paying only a passing, if meaningful, glance to the dangling girl.

塞梅尔维斯：晚上好，列车长女士。您手中的这位小姐——她是我的助手。
Semmelweis: Good evening, Conductress. Would you mind letting her down? This is my assistant.

塞梅尔维斯：请问她为您的工作造成什么不便了吗？
Semmelweis: May I ask what sort of inconvenience she's caused?

调查员手里拿着一顶帽子，她顺手将其扣回女孩的头上，物归原主。
She sets the wayward hat back onto the girl's head.

野树莓：……？
Rubuska: ...?

女孩愣了一瞬，立刻理解了状况。
The girl freezes, then immediately understands. Eyes wide beneath the brim, cheeks flushing red.

野树莓：对、没错！我是她的助理野树莓！你可算找到我了，头儿……
Rubuska: That-That's right! I'm Rubuska, her assistant! What took you so long, boss?

野树莓：雪下得那么大，我都不知道该上哪儿找你……
Rubuska: I couldn't find you anywhere, what with all the snow ...

告死鸟：……
Corvus: ...

列车长放下女孩，平静地看着眼前口音、穿着和气质都毫无共同点的二人。
Corvus lowers her to her feet, studying the two odd figures—so unalike in accent, dress, and bearing.

告死鸟：助手？
Corvus: Assistant?

野树莓：是的，我们有一些非常要紧的事务在身，要不是分开了的话……
Rubuska: Uh, y-yeah! We're on a very, very important mission, haha. But we got separated.

塞梅尔维斯：你已经耽误不少时间了，我们走吧——这次记得拿好你的车票。
Semmelweis: We've wasted enough time. Let's go, and don't forget your ticket this time.

一张崭新的车票递交到野树莓的手里。
A brand-new ticket is pressed into Rubuska's hand.

这原是为七十七分队的成员准备的车票之一，现在它有了新的主人。
Once meant for one of the presently missing members of Squad 77, it now belongs to her.

塞梅尔维斯：如果再发生类似的事情，我会按工作规章准则来处理。
Semmelweis: If you cause trouble like that again, I won't hesitate to punish you, in line with the proper regulations.

野树莓：……谢谢您。
Rubuska: Sure, sure. Thank you.

女孩连连点头，握紧车票，朝调查员投去复杂的一瞥。
She nods rapidly, clutching it tight, casting the investigator a conflicted glance.

告死鸟：……好吧，二位。
Corvus: I see. In that case …

告死鸟：那我代表“多瑙黎明号”列车欢迎两位客人，祝你们旅途愉快。
Corvus: On behalf of the crew of the "Danube Dawn," I wish you a pleasant journey.

她轻轻颔首，摆出一副公事公办的模样。
She dips her head, businesslike.

告死鸟：我们已经因为刚才的事故耽误了不少时间。这里风雪很大，请两位先上车取暖。
Corvus: We're running late now, and the snow is getting heavier.

告死鸟：若有其他事宜，我们可以在车厢内详谈。
Corvus: Come aboard. If there are any other matters to discuss, let us do so in the warmth of the train.

乘客们陆续上车，兴奋地四处观望着。
Passengers file aboard, excitement in their eyes.

乘客Ⅱ：噢……这辆列车似乎比预想的还要更加奢华。
Passenger II: How splendid! This train is more luxurious than I ever imagined!

戴帽子的绅士：毕竟是昔日的豪华专线。听说在它的黄金时代，每一趟车都是贵族与名流们争相集会的社交场合……
Hatted Gentleman: Well, she was a luxury express once upon a time. I heard that durin' her golden age, each journey she took was like a social event in itself, filled up to the brim with nobles and celebrities ...

调查员在人群中四处张望了一会儿，依旧未能发现她的同伴们。
The investigator scans the crowd, but it seems her reinforcements are nowhere to be found.

通讯器也静默着，没有等到任何回复。
The communicator remains silent. No reply.

塞梅尔维斯：……看样子，任务得改为单人执行了。
Semmelweis: It appears I'll have to finish this mission myself.

塞梅尔维斯：呵……倒也不错，回去还能向基金会多要一笔奖金。
Semmelweis: Heh. It's not all bad. At least I'll have a little bonus waiting for me when I get back to the Foundation.

她轻叹一声，眼角的余光捕捉到一抹鬼鬼祟祟、正缓缓蠕动着试图离开的身影。
She offers a soft sigh before turning her sharp glance back to her first catch of the evening—mid-slink in a second escape attempt.

塞梅尔维斯：你似乎走错方向了，野树莓小姐——我们的座位在那边。
Semmelweis: You're going the wrong direction, Ms. Rubuska. Our seats are this way.

野树莓：啊哈，是吗……？
Rubuska: Haha, ha, of course they are.

女孩尴尬地挠了挠头，目光落在调查员轻轻握住女孩胳膊的手上。
The girl scratches her head, feigning awkwardness. But her eyes shoot to the investigator's hand now firmly grasping her arm.

野树莓：我很感谢您，女士……多亏了您我才能上车。
Rubuska: Thank you so much, ma'am. I never would've gotten on board if it weren't for you.

野树莓：可我现在很穷，手头没什么可以报答您的。等到了布达佩斯，如果您还记得我……
Rubuska: I really don't have anything to repay you with, though. Tell you what, when we get to Budapest, if you still remember me—

塞梅尔维斯：不用这么着急离开，野树莓小姐。我还有几个问题需要你来回答。
Semmelweis: Not so fast, Ms. Rubuska. I have some questions for you.

野树莓：呃……
Rubuska: …

拉扯间，车厢内忽然安静下来。
The carriage goes utterly silent despite the commotion of boarding.

女孩顺着人们的视线往后望去，列车长与乘务员正一同站在车门前方。
She follows the others' eyes now locked on the conductress and stewardess standing together at the end of the carriage.

告死鸟：欢迎大家乘坐由维也纳-潘诺尼亚运输公司经营的列车“多瑙黎明号”。
我是列车长告死鸟，这位是主乘务员艾玛。
Corvus: Welcome aboard the "Danube Dawn," operated by Vienna-Pannonian Railways. I am Corvus, your conductress, and this is Aima, your chief stewardess.

告死鸟：“多瑙黎明号”东起伊斯坦布尔，西至维也纳，总路线约800英里，中间将经停尼卡与布达佩斯两个站点。
Corvus: The "Danube Dawn" travels from Istanbul to Vienna, a journey of a little more than 800 miles, with stops in Nika and Budapest.

告死鸟：由于刚才的事故，我们还需要配合当地政府进行调查。为此，列车将推迟至晚餐后启动。
Corvus: Due to an unfortunate incident at the station, our departure will be delayed until after dinner while we cooperate with the local government's investigation.

告死鸟：为表歉意，我们为各位准备了比以往都要更加丰盛的免费餐食。
Corvus: As an apology, we have prepared a substantial meal for every passenger.

野树莓：免费的餐食……！
Rubuska: Free food!

女孩的眼睛“唰”的亮了起来，与此同时，剧烈的饥饿感也一同涌入。
Her eyes flash bright, her stomach quivers with anticipation.

她按住自己略带颤抖的手指，又迅速调整了表情，掩饰住自己的虚弱。
She steadies her trembling fingers and masks her weakness with a smile.

塞梅尔维斯：看来你对免费的食物很感兴趣。
Semmelweis: I see you have a particular interest in food.

调查员微笑着看向女孩，语气温和。
The investigator smiles at her.

塞梅尔维斯：如果你需要的话，可以吃掉我的这一份。
Semmelweis: You're welcome to my meal, if you'd like.

塞梅尔维斯：不过，作为交换，我希望你能老老实实地待在这儿，别到处乱跑，更别再惹上什么麻烦。
Semmelweis: But in return, you need to sit here and stay out of trouble. Do we have an agreement?

野树莓：哇哦，听上去可真诱人！可是……
Rubuska: Well, I mean ... It is tempting, but—

女孩无辜地眨了眨眼。
The girl blinks.

野树莓：我只是个普通人，不值得您这样的女士为我费心。
Rubuska: Why're you doing all this? I'm just an ordinary girl. Why do all this for me?

塞梅尔维斯：我很快就会放你离开。
Semmelweis: I'm not keeping you, if that's what you're thinking. You're free to go anytime.

调查员笑眯眯地凑近女孩，压低了声音。
She leans closer and lowers her voice with intent.

塞梅尔维斯：如果你真如你所说的那样“普通”。
Semmelweis: That is, if you really are a "normal" girl as you claim.

塞梅尔维斯：那位列车长很敏锐，如果被她发现我们并非同僚，你恐怕很难继续待在车上。
Semmelweis: That conductress is sharp. If she figures out you're not my assistant, it may be difficult to convince her not to throw you out.

塞梅尔维斯：更何况……
Semmelweis: And to top it off ...

她环顾四周逐渐落座的乘客们。贵族、军人、作家……人们热烈地攀谈着，对即将展开的旅途充满了期待。
Around them, the rich, the powerful, officers, and writers each settle into their seats, lively chatter filling the carriage with anticipation.

塞梅尔维斯：这趟车远不如它看起来那样安全。
Semmelweis: I don't think this train is anywhere near as safe as it first appears.

TMW-03 用餐愉快 / Bon Appétit

晚餐时间到来，乘客们紧绷的神经终于有所松动。大家围坐在灯光下，开始进食、饮酒、攀谈，笑声此起彼伏。
Dinner arrives, and the tension eases. They hunch over their trays to eat, drink, and chatter, laughter rising and falling.

当然，也有一些小小的“插曲”。
Of course, there are a few "incidents."

索尼娅：这是……牛肉炖菜？
Sonya: You call this beef stew?

艾玛：很抱歉，索尼娅女士。现在是战争时期，我们食物供应十分紧张，质量可能有所下滑……
Aima: I truly am sorry, madam. I'm afraid the war has limited our ability to procure supplies up to our usual standards. It may taste slightly different from our usual fare.

索尼娅：可这也太不像话了，它吃起来简直像过了火的牛革！
Sonya: "Slightly different"? This is boiled cowhide in a thin gruel!

女士气恼地放下手中的刀叉。
She slams her knife and fork down in anger.

索尼娅：战争这，战争那……人们都爱把它当作偷懒的借口。
Sonya: It's always "war this" and "war that" with you people. Excuses piled on excuses!

索尼娅：我付了和以往同样价格的车票钱，当然有资格要求获得同样水准的服务。
Sonya: I paid my fare, the same as usual; I deserve the service I've come to expect.

戴帽子的绅士：真叫人寒心啊，索尼娅女士。
Hatted Gentleman: Wouldn't you say that's a touch harsh, ma'am?

戴帽子的绅士：外面多少人还在挨饿受冻。您倒好，居然还有闲情挑三拣四。
Hatted Gentleman: There's people out there gettin' shelled to kingdom come beggin' for any scraps they can get.

索尼娅：呵呵……阿不思诺先生，你们英国人除了站在世界另一端评头论足，就不能做一些对自己人生更有意义的事吗？
Sonya: Hah! Isn't this what you Brits do—stick your noses into a lady's business and levy pointless accusations? Don't you have something better to do with your miserable little life?

索尼娅：比如去外面晒晒太阳，或者……天哪，做顿不怎么像湿袜子的饭？
Sonya: Perhaps you ought to try feeling the sun on your skin, or, I don't know, cooking a meal that doesn't taste like wet socks?

阿不思诺：嘿，女士——
Arbuthnot: Oh, that's rich, you—

绅士面红耳赤地站起身，背后却传来一声轻笑。
The gentleman flushes red and rises. A stifled giggle sounds behind him.

一位女士坐在他们身后奋笔疾书，眼神不时从笔记上抬起。
A woman sits behind them, scribbling purposefully as they speak.

阿不思诺：这位女士，请问你这是在做什么……？
Arbuthnot: What're you doin', ma'am?

？？？：观察，记录。
???: Me? Just recording what I see.

撰稿人优雅地合上笔记本。
The editor closes her notebook with grace.

？？？：“突发争吵，战时炖牛肉引爆国籍冲突！女士怒怼英国绅士：你们连饭都不会做？”
???: "Train Clash: Beef Stew Sparks National Conflict! Lady Accuses British Gent of Abominable Cooking" ...

？？？：“战火未完，餐桌先燃：一位女士的牛肉炖菜之怒。”
???: Or perhaps, "Battle at the Dinner Table: One Woman's Rage over Beef Stew."

？？？：你们可以接着吵下去，为我提供更多创作的灵感。
???: Don't let me stop you. This is all excellent material.

索尼娅：哼，该死的小报编辑……
Sonya: Hmph. Journalists ...

空心木：眼光不错，我确实是一名编辑，也会写一些报道。我叫空心木。
Verity: That I am. Though, I'm primarily an editor. But I write reports whenever a good one comes along. Call me Verity.

空心木：如果二位发现了有趣的素材，尤其是关于神秘学家的传言，欢迎联络我，我愿意提供对等的报酬。
Verity: If you have any interesting material, especially about arcanists, please contact me. I will pay accordingly.

阿不思诺&索尼娅：……
Arbuthnot & Sonya: ...

争吵在不经意间被调停。
The pair falter, unable to reply, and return to their dinner. The quarrel, now soothed, leaves the stewardess effusively grateful.

艾玛：谢谢您，女士。
Aima: Thank you ever so much, madam.

空心木：别担心，小可怜。
Verity: Don't you worry, poor thing.

撰稿人侧过脸，托腮望向角落里大快朵颐的乘客。
The editor props her head in one hand, turning to watch a passenger feasting in the corner.

空心木：起码不是每个人都认为你们的餐食很糟糕。
Verity: At least someone's enjoying the meal.

野树莓：唔、唔……我很久没有……这么痛快地吃一顿饱饭了……
Rubuska: *munching* I haven't had food like this in *gulp* forever!

面对良久未见的食物，女孩的犹豫最终拜倒在了饥饿之下。
The sight of food, real food, melts away the girl's anxieties.

她进食的样子算不上失态，但速度和胃口都相当惊人。
The speed and ferocity with which she eats is startling, yet the investigator spies a curious inconsistency—good table manners.

野树莓：谢谢你，女士……
Rubuska: Thank you, ma'am!

塞梅尔维斯：你可以叫我塞梅尔维斯。
Semmelweis: It's Semmelweis.

塞梅尔维斯：有人告诉过你吗？你的眼睛颜色很特别。
Semmelweis: Has anyone ever told you that your eye color is very unique?

野树莓：是吗……谢谢夸奖。
Rubuska: Yeah? Uh, thanks.

女孩抬起头，眼睛掩在帽檐的阴影下，那是异于常人的瞳色。
Rubuska lifts her head, eyes shadowed by her brim—unusual eyes.

野树莓：你刚才说，这趟列车没有它看上去的那么安全……
Rubuska: You were saying that this train isn't as safe as it looks.

野树莓：这是什么意思？
Rubuska: Why'd you say that, exactly?

她伸手压低了自己的帽檐。
She presses her hat lower.

塞梅尔维斯：世上很少有表里如一的人，人们往往抱有不同的目的，并为达成这些目的各怀鬼胎。
Semmelweis: People rarely match their deeds to their words. They may say one thing, but I've found their true motives to often be much darker.

塞梅尔维斯：比如车上的这些乘客，比如那位列车长，以及……
Semmelweis: Anyone could be a danger. The passengers, the conductress, or even ...

塞梅尔维斯：你。
Semmelweis: You.

她摊开手，展露出一种十分真诚的无奈。
Her tone is not forceful, falling short of accusation, still Rubuska cannot help but make her case.

野树莓：塞梅尔维斯小姐，无论如何，我是一个连饭都没得吃的人，也不会对任何人造成威胁。
Rubuska: Ms. Semmelweis, all I am is a hungry kid looking for food. Look at me, how could I be a threat to anyone?

塞梅尔维斯：但你拿走了别人的车票，不是吗？
Semmelweis: You did take that woman's train ticket, yes?

她语气温和，敏锐的话语却如同尖刺。
Her voice is gentle, but her words piercing.

野树莓：我……好吧，我是拿走了那张车票。
Rubuska: I ... Well, yeah, I took it.

野树莓：我已经四天没有吃到一顿正常的饭了。这对我来说是个活下去的机会。
Rubuska: But, I hadn't eaten anything for four days. I needed to do something to survive.

野树莓：我并不想伤害那位女士……如果可以的话，我希望那位女士也能登上这趟列车。
Rubuska: I didn't mean to do her any harm. I figured maybe they'd let her on anyway, and then we'd both get on, and there'd be no trouble.

女孩不自觉涨红了脸。调查员沉静地看着她，仿佛早已洞悉一切。
The girl flushes red. Semmelweis holds her stare, as if already knowing the truth and waiting for a confession.

良久，她突然莞尔一笑。
At last, she allows a smile to slip from her face.

塞梅尔维斯：为了活下去，这并没有什么可指摘的。事实上，你也没有造成任何伤害。
Semmelweis: No one can blame you for trying to survive in these conditions. At the very least, you weren't the cause of any harm.

塞梅尔维斯：我只是很好奇，你究竟用什么手法从我眼前拿走了那张车票。
你的神秘术，我说的对吗？
Semmelweis: But there is one thing I'm curious about. How did you reach that ticket earlier? It was your arcane skill, wasn't it?

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

沉默已经表明了问题的答案。意识到自己的破绽，女孩生硬地转移了话题。
Her silence is the answer. Realizing her slip, she stiffly changes the subject.

野树莓：你说每个人都表里不一，那你呢？你能坦白地告诉我你的身份和目的吗？
Rubuska: "People rarely match their deeds to their words," then, what about you? What are you doing here?

塞梅尔维斯：调查那些会造成影响的“表里不一”，就是我的工作。
Semmelweis: I'm here to investigate this "duplicity."

她不动声色地回避了问题的本质，从座椅背后拿出一个文件夹。
She sidesteps the question, producing a folder from her briefcase.

塞梅尔维斯：接下来轮到我提问了……
Semmelweis: But our arrangement was for you to answer the questions.

她从文件夹中抽出一张白色的纸条。
She draws out a white slip of paper.

塞梅尔维斯：你见过这个图案吗？
Semmelweis: Have you seen this pattern before?

野树莓：嗯……
Rubuska: Hmm.

野树莓：这个嘛……我当然见过啦。应该是在某个市场……不，可能是在路过的墙上。
Rubuska: Yeah ... Yeah, I've seen it. Maybe in a market? Uh, or, on a wall somewhere.

野树莓：如果您之后能放我走，我或许能更细致地搜索一下我的记忆……
Rubuska: I might be able to search my memory more carefully, that is, if you let me go later.

女孩正盯着眼前的符号冥思苦想，纸条便被轻巧地抽离。
The girl eyes the symbol again, as if thinking hard. But the facade drops.

塞梅尔维斯：你很聪明。不过很遗憾，你的演技还有待提升。我想我已经得到自己想要的答案了。
Semmelweis: You're quite clever. Unfortunately, your acting skills could use a little work, which means I already have my answer.

塞梅尔维斯：你并非他们中的一员。
Semmelweis: You're not one of them.

野树莓：……啧。
Rubuska: *sigh*

女孩有些懊恼地皱起眉毛。
She frowns bluntly.

塞梅尔维斯：最后一个问题。你知道血食怪的传说吗？
Semmelweis: One last question. How familiar are you with vampiric legends?

塞梅尔维斯：听说他们都有一双“特别”的眼睛，就像……
Semmelweis: It's often said that their eyes have a peculiar quality, just like ...

她意味深长地看向女孩暗红的双瞳，成功在其中捕捉到了一丝慌乱。
She meets the girl's crimson eyes, catching a flicker of panic.

野树莓：我、我完全不明白你在说什么……
Rubuska: I-I have no idea what you're talking about.

告死鸟：打扰一下。这位小姐，方便占用你几分钟吗？
Corvus: Excuse me, madam. A moment of your time.

骤然出现的声音打断了步步紧逼的追问。列车长站在车厢的另一头，朝调查员招手示意。
A voice cuts the tension. At the far end of the carriage, the conductress raises a hand, beckoning the investigator.

塞梅尔维斯：……
Semmelweis: ...

塞梅尔维斯：我很快回来，希望你能履行“助手”的职责，不要再随意离开了。
Semmelweis: Stay put. I'll be back soon. Do exactly as a good little assistant would do, understood?

塞梅尔维斯：要知道，血食怪可不是这列车上唯一危险的东西。
Semmelweis: Vampires aren't the only dangerous things that may lurk on this train.

野树莓：……遵命，头儿——
Rubuska: Sure thing, boss—

对“助手”做出叮嘱后，调查员起身离开，朝着列车长那儿不紧不慢地走去。
After warning her "assistant," the investigator rises and makes her way toward the conductress.

告死鸟：她不是你的同伴。
Corvus: That girl is not your assistant.

告死鸟：别试图瞒过我，我能看出来。你们没什么默契，你和那小姑娘认识的时间不会超过半个钟头。
Corvus: Save your explanation. I doubt you've known each other for more than half an hour.

列车长倚着墙壁，毫不留情地点破了调查员的谎言。
The conductress leans against the wall in what must, for her, be a supremely exaggerated gesture.

塞梅尔维斯：我认为这属于乘客隐私。或许战时没那么多讲究，但我想我们仍然得遵守最基本的人道主义原则，您觉得呢？列车长女士。
Semmelweis: I wouldn't have expected you to probe into matters of passenger privacy. I believe we should abide by certain basic humanitarian principles, even during wartime. Wouldn't you agree, Conductress?

告死鸟：如果你只是一位普通乘客，那你的事与我无关，我没有理由也没有兴趣介入。
Corvus: If you were an ordinary passenger, as you claim, I wouldn't have "probed."

告死鸟：但你来自那个什么“基金会”，我说得对吗？
Corvus: But you are from that "Foundation," correct?

她的目光落在调查员胸前的徽章上。
Her gaze falls on the badge at the investigator's chest.

告死鸟：我见过你的徽章和黑白格纹。通常来说，基金会的人出现意味着……麻烦。
Corvus: That badge with the black-and-white print. Wherever the Foundation shows up, trouble follows.

塞梅尔维斯：不必紧张，列车长女士，也许我只是去维也纳休假呢？
Semmelweis: No need to be nervous, ma'am. I'm just on my way to Vienna for a little holiday.

告死鸟：能让你冒险穿过战区，花费重金购买车票，我猜这一定是很重要的假期。
Corvus: Aboard an express train bound to pass through a war zone—you must take your vacations very seriously.

塞梅尔维斯：……
Semmelweis: ...

调查员轻叹一口气，掏出自己的基金会身份证件。
The investigator sighs and pulls out her Foundation ID.

塞梅尔维斯：圣洛夫基金会，这是我的证件。
Semmelweis: St. Pavlov Foundation. I'm sure you'll find my identification is in order.

告死鸟：圣洛夫基金会……
Corvus: St. Pavlov Foundation ...

告死鸟：调查员，塞梅尔维斯。
Corvus: Investigator Semmelweis.

列车长将工作证双手交还给调查员，语气没有丝毫改变。
The conductress returns the card without a change in tone.

告死鸟：我明白了。调查员小姐，有什么我能为您服务的吗？
Corvus: I see. Is there anything that I might do for you, Investigator?

塞梅尔维斯：我收到了情报，一名危险的血食怪极有可能潜藏在您的列车上。因此，我需要您的配合以进行调查。
Semmelweis: We've received intelligence that there may be a dangerous vampire on this train. I could use your help in the investigation.

调查员开门见山，直接抛出任务的主题。
She cuts straight to the point, stating her mission boldly and without restraint.

告死鸟：血食怪……
Corvus: A vampire.

听到“血食怪”一词，列车长的脸色蒙上了一层阴翳。
A grim shadow passes over the conductress's face.

告死鸟：这儿的人从小听血食怪的故事听到大，它只是民间传闻，从来没人真的见过血食怪。
Corvus: You're chasing fairy stories. If you ask around, all you'll get is a hundred different stories; none of them real.

告死鸟：如果这是你的任务目标，我恐怕很难给予帮助。
Corvus: I can't help you chase a myth.

列车长坐回沙发上，顺手拿起一旁的棒针和毛线，无比自然地编织起来。
She returns to the sofa, picking up a pair of knitting needles.

告死鸟：请坐，调查员小姐。希望你不介意我额外的工作。
Corvus: Please have a seat, Investigator. I hope my handicraft doesn't bother you.

塞梅尔维斯：这是……什么？
Semmelweis: W-What are you working on?

告死鸟：围巾，给艾玛的。
Corvus: A scarf for Aima.

塞梅尔维斯：……
Semmelweis: ...

调查员定了定神，竭力将注意力从列车长上下翻飞的棒针中移开。
Semmelweis steadies herself, forcing her eyes away from the flickering needles.

塞梅尔维斯：关于情报的真伪，只有调查后才能下定论。倒是您的态度……
Semmelweis: I've been tasked with verifying the authenticity of this intelligence. However, your attitude ...

她脑海中忽然划过一个可能性。
A thought flashes through her mind.

塞梅尔维斯：您刚才说过，您认识这个徽章和标志。所以，您最近还看到过戴着和我一样徽章的人吗？
Semmelweis: You mentioned that you've seen this badge and pattern before. Was it someone you met recently?

告死鸟：我在“多瑙黎明号”上已经很多年了，调查员。除了血食怪，我什么样的东西都见过。
Corvus: I have worked on the "Danube Dawn" for many years, Investigator. I have seen everything except a vampire.

她从针脚细密的织物中抬起眼睛，看向调查员。
The conductress lifts her eyes from the tight stitches to meet hers.

塞梅尔维斯：我明白了。
Semmelweis: I see.

塞梅尔维斯：那么，假定您从未见过血食怪。可以理解，人的确很难想象自己从未见过的事物。
Semmelweis: Then let's presume you're telling the truth. It's understandable that it would be difficult to imagine something you've never seen.

调查员身体前倾，毫不避让地直视列车长的眼睛。
The investigator leans forward.

塞梅尔维斯：根据基金会提供的资料，血食怪是极为危险的物种，只要被他们咬伤，不论人类，抑或神秘学家，有极大概率会在短时间内毙命。
Semmelweis: According to our intel, vampires are extremely dangerous creatures. Once bitten, death is a near certainty, regardless of whether the victim is human or arcanist.

塞梅尔维斯：这些不幸的产物，通常被称为“感染种”。
Semmelweis: Those few who survive become what is known as "Infected."

塞梅尔维斯：他们正如哑弹，无人知晓他们会在什么时候突然失控。
Semmelweis: They're like a bomb with a broken fuse, no predicting when they'll go off.

塞梅尔维斯：列车长女士，这正是摆在您面前亟待解决的问题——一趟封闭的列车上，有可能隐藏着一名血食怪。
Semmelweis: Therein lies our problem, Conductress. We believe one such vampire is hiding somewhere on this train.

塞梅尔维斯：想必你我都很清楚，他会对全体乘客造成怎样的威胁。您打算就这样视而不见吗？
Semmelweis: There's no need to exaggerate the threat this may pose to your passengers. You aren't going to turn a blind eye now, are you?

告死鸟：……
Corvus: ...

列车长不自觉地皱了皱眉，随即自然地看向门的方向。

艾玛：列车长，我接到车站的讯息，他们希望能和您当面确认一些问题——咦？
Aima: Conductress, the station staff said they want to confirm something in person with—Huh?

告死鸟：眼前的二人隔得很远，脸上的表情都不太好看，似乎刚经历一场不愉快的对话。
Corvus: The two women sit facing one another, their expressions cold and serious.

艾玛：噢！你们似乎在谈很重要的事，那么我一会儿再……
Aima: Oh, am I interrupting something important? My apologies, I'll just ...

告死鸟：等等，我和你过去。
Corvus: Wait. I'll go with you.

列车长轻轻将围巾放在沙发一角。
The conductress sets the scarf on the sofa's edge.

告死鸟：不好意思，我得失陪一会儿。
Corvus: Excuse me for a moment, Investigator.

告死鸟：一个行政流程，为了刚才掉下铁轨的旅客。列车和车站都需要一同配合。
Corvus: It's an administrative process for the passenger who fell on the tracks.

“行政流程”。列车长刻意强调了这个词。
"Administrative process." She stresses the words.

告死鸟：我们走吧，别让他们久等。
Corvus: Let's go. Best not to keep them waiting.

她从敞开的车门离开，乘务员则像小鸭子般跟在她身后。
She leaves through the open door, her stewardess trailing behind like a lost duckling.

隔着厚厚的玻璃，调查员正通过口型仔细辨认着双方的对话。
Semmelweis watches the guards on the platform, studying the movement of their lips.

车站守军：出了这样的事故，我们必须向上头交代……
Platform Guard: Our supervisors need an answer.

车站守军：……必须暂停发车，除非……
Platform Guard: The train can't depart unless ...

塞梅尔维斯：准备借事故之名勒索吗？战乱年代倒不是什么稀罕事。
Semmelweis: Are they trying to blackmail her? I suppose it isn't unheard of in times of war.

塞梅尔维斯：如果真能晚些发车，倒是更利于我的调查……
Semmelweis: A long stop could prove helpful to my investigation.

意料之外的，列车长并未对守军的无理要求有过多反应，只是从怀中掏出一枚徽章交给了对方。
Unexpectedly, the conductress does not resist the guards' demands. Instead, she produces a badge.

车站守军：哈哈，原来是自己人……
Platform Guard: Oh, so you're one of us, hahahahaha.

原本紧绷的态势和缓下来，就连列车长脸上也带了一丝淡淡的笑意。
The standoff ends. A faint smile creeps over Corvus's face.

塞梅尔维斯：……列车和当地驻军有关系？不，如果他们真的这么熟悉，就不会有这个“行政流程”了。
Semmelweis: Could the railway be working with the army? No, then this conversation wouldn't be happening.

塞梅尔维斯：还有她交出去的东西，似乎是一枚徽章……
Semmelweis: Is she handing him a badge?

像是感觉到车内的注视，列车长忽然抬起头。
Then, as if sensing her eyes, the conductress suddenly turns to the window.

告死鸟：……
Corvus: ...

几乎是在一瞬间，列车长原本笑着的脸迅速垮了下来。
Her smile collapses in an instant.

塞梅尔维斯：真是敏锐。
Semmelweis: Perceptive, aren't you?

她状似随意地靠回沙发，看着列车长与乘务员正一前一后走在漫天飞舞的风雪中。
She leans back, watching as the conductress and stewardess disappear from view.

走到车门前，列车长停下脚步，背朝乘务员利落地挥了挥手。
On the steps of the train, the conductress halts and waves her hand briskly.

告死鸟：通知车站，去轨道上撒砂。准备发车了。
Corvus: Alert the station to begin sanding the tracks. We're departing soon.

TMW-04 雪夜快车 / The Midnight Piercer

伴随一声急促的鸣笛，列车终于启动，开足马力行驶在一望无际的漆黑原野上。
With a sharp whistle, the train surges forward, chugging with growing speed into the black expanse.

野树莓：呼……终于发车了！
Rubuska: Phew. The train is finally moving!

一路悬着的心终于轻轻落下。
Hearts long held in suspense settle, lulled by the rhythmic sway of the train.

野树莓：等到了布达佩斯，我得想想该做些什么……先吃一大份卡帕玛！
Rubuska: Now, what to do when I get to Budapest? First, eat a lot of Kapama!

野树莓：不，不对。还是得先找份工作……然后再吃卡帕玛！
Rubuska: No, no, wait. First thing's first. Find a job, then Kapama!

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

野树莓：找工作是为了卡帕玛，吃卡帕玛是为了找工作。
Rubuska: Find a job so I can eat Kapama. Eat Kapama so I can work harder.

女孩拿出挂在身侧的卡瓦尔长笛，手指在细小的裂纹上轻轻摩挲着。
The girl draws her kaval flute, fingers brushing the tiny cracks.

野树莓：妈妈……布达佩斯的卡帕玛，会和你做的味道一样好吗？
Rubuska: Мама, will the Kapama in Budapest taste as good as yours?

她望着窗外连绵起伏的群山，好像见到了那个在山中独自奔跑的身影。
She looks out at the rolling mountains in the distance, seeing a lone figure running along their spine.

身影穿过墓园，踩过腐烂的橙子，天空低垂得像要塌下来。
The figure dashes through a graveyard, over cold fields, beneath a sagging sky.

哦，还有声音。发疯一般的、女人的呐喊声。
Her silent film is suddenly pierced with sound—a scream that only she can hear.

野树莓：不管怎么说，妈妈，我会先填饱肚子，活下去再说。
Rubuska: Whatever happens, I'll do my best to stay alive. I promise, Мама.

女孩吸了吸鼻子，小心翼翼地收起木笛，环顾车厢四周。
The girl sniffles, putting the flute away before taking a quick look around the carriage.

野树莓：塞梅尔维斯她，应该短时间内不会回来了吧……
Rubuska: Ms. Semmelweis won't be back for a while, right?

塞梅尔维斯：调查那些会造成影响的“表里不一”，就是我的工作。
Semmelweis: I'm here to investigate this "duplicity."

塞梅尔维斯：你知道血食怪的传说吗？
Semmelweis: One last question. How familiar are you with vampiric legends?

塞梅尔维斯：要知道，血食怪可不是这列车上唯一危险的东西。
Semmelweis: Vampires aren't the only dangerous things that may lurk on this train.

野树莓：虽然她请我吃了美味的牛肉炖菜和云雀蛋糕，但她似乎对血食怪很感兴趣……
Rubuska: She did pay for my beef stew and lark cake, but she seems really obsessed with vampires.

野树莓：……不行，还是早点离开为妙。
Rubuska: No, the sooner I leave, the better.

女孩跳下座位准备离开，犹豫了一会儿，又从口袋里数出两枚硬币放在桌子上。
She jumps from her seat, hesitates, then drops two coins on the table.

野树莓：原谅我吧，好心的塞梅尔维斯小姐。有机会我一定会报答您的！
Rubuska: Forgive me, Ms. Semmelweis. I'll repay you, someday! Cross my heart!

下定决心，女孩回过头去，准备寻找下一个栖身之地。
Resolute, she turns back, searching for another refuge.

野树莓：……哎呀！
Rubuska: Ouch!

安娜贝尔：呜呜呜……
Annabelle: *sob*

安娜贝尔：安娜贝尔和她的，嗝，朋友走丢了……
Annabelle: I-I'm lost. *hiccup* I can't find my friends.

野树莓：呃……你的朋友总不至于被人打开车窗丢出去了吧，只要把列车从里到外都翻上一遍，总会找到的！
Rubuska: Uh, I'm sure you'll find them sooner or later! It's not like they were thrown off the train or something.

野树莓：别着急哦，耐心是一种美德……
Rubuska: So, just keep on searching! Go on, you can do it!

女孩匆忙地准备离开，衣摆却被紧紧攥住。
The girl hurries to leave, but her hem is caught.

安娜贝尔：姐姐，帮帮安娜贝尔……安娜贝尔现在不知道自己在哪个车厢……
Annabelle: Please help me. *sniffle* I don't know where I am.

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

可怜的哭声不绝于耳，足以飘至三个车厢外。
Her sobbing echoes so loudly that people three carriages away prick their ears.

一番纠缠后，野树莓不得不使出最后的“杀手锏”——她摘下帽子，露出一截小小的尖牙与暗红色瞳仁。
At last, she plays her trump card, removing her hat to reveal her fangs and crimson eyes.

野树莓：不、不许哭！我可是血食怪喔，再哭我就咬断你的脖子！
Rubuska: S-Stop crying. I'm a vampire. If you don't stop, I'll bite you!

安娜贝尔：……
Annabelle: ...

安娜贝尔：真的吗？
Annabelle: Really?

没有恐惧，也没有厌恶。
No fear. No disgust.

她得到的是听众越发好奇的、天真的疑问。
Only curiosity. Innocent wonder.

野树莓：呃，你不怕血食怪吗？红眼睛的血食怪——
Rubuska: Uh, aren't you afraid of me? I'm a red-eyed vampire. See?

野树莓又凑近了些，拉下眼睑。
She leans closer, pulling down her eyelids.

安娜贝尔：哇……好漂亮的眼睛！像红红的宝石！
Annabelle: Wow! Your eyes are so pretty! Like rubies!

野树莓：宝石？我还是第一次听人这么形容……
Rubuska: Rubies? Never heard that one before.

向来独行的血食怪不知所措地红了脸。
She flushes red, caught off guard by the compliment.

安娜贝尔：像宝石，也像大马士革的红玫瑰！
Annabelle: Rubies or-or maybe the red roses of Damascus!

野树莓：玫瑰？这……当然，还是永远不会凋谢的那一种！
Rubuska: Roses? I—Sure they are! Roses that never wither!

野树莓：你还有什么好听的、夸血食怪的话，都说给我听听！
Rubuska: Tell me more—more of these good things about vampires.

女孩兴奋地围着野树莓转悠，像小狗一样在她身上轻轻蹭着。
The girl circles her while jumping up and down like an excited puppy.

安娜贝尔：多萝西老师不让我们读血食怪的故事，说那样学不到知识，也缺乏教养，可、可是，血食怪多厉害呀……
Annabelle: But Ms. Dorothy doesn't let us read vampire stories. She says they're, um, made-up-believe. I don't care, though. I think they're amazing, don't you?

安娜贝尔：我有偷偷看那些书，我知道纯种的血食怪是最厉害的，他们都住在大大的城堡里！姐姐肯定也一样吧！
Annabelle: So I read them myself. The pure-blooded vampires are the strongest, and they live in big, big castles! You must live in one too, right?

野树莓：当、当然！既然你都这么问了……
Rubuska: S-Sure I do. Now that you mention it ...

野树莓：那我可就要跟你讲讲我荣耀的祖先们了！
Rubuska: Maybe I can tell you all about my glorious ancestors.

她假意轻咳，双手一拍，随即将自己的荣耀历史一一道来。
Rubuska coughs lightly, claps her hands, and recounts her proud history.

野树莓：在很早很早以前的……总之是很早之前的哪一年，特别特别早的一个时候吧。
Rubuska: Ahem. Long, long, long ... a lot of longs ago, back in the earliest times.

野树莓：我最最了不起的祖先，把那些从东边来的人狠狠地揍了一顿。
Rubuska: A most amazing ancestor of mine gave some invaders a good beating!

野树莓：对，没错，他就是大名鼎鼎的穿刺公！人称“德古拉”的阿诺德——阿诺德五世！
Rubuska: Yeah, that's right. He was the famous Impaler, known as Dracula, Arnold, um, Arnold V!

安娜贝尔：德古拉！德古拉！
Annabelle: Dracula! Dracula!

野树莓：太爷爷阿诺德活了一百五十五岁，最后心脏被木桩狠狠刺中，鲜血流尽而死！
Rubuska: My great-grandfather Arnold lived for 155 years! Then he took a wooden stake to the heart and bled to death.

安娜贝尔：咦，那你今年多少大了呀，姐姐？
Annabelle: Then, how old are you? Um ...

野树莓：叫我野树莓就好！我今年十四岁！
Rubuska: Name's Rubuska. I'm 14 years old.

野树莓：噢不，是二百一十四岁。
Rubuska: Erhm, I'm, I mean, I'm 214 years old.

她急忙纠正自己。
She quickly corrects herself.

野树莓：两个一百岁，再加上两个七岁，就是我的年纪。
Rubuska: Yep! I've already lived two hundred plus two times seven years.

野树莓：当然，这在我们血食怪种族里，还是非常年轻的……
Rubuska: But I'm still young for a vampire of my lineage.

少女热烈地诉说自己记忆里的故事。
The young girl speaks with fervor, reciting the stories from memory.

它们从无数个下着雪的冬季中走来。万籁寂静，炉火烧得正旺，女孩趴在母亲的膝盖上，双眼微合，几乎就要睡着了。
Stories that rise up from the endless snowy winters: silence, a blazing hearth, her head on her mother's lap, eyes drifting shut.

鲜血、夜、墓碑……她缠着母亲一遍又一遍地讲述着独属于她的瑰丽传说。
Fangs soaked with blood, moonlit nights, and dark castles ... She begged her mother to tell those wondrous tales again and again.

母亲的声音越来越轻，越来越沉……
Until her voice grew faint.

女孩于是又睡上了一个甜甜的觉，一夜好梦。
And the little girl drifted into blissful sleep.

？？？：血食怪……？
???: Vampire?

仿佛被无形的魔法牵引着，孩子们一个接一个地围拢过来。
Children gather as if drawn by unseen magic.

安娜贝尔：威廉！
Annabelle: William!

一只落单的小鸟终于找到伙伴。
The lone bird finds companions at last.

安娜贝尔：终于找到你们了！我来介绍一下，她叫野树莓——一位真正的血食怪！
Annabelle: You're here, hahaha. This is my new friend, Rubuska. She's a vampire!

孩童Ⅰ：哇，是活着的血食怪……
Child I: Wow, a real-life vampire!

孩子们激动不已。然而一个男孩却应声从阴影中走了出来，表情不屑一顾。
Excited voices fill the air, until a boy steps from the shadows, scorn written on his face.

小威廉：哼……你说你是血食怪，可你只会讲故事，什么证据都没有。
Little William: How do you know she's a vampire, huh? You don't have any proof.

孩童Ⅱ：对、对哦，这些故事我们也听过呢……
Child II: Yeah! Does she look anything like the ones in the stories?

安娜贝尔：她……她不一样！她有一双红色的眼睛哦，像红宝石一样的红色！
Annabelle: She does! Her eyes are red! Like rubies!

小威廉：可是，亨利叔叔生病的时候，眼睛也是红的呀。你还记得吗？当时你还悄悄和我说，亨利叔叔也是血食怪。
Little William: But-But when Uncle Henry was sick, his eyes went all red, and you said he was a vampire too. Remember?

小威廉：多萝西老师还训了我们一顿，说我们对亨利叔叔太没礼貌……
Little William: Ms. Dorothy even scolded us for being rude.

安娜贝尔：别、别听他的，姐姐！我知道你就是真的血食怪，我说得对吗？
Annabelle: Don't listen to him! You're a real vampire, right, Rubuska?

野树莓：当……当然是真的！
Rubuska: O-Of course I am!

女孩涨红了脸，决心捍卫血食怪一族的荣耀。
She flusters, now determined to defend the honor of her kind.

野树莓：想要证据是吧……那就给你们展示一下，真正的血食怪是什么样的！
Rubuska: You want proof? Then here it is. I'll show you what a real vampire looks like.

灯光之下，她随意左右走动了几步。
She makes a performance of strolling under the light.

野树莓：喏，你们能找见我的影子吗？
Rubuska: Take a look. Can you find my shadow?

安娜贝尔：影子……
Annabelle: Shadow ...

孩童Ⅱ：哇……真的没有影子……
Child II: Wait, you don't have a shadow!

灯光照亮了每一个孩子，每一张脸，每一双手，每一道影子——
Shadows accompany every child, an identical twin matching the movement of their hands in the darkness.

唯独她站在光中，却又像是被光绕开了似的，仿佛她本就无需遵从影子的律法，也不属于这个被光照亮的世界。
But Rubuska stands alone. As if the light itself goes straight through her, as though she was never bound to its law, never part of the world it illuminated.

野树莓：我们血食怪，是不会被照出影子的喔！
Rubuska: Exactly! We vampires don't have shadows.

孩子们：血食怪！血食怪！
Children: Vampire! Vampire!

孩童们兴奋地鼓起掌来，欢呼一声高过一声。
The children cheer louder and louder, clapping with glee.

小威廉：这……现在我宣布，这是确凿的、无疑的血食怪！
Little William: Whoa! She really is a bone-and-fide vampire!

野树莓：哼哼。
Rubuska: Told you so.

得意还没持续一会儿，下一个难题就接踵而至。
Her pride is short-lived. Another challenge soon follows.

孩童Ⅰ：既然你是血食怪，那一定什么都不怕了！你敢和那个很吓人的列车长说话吗？
Child I: So, you're a vampire. Then you must be brave. How about the scary conductress? Have you ever talked to her?

野树莓：列、列车长？咳……说话算什么，我和她可是顶要好的朋友！
Rubuska: Conductress? Umm, I mean, more than just talk. She's actually one of my best friends.

野树莓：别看她块头那么大，其实反应很迟钝，这一路少不了我的帮忙……
Rubuska: You think she's scary, huh? I'm telling you, she's big, but she's slow. If it weren't for me ...

孩子们歆羡不已地望着女孩，眼里的崇拜几乎溢满了整个车厢。
The children watch with rapt attention.

小威廉：哇……以后你就是我们的老大！
Little William: Wow, you're like a boss! Our boss!

孩子们：老大！老大！
Children: Boss! Boss!

女孩在一阵恭维声中晕眩不已，逐渐迷失自我。
She feels almost dizzy with power.

野树莓：嗯哼，既然你们强烈要求，那我只能勉为其难收了你们……
Rubuska: Well, if you insist ... Alright, fine. I'll be your boss.

告死鸟：看来你玩得很开心啊，朋友。
Corvus: Looks like you're having fun, "best friend."

一个阴沉的声音从背后响起。
A rumbling voice cuts through.

野树莓：你、你都听见了？
Rubuska: Y-You heard all that?

艾玛：我们刚进车厢，就听见你聊起列车长。真高兴你们相处得这么好呀！
Aima: We heard you the moment we entered the carriage. How wonderful to see you all getting along!

告死鸟：块头大，反应迟钝？
Corvus: "Big but slow," is that right?

野树莓：我们在玩游戏呢，哈哈，哈哈哈。
Rubuska: Haha, it's just—just a game. Hahahaha.

告死鸟：……
Corvus: ...

告死鸟：玩游戏可以，但不能阻碍车厢的过道。
Corvus: Play as you like, but don't block the aisle.

野树莓：放心，咱们可是好……好朋友，这点请求不算什么。我们会注意的！
Rubuska: Sure thing, uh, old pal. Hahaha. We'll, uh, make sure we do that.

艾玛：这些是你的新朋友们吗，野树莓小姐？
Aima: Are these your new friends, Ms. Rubuska?

乘务员的眼神在女孩与孩童们中间不住地逡巡着。
The stewardess examines the gaggle of children surrounding Rubuska.

野树莓：准确来说，他们是我的……嗯……应该是“跟班”！
Rubuska: Not just friends. They're more like, uhm, familiars!

野树莓：对吧，伙计们？
Rubuska: Right, everyone?

她努努鼻子，为自己新“收服”了“随从”而骄傲。
Rubuska sniffs, proud of her new "followers."

安娜贝尔：没错！我们是尊贵的血食……
Annabelle: Exactly! We're the familiars of the great vam—

野树莓：咳咳咳！这里太挤了，身为老大，我需要一个更加宽敞的“城堡”！
Rubuska: Ahem, ahem! This place is too crowded. I must have a larger castle, you hear me?

女孩火速打断了这个危险的话题。
She changes the subject abruptly.

野树莓：等到了新城堡，我还可以给大伙儿讲一些新的、关于“那个”的故事……
Rubuska: When we get there, I can tell you some more stories about "that."

安娜贝尔：那个？噢……那个！那个！
Annabelle: That? Oh, "that"!

孩子们：新故事！新故事！
Children: New stories! New stories!

喧闹声远去，车厢再度回归往日的宁静。
The noise fades, and the carriage returns to calm.

艾玛：真叫人羡慕呀，野树莓小姐能交到这么多朋友。
Aima: How lovely it is to see Ms. Rubuska making so many new friends. I'm almost a little jealous.

告死鸟：为什么，你没有朋友吗？
Corvus: You've never had many friends; is that why?

艾玛：我……
Aima: I …

乘务员偷偷看了一眼列车长，欲言又止。
Aima sneaks a glance at her, hesitating.

艾玛：哎呀，我想我们还是先回去吧……!塞梅尔维斯小姐还在等着呢!
Aima: Ah, it's about time we headed back. Ms. Semmelweis must be waiting.

告死鸟：嗯，走吧。
Corvus: It is. Let's go.

离开前，乘务员担忧地回望向那位调皮的乘客，想起她帽檐阴影下的笑容。
Before leaving, the stewardess casts a final worried look at the mischievous passenger, remembering her shadowed smile.

以及那双漂亮得不似真实的血色双瞳。
And those impossibly brilliant crimson eyes.

艾玛：野树莓……
Aima: Rubuska ...

TMW-05 四个半朋友 / Four and a Half Friends

列车颠簸在寒冬的风雪中。
The train rocks as it plows through the winter storm.

调查员看向窗外，脑中依然探究着那个在大雪中被递交出去的徽章。
The investigator lets her vision glaze over the scene beyond the window, still pondering the meaning of the conductress's badge.

塞梅尔维斯：她的动作很自然，显然不是第一次。
Semmelweis: She handed it over so naturally, as if she had done it countless times.

塞梅尔维斯：再加上她似乎见过基金会的人……看来这位列车长女士身上还隐藏着其他不为人知的秘密，需要更细致的调查。
Semmelweis: Plus, it appears she's encountered someone from the Foundation before. I am forced to conclude that our conductress is hiding something from me.

调查员从衣兜里掏出怀表，轻轻打开。
She pulls a pocket watch from her coat and flicks it open.

塞梅尔维斯：她们离开也有一段时间了，接下来……
Semmelweis: They've been gone for a while now. Well ...

她抬起头，眼神扫过车厢内部。
Then she looks around the room.

由于列车长的“行政流程”，调查员似乎能够在无人知晓的情况下翻看这儿的每一份载录文档。
Thanks to the conductress's fine administrative processes, every file is simple to find.

从行车时刻表到历年来的驾驶日志，这些文件于她而言，几乎触手可及。
From timetables to station logs, everything is within reach.

塞梅尔维斯：全都摆在这里，简直像是引诱我去查阅一样。
Semmelweis: These files are just sitting out on the table. Do they have no sense of confidentiality?

塞梅尔维斯：……
Semmelweis: ...

塞梅尔维斯：太容易得到的线索往往是陷阱，还是谨慎为好。
Semmelweis: An easily laid clue is often a trap, though. This could be bait. Better act cautiously.

调查员摇摇头，甩开心中的念头。
The investigator shakes her head, casting the thought aside.

告死鸟：久等了。
Corvus: I apologize for keeping you.

列车长推门而入，径直坐向她的座位，而侍候在身旁的则是她忠诚的乘务员。
Corvus enters and returns to her sofa; her loyal stewardess follows in behind.

她瞥了一眼屋内的陈设，一切依然同她离开时一样。
She takes stock of the room, confirming that nothing has changed since she left.

告死鸟：艾玛把你的行李放到了对应的座位上，别担心，“多瑙黎明号”从来没丢过东西。
Corvus: Aima has placed your luggage at your seat. No need to worry; nothing has ever gone missing from the "Danube Dawn."

告死鸟：既然你执意留在这里……那就聊聊吧，调查员。
Corvus: You've waited for some time. Where were we?

告死鸟：你先前提到上级、血食怪还有调查……
Corvus: The Foundation, your vampire, and this investigation you mentioned.

塞梅尔维斯：为了确保大家的安全，我需要对所有登车乘客的身份进行一次普查登记。
Semmelweis: To rule out any threat, I need to verify every passenger on board, carriage by carriage.

调查员转变策略，以更为直接的方式提出需求。
The investigator shifts tactics, speaking more directly.

告死鸟：……现在是战时，很多事情我们都会从简处理。突如其来的普查登记很容易让人产生不好的联想，进而引发骚乱。
Corvus: That would be controversial, especially in the midst of this war. I fear it may cause unnecessary disturbances.

告死鸟：我们都不愿意再见到白天车站发生的那一幕。
Corvus: I'm sure neither of us would like a repeat of the incident from before.

塞梅尔维斯：抱歉，我谨代表基金会前来与你进行交涉。严格来说，这是通知，而非交涉。
Semmelweis: I apologize, but my mission parameters are clear. You've misunderstood my intent; this was a notification, not a negotiation.

告死鸟：既然如此，那么麻烦出示一下允许采集乘客信息的官方同意书。
Corvus: In that case, I will need to see some formal authorization.

告死鸟：如果任何人都可以自由上车，凭借一番演讲就能对我的列车进行搜查，那我的乘客们恐怕再也不需要睡觉了。
Corvus: I won't allow someone to disturb the peace of my passengers just because they claim it to be necessary.

她挑眉望着调查员，像是笃定她手上根本没有这种东西。
She arches a brow, certain that the investigator doesn't have the authorization.

塞梅尔维斯：……多亏了“高效”的政府，我连官方同意书的影子都没看到。
Semmelweis: I fear that authorization is still little more than a draft on their desk—the "joys of bureaucracy."

塞梅尔维斯：但既然您如此看重行政手续，那么按照规定，如果您坚持不配合的话，我将会行使身为基金会调查员的权利——
Semmelweis: But as you seem to be a fan of red tape, if you refuse to cooperate, regulations state that it is within my power ...

调查员稍作停顿。
She pauses to draw out the effect.

塞梅尔维斯：紧急截停“多瑙黎明号”。
Semmelweis: To stop the "Danube Dawn."

告死鸟：……
Corvus: ...

艾玛：紧急截停？！不……
Aima: Stop the train? No.

塞梅尔维斯：很遗憾。从程序上讲，截停列车是基于条约的一项标准操作，完全合乎规定。
Semmelweis: Indeed. I am fully within my authority to stop this train at any time to conduct an investigation.

艾玛：我明白，但是……这样可能会给其他乘客造成不便……
Aima: I understand, but it could inconvenience our passengers.

塞梅尔维斯：只是对“乘客”造成不便吗？
Semmelweis: Just the passengers?

艾玛：——！！
Aima: ...!

乘务员张开嘴，又立即闭上，下意识看向身旁的列车长。
Aima opens her mouth, then closes it again, glancing at the conductress.

列车长并不言语，只轻轻拍了拍她的肩膀，随后走上前。
Corvus stands and pats her on the shoulder.

告死鸟：我明白了。
Corvus: I see.

告死鸟：我们接受你的提议，调查员。但有个条件——你的登记工作必须由乘务组亲自陪同。
Corvus: I have one stipulation that my stewardess and I accompany you during your inspection.

塞梅尔维斯：当然可以，登记工作本就应该公开透明。
Semmelweis: As you wish. I assure you the process will be carried out with openness and transparency.

告死鸟：在登记目的也公开透明的情况下，是的。
Corvus: If the purpose is likewise open and transparent, yes.

塞梅尔维斯：别担心，列车长女士。我已对你们毫无保留——在职责允许的范围内。
Semmelweis: Naturally, Conductress, I have told you everything—as far as I'm permitted, at least.

调查员保持着一贯的官方微笑。她站起身，向眼前的“伙伴”伸手示好。
The investigator maintains a practiced, businesslike smile as she extends her hand.

塞梅尔维斯：事不宜迟，现在就开始行动吧。
Semmelweis: There is no time to lose. Let's get started.

塞梅尔维斯：合作愉快，列车长女士。
Semmelweis: Glad we could come to an agreement, Conductress.

告知乘客，解释情况，登记信息……“合作”调查有条不紊地继续着。
Announcements, explanations, records ... their "cooperation" continues smoothly.

告死鸟：还有几节车厢？
Corvus: How many carriages left?

艾玛：嗯，除去驾驶室、守车和我们的休息室，再去掉这里和已经登记了的两节车厢的话……
Aima: Um, except the locomotive, the brake van, our compartment, two registered, and this one we're registering ...

塞梅尔维斯：十二减三，再减二，再减一。
Semmelweis: Twelve minus three, then minus two, then minus one.

塞梅尔维斯：还有六节车厢。
Semmelweis: 6 carriages to go.

调查员微笑着给出答案。
Semmelweis answers with a subdued smile.

多萝西：列车长，乘务员，我需要你们的帮忙……我的两个学生在车厢里走丢了。
Dorothy: Conductress, Ms. Aima, I need your help. Two of my students have gone missing.

衣着整洁、神情严肃的女士迈着稍快的步伐走来，额角已经微有汗珠。
A worried lady approaches, concern evident on her brow.

告死鸟：请冷静，女士。您和学生走散多久了？他们的样貌有什么特征吗？
Corvus: Please remain calm, madam. How long have they been missing? Could you describe them in detail?

多萝西：大概这么高，一个怀里抱着玩偶，另一个留着很短的棕色卷发，喜欢四处跑动。
Dorothy: The two of them are about this tall. The little girl always carries a doll with her, and the boy has short, brown curly hair.

多萝西：已经快要两刻钟了，就在餐车附近，他们趁着人多，把列车当成了游戏场……
Dorothy: I lost sight of them in the dining car about half an hour ago. Seems they've taken this train as some sort of playground.

艾玛：列车长……似乎是我们刚才见过的孩子们。
Aima: Conductress, they sound like the little boy and girl we met just now.

记录着样貌特征的乘务员小声提醒着列车长。
She notes down each description carefully, attentive to all the passengers.

告死鸟：哦……野树莓的“跟班”们？
Corvus: Ah, Rubuska's "familiars."

告死鸟：女士，请您回过身看看，那是不是您的两位学生？
Corvus: Look behind you, madam. Are these your students?

跟随列车长的话音，众人的视线越过半节车厢，落在车厢尾部座位的几个孩子身上。
Following the conductress's words, all eyes turn to the children at the back.

野树莓：然后呢，在荣耀而强大的阿诺德五世伯爵之后，是我了不起的祖父萨瓦诺维奇。
Rubuska: After the glorious Count Arnold V came my grandfather Savonovic!

野树莓：萨瓦诺维奇祖父带我们去了多瑙河北边的埃杰什，修建了埃杰什磨坊……不对，是城堡！
Rubuska: Grandfather Savonovic brought the whole family north of the Danube and built Arges Mill—er, I mean, Arges Castle!

野树莓：在埃杰什城堡，他活了一百六十五岁……
Rubuska: He lived to be 165 years old.

孩童们：呼……
Children: *snore*

她兴致勃勃地讲述着自己的荣耀往昔，却没注意身旁的听众已经合上双眼，几乎睡倒过去。
The girl eagerly continues her tales, unaware and unconcerned that her audience has drifted off to sleep.

多萝西：威廉！安娜贝尔！你们怎么可以没有经过我的同意就到处乱跑！
Dorothy: William! Annabelle! You can't go messing about yourselves like this!

严肃的家庭教师疾步走过去，一尘不染的裙摆扬起比平时要更大的幅度。
The governess storms over, skirt swaying wider than usual, appearing almost like a bowling ball rolling down the aisle.

安娜贝尔：嗯……唔？啊……！
Annabelle: Mmm. Hm? Ah!

小威廉：多、多萝西女士！真要命……
Little William: M-Ms. Dorothy! Uh-oh.

熟睡的孩童们一下惊醒，安娜贝尔也吓得从野树莓的膝上弹了起来。
The children jolt awake, Annabelle springing from Rubuska's lap.

多萝西：安娜贝尔！你立刻、马上给我下来，你怎么可以和……和那样的人待在一起？
Dorothy: Annabelle! You get back here right now! You should know better than to associate with that kind of company.

多萝西：还有你！威廉，赶紧给我过来！
Dorothy: That goes for you too, William! Come on, quickly!

野树莓：那……那样的人？
Rubuska: That ... that kind of company?

野树莓：是在说我吗？
Rubuska: Is she talking about me?

从这位严肃女士来回扫射的眼神之中，野树莓终于注意到自己与新朋友在衣着上的差异。
From her sharp gaze, Rubuska realizes the difference in their clothes.

一只手轻轻搭在女孩的肩膀上，打断了她的思考。
A hand lands on her shoulder, breaking her thought.

告死鸟：方便做个信息登记吗？这位小姐。
Corvus: We meet again, "old pal." We're here to register your information if you might spare the time.

野树莓：我如果说我不方便，你们会放我离开吗？
Rubuska: If I said I couldn't, would you let me go?

多萝西：列车长，我建议您好好盘查一下这个人的身份，她很有可能拐带了我的学生们……
Dorothy: I suggest you do a thorough check on her background. I suspect she could be a trafficker!

安娜贝尔：不……多萝西女士，是我迷路了……还是野树莓姐姐帮了我！
Annabelle: No, Ms. Dorothy, I was lost, a-and Rubuska helped me!

多萝西：安娜贝尔，临行前我告诉你多少遍了，在外要时刻注意身份，不管是自己的，还是别人的……
Dorothy: How many times have I told you? You are a young lady of a certain stature. It won't do to get too close to this riff-raff.

野树莓：身份……？喂，女士，请把话说清楚……
Rubuska: Riff-raff? Hey, lady, what do you mean?

艾玛：很抱歉，这位女士。这只是一次临时的乘客信息登记，并非针对野树莓小姐个人的盘查……
Aima: A-Apologies, madam, but this is just a simple passenger registration.

艾玛：别担心，我来为您登记……野树莓小姐，您的身份是？
Aima: No need to worry, Ms. Rubuska. We just have a few simple questions for you. Let's see. Um, what are you?

野树莓：我是野树莓。
Rubuska: I'm Rubuska!

她挺直腰杆，理直气壮地如此答道。
She straightens her back and speaks firmly.

塞梅尔维斯：……
Semmelweis: ...

艾玛：不、不是这样的……野树莓小姐。我的意思是……您需要登记一下种族信息。
Aima: Um, sorry, perhaps I wasn't clear. I mean your lineage.

野树莓：种族。噢，没问题！我……我是瑟尔玛尼奇人。
Rubuska: L-Lineage. Oh, sure, I'm Th-Thermanikian.

告死鸟：不是名字，不是出身地，也不是性别。
Corvus: Let's hurry this along. Not your name, nor your place of birth, nor gender.

告死鸟：“神秘学家”还是“人类”？
Corvus: Arcanist or human?

野树莓：哦！那我大概，应该是……
Rubuska: Oh! Um, then, I guess I'm ...

告死鸟：没有第三种选项。
Corvus: There is no third option.

野树莓：你怎么知道……好吧！我，我是……
Rubuska: Wow, how do you know? Alright! I, I'm—

女孩面露难色，眼神躲闪，可一旁的小孩子却替她开了口。
The girl falters, eyes dodging, but it's William that leaps to explain.

小威廉：她是我们的血食怪老大，当然是神秘学家！
Little William: She's our vampire boss; of course she's an arcanist.

多萝西：住口！威廉！谁教你这么说话的？
Dorothy: Silence, William! Who taught you to say such things?

艾玛：……咦！
Aima: Oh!

塞梅尔维斯&告死鸟：……
Semmelweis & Corvus: ...

野树莓：哈哈，我刚才和孩子们开玩笑瞎编的，这可作不得数！
Rubuska: Ha, hahaha, ah, I was just messing around with the kids.

野树莓：难、难道你们小时候没玩过过家家游戏吗？我不仅扮演过血食怪，还扮演过狼人、鲁萨尔卡……
Rubuska: Didn't you ever play make-believe when you were young? Vampires, werewolves, Rusalka ...

告死鸟：我从没有过这种经历。
Corvus: I did not.

列车长异常冷淡地打断女孩。
The conductress coldly interrupts her.

告死鸟：现在是非常时期，以后别在列车上开这种玩笑。
Corvus: Given these extraordinary times, I'll ask that there be no more such make-believe on the train.

野树莓：我发誓，我以后再也不敢了——
Rubuska: I won't do it again, I swear.

野树莓呼出的一口气还悬在半空中，一旁刚刚从睡梦中清醒，对眼前的情境感到十分困惑的女孩却开了口。
She exhales, but Annabelle, now awake and confused, speaks up.

安娜贝尔：可是姐姐，你确实是血食怪呀。
Annabelle: But you are a vampire, Rubuska.

空气变得安静。
The air stills.

安娜贝尔：你还用影子向我们证明了……你说，真正的血食怪是没有影子的。
Annabelle: You don't have a shadow. You showed us. And real vampires don't have shadows, right?

安娜贝尔：血食怪都很厉害，很强大，而且姐姐是善良的血食怪，我觉得……我觉得你们都应该尊重她。
Annabelle: Vampires are really, really strong, and Rubuska is a good vampire. S-So you should all be nice to her!

她鼓起勇气，顶着家庭教师愈发可怕的神情，声音小且坚定地为众人的态度提出了质疑。
She gathers her courage, standing firm even under the governess's glare, her voice quiet but sure as she challenges their attitude.

人们齐刷刷低头望向女孩脚下，那里的地毯上刺绣着精美的花卉与几何图样，却不见一丝阴影。
The crowd looks down to the finely embroidered carpet beneath the girl's feet and fails to find her shadow.

艾玛：呀，真的没有影子。
Aima: She's right. She really has no shadow.

野树莓：呃……糟了……
Rubuska: Uh-oh.

告死鸟：这就是你所谓的……“玩笑”。
Corvus: You call this "messing around"?

列车长上前一步，高大的身影吓得孩童们连连后退。
The patchwork conductress takes a step forward, her towering figure making the children stumble back in fear.

她的手再次搭上女孩的肩膀，兼具礼仪与力量，不让女孩有任何逃离的机会。
Her hand rests once more on Rubuska's shoulder, firm yet proper.

告死鸟：很遗憾，接下来你需要跟我们走一趟。
Corvus: You're going to have to come with us.

告死鸟：——根据“多瑙黎明号”列车安全手册，我将依照规章制度，对你进行封闭审讯。
Corvus: I'm afraid that "Danube Dawn" security protocol dictates an immediate closed interrogation.

TMW-06 野树莓的证词 / The Suspect's Testimony

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

你是谁？
Who are you?

野树莓：……野树莓。
Rubuska: I'm Rubuska.

野树莓：好了，别开这种玩笑了……这一点也不好玩。
Rubuska: Are we done? This isn't funny, you know.

上车的目的是什么？
What's your purpose on this train?

野树莓：去布达佩斯，找工作，讨生活。
Rubuska: I'm going to Budapest to find a job.

野树莓：快放开我……
Rubuska: Let me go.

你的其他同伴呢？
Do you have any companions aboard?

野树莓：哼，你见过成群结队的血食怪吗？
Rubuska: Hmph, vampires don't team up.

野树莓：其他人怕我还来不及呢。
Rubuska: People are too scared of me.

你是血食怪吗？
Are you a vampire?

野树莓：好吧，我是……
Rubuska: Yeah, I'm a vampire, okay?

野树莓：但是血食怪又怎么了，我什么也没做……
Rubuska: But so what? I didn't do anything.

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

女孩耷拉着脑袋，从头发丝到脚后跟都透着沮丧。
She hangs her head, her whole body radiating defeat.

塞梅尔维斯：她身上没有重塑之手术式的痕迹，看样子确实与他们无关。
Semmelweis: She doesn't bear any signs of Manus Vindictae's rituals. She may indeed be innocent.

塞梅尔维斯：但也不能完全排除嫌疑。谨慎起见……
Semmelweis: But can't rule her out for definite yet. Best to be safe.

她回到列车长身旁。
Semmelweis returns to the conductress's side.

塞梅尔维斯：我已经检查过了。她没有危险，不是我要找的人。
Semmelweis: I've checked her over. She's not a threat, nor is she my target.

告死鸟：所以你要找的，并非普通的血食怪。
Corvus: Then this isn't any ordinary vampire you're searching for.

塞梅尔维斯：很抱歉，我只按规章办事，更具体的细节不便透露。
Semmelweis: I'm not at liberty to say.

野树莓：哦……你们都听到了吧？她说过了，我没有危险！
Rubuska: You hear that? She says I'm not a threat!

她再度雀跃起来，脸上也恢复了一点血色。
Soon, she perks up again, a hint of color returning to her face.

塞梅尔维斯：不过按照规定，血食怪属于危险生物，理应被收容监禁。
Semmelweis: But, according to regulations, dangerous creatures like vampires should be contained in such situations.

野树莓：呃……？
Rubuska: Huh?

塞梅尔维斯：这是为了其他乘客的安全着想。一只饥饿的小血食怪，又是在列车这样的封闭空间里——你的存在本身便是一种威胁。
Semmelweis: It's for the safety of all passengers. A hungry young vampire in an enclosed space like the train is always a risk.

野树莓：我……我不接受监禁。我现在也不饿！
Rubuska: N-No, don't lock me up! I'm not even hungry!

塞梅尔维斯：这不是请求，是告知。既然你承认自己是血食怪……
Semmelweis: This is not a request; it's a notification. You've already admitted that you're a vampire.

野树莓：血食怪血食怪血食怪！血食怪又怎么了？！
Rubuska: Vampire, vampire, vampire! Yeah, I'm a vampire, so what?!

女孩抬起头，眼里升起两团熊熊燃烧的怒火。
Her ruby eyes seem ablaze with fury.

野树莓：我咬过任何人吗？我吸过任何人哪怕一滴血吗？我伤害过任何人吗？
Rubuska: Have I bitten anyone? Have I sucked any blood? Have I hurt even a single person?

野树莓：真搞不懂你们这些人……
Rubuska: I don't understand you people.

野树莓：你们老爱把人分门别类，戴上不同的帽子，再根据这些帽子来决定你们的态度，就好像你们的大脑只是源源不断的帽子的奴隶。
Rubuska: Always putting everyone in boxes and then treating them differently just because you put them there! It's like your brains are all square or something!

野树莓：上一秒我们还是朋友，下一秒你们就要把我绑起来。一切都是因为这些帽子。
Rubuska: One minute we're friends, and then the next you're tying me up. All because of these boxes you're so obsessed with.

野树莓：就因为这些愚蠢的帽子，到处都在打仗，野树莓只能四处流浪……
Rubuska: It's because of these boxes—these stupid labels—that this whole war started. Why I have nowhere to go?

野树莓：现在你们迫不及待想要为我戴上帽子，很好，我可以满足你们。
Rubuska: And now you can't wait to do the same to me. Then, fine, go ahead!

配合着语调，她的眼中逐渐蓄满泪水。
Tears begin to streak down her face.

野树莓：没错，我就是血食怪！既然大家都讨厌我们、害怕我们，那还愣着干什么……
Rubuska: I'm a vampire! Everyone hates me! Go on! What are you waiting for?

野树莓：快快服从帽子的神圣意志，将我钉死在木桩上吧！
Rubuska: Follow your rules! Pierce me through with a stake!

告死鸟&塞梅尔维斯：……
Corvus & Semmelweis: ...

艾玛：哇！野树莓，你……
Aima: Goodness, Rubuska, you ...

车厢内一片寂静。人们打量着眼前的少女，仿佛又重新认识了她。
The carriage is silent for a moment. The passengers stare at the girl as if seeing her anew.

列车长默默将缠绕在女孩身上的毛线圈松开少许。
The conductress loosens the strings that bind her.

告死鸟：抱歉，你挣扎得太厉害，我们不得不……
Corvus: Apologies, we had to tie you up to prevent you from—

野树莓：啊哈，终于露出破绽了——
Rubuska: Ah-ha! The weakness is revealed.

野树莓：我咬！
Rubuska: Take this, pal!

野树莓：呃啊——我还一口都没咬到呢……
Rubuska: Argh! I didn't even get a good bite in!

“囚犯”徒劳的反抗被列车长轻而易举地化解，列车长握住她的肩膀，使她动弹不得。
Resistance is futile. The conductress pins her down with ease.

告死鸟：你很勇敢。
Corvus: You're brave.

告死鸟：很莽撞。
Corvus: Bold, even.

告死鸟：但很遗憾，我还不能放开你。
Corvus: But you're not going anywhere for now.

野树莓：放开我……放开——
Rubuska: Let me go! Let me—

告死鸟：交给你了，调查员。“多瑙黎明号”不是拘留所，我们没有义务替你看管小孩。
Corvus: I'll leave her to you, Investigator. The "Danube Dawn" is not a detention center. We have no obligation to take care of your travel companion.

塞梅尔维斯：……
Semmelweis: ...

一个不大不小的“麻烦”。
A minor nuisance, nothing more.

如果不是那几个失踪的队友，调查员并不介意做一天临时教管。
If it were not for her missing teammates, the investigator wouldn't mind playing chaperone for a day.

艾玛：……我们可以代为看管她的，对吗，列车长？
Aima: But, perhaps we could offer a personal favor to Ms. Semmelweis?

一直沉默的乘务员小心翼翼地开口。
The stewardess, silent until now, finally speaks with a strange note of eagerness.

艾玛：找一个车厢，然后把她放进去。我、我会负责照顾——不对，看管小树莓的！
Aima: I'm sure I could find an empty room to take care of her, I mean, keep an eye on her.

告死鸟：……
Corvus: ...

告死鸟：今天晚些时候列车会抵达边境检查站。
Corvus: The train will arrive at the border checkpoint later today.

告死鸟：在此之前，由我们来看护她。
Corvus: She can stay with us until then.

调查员轻轻松了一口气，这似乎是眼下唯一的选择。
Semmelweis lets out a steady, meaningful breath, resigned to this course of action.

塞梅尔维斯：感谢您的配合。
Semmelweis: I appreciate your cooperation.

野树莓：等等，你们问过我的意见了吗？又想把我关到什么地方！
Rubuska: Wait, what about what I think? Where are you taking me?

仿佛看出了“囚犯”的不安，乘务员轻轻握住了她的手。
Sensing the girl's unease, Aima gently takes her hand.

艾玛：你可以去我的房间，小树莓。
Aima: You can stay in my room, Rubi.

艾玛：我的房间里还有一张沙发，里面填充了最柔软的鹅毛。你要是困了，就好好睡一觉。
Aima: There's an extra sofa stuffed with goose feathers. It's ever so soft. You're welcome to have a rest there if you're tired.

野树莓：小树莓？
Rubuska: Rubi?

野树莓：不管怎么说，鹅毛做的沙发，听上去还挺诱人……
Rubuska: Come to think of it, that sofa does sound tempting.

告死鸟：这叫“软禁”。
Corvus: Call it "house arrest."

告死鸟：走吧，带她过去。
Corvus: Allow us to escort you.

一大一小两个身影穿行在狭小的列车走廊中。
The two figures march down the narrow train corridor.

一个被拎起衣领，另一个几乎顶到了天花板，二者紧密依靠，像是不可分割的有机和谐整体。
One dangles by her collar, the other nearly scraping the roof. Together, an inseparable, uncanny whole.

野树莓：哎哟，轻点儿！你扯着我的头发了……
Rubuska: Ach, watch it! You're pulling my hair!

野树莓：我要把你们全都咬一遍……我发誓……
Rubuska: I'll bite you! All of you! I swear ...

如果忽略一点小小的杂音的话。
If you ignore the faintest bit of noise, that is.

TMW-07 多瑙黎明 / The Danube Dawn

野树莓：非法拘禁——非法拘禁——放我出去——
Rubuska: This is illegal, you know? Criminal! Let me out.

野树莓：放我出去……
Rubuska: Let me out.

女孩大声叫嚷着，右耳紧贴在门背上，恨不得要将自己整个儿塞进去。
The girl shouts, pressing her right ear hard against the door, desperate to melt into it.

“嗒嗒，嗒……”
"Tap, tap ... tap ..."

脚步声越来越轻，伴随着回音在空旷的走廊里逐渐消失。
The footsteps grow fainter, echoing down the empty hallway.

野树莓：嗯……终于走远了！接下来嘛……
Rubuska: Phew, finally gone. Alright, Rubuska, what's next?

她从破布条中抽出一根金属小玩意儿，凑近门锁。
She pulls a metal trinket from her rags and brings it to the lock.

野树莓：想把我关起来？
Rubuska: Think this lock'll stop me, eh?

野树莓：这么个门锁可难不倒我。
Rubuska: Hmph. You're going to have to try harder than that.

野树莓：好耶，成了！
Rubuska: Gotcha!

门悄无声息地打开了一道缝。
The door opens, only to a sliver, just wide enough for a ruby eye.

野树莓：很好，附近没有人。
Rubuska: Okay, coast is clear.

野树莓：轻松搞定。不愧是你，野树莓！
Rubuska: Hah. Easy. You've done it again, Rubuska.

她双手叉腰，正准备向自由迈出一步——
She plants her hands on her hips triumphantly, only one more step before freedom.

艾玛：小树莓？
Aima: Rubi?

野树莓：——！！
Rubuska: ...!

野树莓：你、你从什么地方冒出来的……
Rubuska: Wh-Where did you come from?

艾玛指了指背后。当门打开时，小乘务员的身影便被这扇门给牢牢挡住了。
Aima gestures behind her. As the door swings open, the small stewardess is revealed, standing in place.

野树莓：你，我，呃……
Rubuska: You, I, uh ...

未曾料想的情况使女孩陷入了短暂的大脑空白。错过了最佳的辩解时机，女孩只能放弃挣扎。
Caught off guard, Rubi freezes. She doubts her chances to talk her way out of this.

野树莓：好吧，你想怎么办？要去给你的老大打小报告吗？
Rubuska: Alright, I'm caught. So, what, you going to report me to your boss?

艾玛：嘘……
Aima: Shh ...

乘务员伸出食指放在嘴唇上，朝野树莓眨了眨眼。
The stewardess presses a finger to her lips and winks at Rubuska.

艾玛：小声一点，他们会听见的。
Aima: Be quiet, or they'll hear you.

艾玛：你好像在害怕，我能闻到。
Aima: Are you afraid? I can smell it on you.

野树莓：害怕？那你恐怕还不了解我。所以……你会告诉她们吗？
