Rubuska: Afraid? *scoff* Clearly you don't know me. So, are you going to tell them or not?

艾玛：没关系。只要你不乱跑，我不会告诉她们的。
Aima: As long as you don't go running off, I won't.

乘务员左右张望一眼后，走入室内，轻轻关上房门。
She checks the hall, then slips inside, delicately closing the door.

野树莓：你、你想做什么？列车长她们人呢？
Rubuska: So, uh, why are you here? Where's the conductress?

艾玛：塞梅尔维斯小姐说她还需要查阅一点儿有关列车的资料，两个人现在一同待在守车里呢。
Aima: They're in the brake van. Ms. Semmelweis needs to check over some files.

艾玛：放心吧，不会有事的。一个人看门总是容易犯困……不如我们来聊聊天吧。
Aima: Don't worry. Anyway, it's a bit dull all alone in here. Why don't we have a chat? Come, sit next to me.

乘务员轻巧地坐上沙发，拍了拍身旁的空位。
Aima reclines on the sofa, patting the space beside her.

野树莓：我……
Rubuska: I …

女孩看了看自己黑乎乎的手心和裤脚。
The girl glances at her dark palms and ragged cuffs.

野树莓：我身上不干净，会弄脏你的沙发。
Rubuska: My clothes are kind of dirty. I don't wanna mess up your sofa.

艾玛：没关系……我是沙发的主人，我说了算。
Aima: Really, I don't mind.

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

温声的宽慰并未起到应有的作用。女孩仍旧站在原地，仿佛双腿生了根。
Warm words don't reach her. She stays rooted to the floor.

艾玛：既然你不愿意……
Aima: Hmm, then how about ...

乘务员忽然合掌一拍，灵光一闪般抓起野树莓。
The stewardess claps her hands, then seizes Rubuska as if inspired.

艾玛：那我来给你换一件衣服，这样你总愿意和我一块坐下来了吧！
Aima: Ah! Let's get you changed! Then you can join me without a worry!

野树莓：你，你要做什么……哎哟，你力气好大……
Rubuska: Wait, I didn't—Ah, Lord, you're strong!

艾玛：这件，还有这件……找到了！
Aima: Not this ... or this one ... Ah! Found you!

艾玛：来，看看这件！
Aima: Here, put this on!

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

艾玛：这看起来……真可爱！
Aima: Oh my! You look wonderful!

野树莓：合身吗？
Rubuska: Does it fit?

艾玛：非常、非常、非常合身！
Aima: Oh, it fits you splendidly!

艾玛：现在我宣布，这件衣服是你的了！
Aima: I hereby declare that these clothes are yours to keep!

野树莓：真、真的吗……
Rubuska: R-Really?

天晓得她多久没换过一身干净衣服了。
God knows how long it's been since she's worn clean clothes.

红白相间的针脚紧密相扣，在裙摆上画出一个美丽的弧度。
Red-and-white stitching traces arcs across the hem of her skirt.

女孩一眨也不眨地看着它们，说不出一个拒绝的字眼。
She chokes back words, trying to believe what she sees.

野树莓：谢谢你，艾玛。
Rubuska: Thank you, Aima.

野树莓：对了。这里有这么多衣服，为什么没有镜子呀？
Rubuska: Hold on, why don't you have a mirror in your room? You've got so many clothes.

乘务员羞赧地摸了摸右眼的眼罩。
The stewardess shyly touches her eyepatch.

艾玛：我、我的眼睛不好看，不习惯照镜子。
Aima: Oh, I don't much like mirrors. My eyes aren't very pretty.

野树莓：真是胡说！你明明那样好看，那样……
Rubuska: What're you talking about?! You, I mean, your eyes, um, eye looks good—more than good! You're ...

野树莓：……总之，你什么都很好。
Rubuska: Well, in short, you're good through and through!

说完她挠了挠头，勉强将视线调转到眼前衣物堆积的小山上。
She scratches her head, gaze sliding to the pile of garments stacked nearby.

野树莓：以前我也有这么大一柜子东西，绸子的、羊毛的，纱的……什么料子都有。
Rubuska: I used to have a closet like yours, filled with silks, cashmere, corduroy ... All kinds.

野树莓：这么多衣服，都是你自己收藏的吗？
Rubuska: Did you buy all these clothes yourself?

艾玛：不是哦，大多是我的家人送给我的。
Aima: Oh, no. Most of them are from a family member.

艾玛：他说乘务员的生活太单调了，就连制服也是……所以只要出了远门，他就会带新的衣服给我。
Aima: He said that life as a stewardess is as boring as our uniforms, so whenever he goes off on a long trip, he buys me new clothes.

艾玛：这样我穿上新衣服的时候，就好像也陪家人一起去了那些地方。
Aima: That way, no matter how far apart we are, I always feel like he's right here with me.

野树莓：家人……哼，确实挺单调的。我像你这么大的时候，已经一个人跑过很多地方啦！
Rubuska: Family. Pft, boring! By the time I was your age, I'd already been halfway around the peninsula all by myself.

艾玛：哈哈，你的生活听上去好精彩呀！不过我觉得，在列车上也不错呢。
Aima: Haha, goodness, that sounds wonderful! But I think my life is rather pleasant too.

艾玛：看着不同的乘客上上下下，每天都有新的故事。对我来说，这也是一种“旅行”。
Aima: Every day the train welcomes new passengers, all bringing their own stories. I can "travel" without ever having to leave.

艾玛：还有列车长，她虽然总是板着脸，但一直都在照顾我们。不仅如此，她还是一位顶好的裁缝呢！
Aima: And the conductress looks after us. I know she seems stern and maybe a little angry, but she's truly lovely underneath, and a wonderful tailor too!

女孩指向车窗边摆放着的一排套娃。
She points to the row of matryoshkas by the window.

艾玛：你看！这些娃娃身上的衣服也是她亲手织的，是不是很可爱？
Aima: See the clothes on the matryoshkas? She made every single one. Aren't they darling?

套娃们身着保暖的、花色活泼的小毛衣，朝野树莓露出整齐划一的、憨厚且无害的微笑。
Each wears a colorful knit sweater, their smiles stiff yet harmless.

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

野树莓：我有个问题，艾玛。这趟列车上该不会有两个列车长吧？
Rubuska: Wait, sorry. Are there two conductresses on this train?

野树莓：不然我实在难以想象……不，我完全无法想象……
Rubuska: I mean, I just, no, I can't picture it at all.

野树莓狠狠甩头，试图甩开意外涌入脑海的诡异场景。
Rubuska jerks her head, attempting to banish the uncanny image.

野树莓：列车长？织毛衣？
Rubuska: That conductress? Knitting little sweaters?

野树莓：不……光是想象这个场景，就已经叫人很害怕了……
Rubuska: *shudder* Just imagining it is giving me the creeps.

告死鸟：……
Corvus: ...

塞梅尔维斯：列车长女士，您的东西掉了。
Semmelweis: Conductress, you dropped this.

红色的线团滚落到正在一旁整理资料的调查员脚边。
A ball of red yarn rolls to Semmelweis's feet.

调查员拾起它，无比自然地递到列车长身边。
She picks it up, handing it back to the conductress.

告死鸟：谢谢。有关列车的资料都在这里了，行车日志在左边第一个抽屉，交接班记录本在右边第二个抽屉最底层，调度指令就在桌上……
Corvus: Thank you. All the files are here. Logbook's in the first drawer on the left; shift handover logs are at the bottom of the second drawer on the right; dispatch instructions are on the table.

塞梅尔维斯：我明白了，感谢您的配合。
Semmelweis: Much appreciated. Thank you again for your cooperation.

叮嘱完成后，列车长继续织起手中长长的围巾，不声不响地坐在沙发上“陪伴”着调查员的工作。
Without a word, Corvus resumes her handiwork; the scarf billows out with every stitch, keeping silent company.

难得和平的共处时光。或许，这也是一个了解对方的好机会。
A rare moment of peace. Perhaps a chance to understand each other.

塞梅尔维斯：很整齐的针脚。真没有想到，您的业余爱好是针线活。
Semmelweis: The stitching on this is immaculate. I'm surprised to see you're fond of needlework.

告死鸟：在我的家乡，所有人都会这个。这不稀奇。
Corvus: It's a common skill, nothing special.

生硬的语调，生硬的收尾。话题终结。
Blunt words, blunt endings. The topic dies.

调查员只得继续翻阅手头的文件。无数列车的参数和零件一一略过，调查员看了一会儿，再度寻找到了一个话题的突破口。
The investigator returns to her files, scanning endless logs and numbers until she finds another opening.

塞梅尔维斯：“多瑙黎明”……我一直觉得这个名字很有趣。它的背后有什么寓意吗？
Semmelweis: The name of this train is very intriguing to me. The "Danube Dawn" ... Does it hold any special meaning?

告死鸟：……
Corvus: ...

车厢内一片寂静，只余车轮摩擦在铁轨上单调而冗长的声音。
The carriage hums with the grinding of wheels.

话题再度终结。
Another topic dies.

塞梅尔维斯：抱歉。我似乎忘了，我们之间不是能坐在一起闲聊的友爱关系……
Semmelweis: Sorry. I've never been much good at small talk or knowing when it's appropriate or with whom ...

告死鸟：把多瑙河沿岸的所有地区，联合在一起。
Corvus: To unite all regions along the Danube.

塞梅尔维斯：……？
Semmelweis: ...?

告死鸟：刚才你问我，“多瑙黎明”名字背后的寓意。我现在正在回答你。
Corvus: You asked if it meant something.

列车长停顿了一下，静静地看着调查员的眼睛。
She pauses her work to meet the investigator's eyes.

告死鸟：其实很简单，和它字面的意思一样：把多瑙河沿岸的所有地区联合在一起，然后……
Corvus: It's simple: Unite all regions along the Danube, and ...

告死鸟：一起驶向明天。
Corvus: Move forward into the new day as one.

野树莓：联合在一起？怎么个联合法？
Rubuska: Unite all regions?

另一头，两个女孩并肩靠在柔软的沙发上，感受着身下轮毂行进时带来的震颤。
Elsewhere, two girls lean against one another on a plush sofa, feeling the rhythmic tremor of the wheels beneath them.

艾玛：从伊斯坦布尔一路走到维也纳，中间经过贝尔格莱德、尼卡和布达佩斯……
Aima: From Istanbul to Vienna, through Belgrade, Nika, and Budapest ...

手指在半空中轻盈地划出一条蜿蜒的弧线。
Fingers trace lazy lines through the air.

艾玛：你瞧，是不是正好将多瑙河沿岸的地区都包含在内了？
Aima: See how the train is like a line connecting all the dots along the Danube?

野树莓：联合起来……真讽刺，现在他们正打得不可开交呢。
Rubuska: Huh. Makes the war seem even more ironic.

艾玛：哎呀……我也弄不清楚大人们的事情，太复杂啦。
Aima: Well, I don't really understand all that's going on out there.

艾玛：我只知道我很喜欢这个名字。“多瑙黎明”，听上去很温暖，就像一个大家庭一样。
Aima: But I do know that I like this name. The "Danube Dawn"—it sounds warm and bright, like we're all a big family.

艾玛：其实，刚才你说的那些话我也很赞同！为什么大人不能坐下来，扔掉那些帽子，好好谈谈呢？
Aima: What you said earlier about putting people in boxes—I feel the same way. Why can't they just sit down and have a good chat, like we're doing now?

野树莓雀跃起来。
Rubuska brightens.

野树莓：哈哈，你也同意我的观点是吧！我就知道我们合得来！
Rubuska: I know, right? Haha, I knew we'd get along!

艾玛：当然。我喜欢人类，也喜欢神秘学家，血食怪……
Aima: Of course! I get along with all types. Humans, arcanists, vampires ...

她偷偷看了一眼野树莓。
She makes a sly glance toward Rubuska.

艾玛：你还是我见到的第一个血食怪呢！这种感觉很新奇，我很喜欢你。
Aima: Actually, you're the first vampire I've ever met. It's a little strange and new, but I'm not scared. I like you.

野树莓：嗯哼！我也……不讨厌你。不过我很好奇，像你这样的家伙……你有不喜欢的人吗？
Rubuska: Hah, yeah! You're not so bad yourself. But, is there actually anyone you don't like?

乘务员仰起头，仔细思索了一番。
The stewardess tilts her head back in deep thought.

艾玛：……好像没有。
Aima: Hmm, I can't think of anyone.

野树莓：哼，我就知道。大家都喜欢你，你也喜欢大家。你是个幸福的小公主。
Rubuska: Hmph, knew it. You like everyone, and everyone likes you. Like a happy little princess.

“小公主”点点头，大方接受了新朋友略带酸意的点评。
The "princess" nods, graciously accepting her teasing.

艾玛：我很感激自己能拥有这样的生活，所以我希望你们也一样。
Aima: I'm grateful for the life I'm living, and I hope you are too.

艾玛：大家能和平共处最好啦。
Aima: My only wish is that everyone could live together peacefully.

她轻轻握住野树莓的手。
She clasps Rubuska's hand.

艾玛：就像这样，你看——
Aima: Like this, see—

艾玛：五根手指，原本各自分开，彼此孤单。
Aima: Our fingers are born separate and alone.

艾玛：可一旦握紧，它们就成了一体，再也分不开了。
Aima: But if we lock them together, they become one. Nothing can break them apart.

野树莓：哼，这有什么。只要我想，随时都能挣脱……
Rubuska: Pft, no, they don't. I could break free anytime I want, oh.

她往后缩了一点，艾玛的手却依旧扣在她掌心，温柔而坚定。
The girl recoils slightly, but Aima's grip holds, gentle yet firm.

艾玛：你希望挣脱开吗？小树莓。
Aima: Do you want to break free, Rubi?

野树莓：我……
Rubuska: I …

两人的皮肤都很白，白得几乎透明，手背上青色的血管若隐若现。
Her pale hands are nearly translucent, faint blue veins showing through.

此刻，她们掌心相贴，那些细细的脉络也仿佛悄然缠绕、连接在了一起。
Palm to palm, those threads intertwine, binding them.

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

塞梅尔维斯：联合多瑙河沿岸，一起驶向明天？真是意想不到的愿景。
Semmelweis: Unite together and move into a new day as one? That's a truly unimaginable concept.

昔日的创始人们全票通过了这个名字，那时他们的心中没有阴影，眼里盛满光明。
Dream though it was, the spirit of the times brought many who believed it could be real,

他们坚信，多瑙河永不停歇，它将一直流向未来。
wanting to believe the lands along the Danube could live as one.

塞梅尔维斯：真正的理想主义，自然……也很不切实际。
Semmelweis: Idealism does often come hand in hand with impracticality.

塞梅尔维斯：虽然我不理解，但我敬佩他们对信念的执着——至少在说出那些话的时候，他们是真诚而坚定的。
Semmelweis: Still, it's admirable to stand firm in your beliefs. Impractical or not, I respect it.

告死鸟：……
Corvus: ...

意料之外的回应让列车长短暂沉默了一会儿。
Her unexpected approval is met with an equally strange curiosity.

针尖仍旧在柔软的织物中穿梭。列车长的眼神变得温柔而专注。她先用左手将线圈绕过右针的头，再熟练地把线从上方拉回……
Her needles continue their motion. With her left hand, she loops the yarn over the right needle's tip, then deftly draws it back down.

每一次拉紧毛线，织物便更加紧密，在她的指尖下结成坚不可破的堡垒。
Each pull tightens the fabric, fortress walls forming beneath her fingers.

再度开口时，她的声音带上了几分柔和。
When she speaks again, her voice has softened.

告死鸟：对我来说都没有区别，我只负责完成我的本职工作。
Corvus: It's no difference to me. This is only a job.

告死鸟：十三节车厢，一个不少，我会把大家都平安带到安全的地方。
Corvus: Deliver thirteen carriages and our passengers from one point to another safely. That's it.

塞梅尔维斯：十三节，你确定吗？
Semmelweis: Thirteen carriages? Are you sure?

调查员敏锐地捕捉到了这个关键的数字。
The investigator catches the crucial number.

塞梅尔维斯：没有哪趟列车会选用这个倒霉的数字。
Semmelweis: Seems unusual to choose an unlucky number for a train.

针尖停滞了一瞬。
The needle halts.

告死鸟：加上火车头的话……可以是十三。
Corvus: I meant ... including the locomotive.

告死鸟：你不能说火车头不算一节“车厢”。这只是一个简单的定义问题。
Corvus: "Rolling stock," then? I didn't want to be too technical.

塞梅尔维斯：……好吧，那祝你顺利，列车长女士。
Semmelweis: It's fine, really. I suppose I should wish you luck, Conductress.

塞梅尔维斯：毕竟，把大家平安带到安全的地方是我们共同的期望。我说得对吗？
Semmelweis: After all, it is our common goal to have the train arrive safely, yes?

告死鸟：当然。让你在这里自由地查阅资料，这就是我的“照应”。现在……
Corvus: Which is why you've been allowed access here. Now ...

最后一针终于完成，列车长停下了手中的活计。
The last stitch done, Corvus sets her work aside.

现在，一条松软的红色围巾静静地躺在她的膝上。
A soft red scarf now rests in her lap.

塞梅尔维斯：很漂亮。我想艾玛会喜欢的。
Semmelweis: It's a beautiful scarf. I'm sure Aima will appreciate it.

告死鸟：谢谢。
Corvus: Thank you.

笑意一闪而过。
A flicker of a smile.

列车长的视线越过调查员，看向挂钟，确认时间。
Her gaze slips to the clock, checking the time.

告死鸟：你的资料查阅工作有进展了吗？
Corvus: Have you made any progress?

塞梅尔维斯：也不算全无收获。我找到了一批预定乘客的信息，可以用于参考对照，以防部分乘客没有说实话。
Semmelweis: Not much, but I did find something helpful—the ticket reservation log. Could be useful to cross-check against what our passengers said.

列车长点点头。
She nods.

告死鸟：那很好。我们已经在这里待得够久了。
Corvus: Good. We've been here long enough.

告死鸟：走吧，调查员，继续你的职责。我还有其他工作，接下来可能要失陪了。
Corvus: If you'll excuse me, I have a job to do.

塞梅尔维斯：没关系。合作愉快，列车长女士。
Semmelweis: It's been a pleasure working with you, Conductress.

她与列车长一同开门离去。
Together, they rise and step out.

室外风雪吹袭，列车正疾行平静的夜色之中。
A blizzard rages outside, buffeting the train as it speeds into the night.

TMW-08 铁道猫 / The Railway Cat

时间已来到深夜。完成登记的乘客陆续回到各自的车厢，在香软的卧铺中进入沉沉梦乡。
The hour is late and the lamps dim. Passengers return to their compartments one by one, the soft sway of the train soothing them to sleep like a lullaby.

喧嚣散尽，车厢内只剩两名乘客面对面坐着，彼此沉默不语。
Only two passengers remain in the shared space, seated face-to-face in silence.

塞梅尔维斯：……
Semmelweis: ...

空心木：……
Verity: ...

塞梅尔维斯：这位女士，你可以先放下笔。现在是我在做信息登记。
Semmelweis: Madam, would you mind putting down your pen? I need to take your information.

空心木：空心木，英国人，神秘学家。喜欢咖啡、银鳕鱼还有起风的夜晚。
Verity: Verity, British, arcanist. I like coffee, battered cod, and breezy nights.

空心木：讨厌截稿日和下雨天。
Verity: I hate deadlines and rainy days.

空心木：好了，以上就是我能给到你的全部信息。接下来轮到我了……
Verity: There. That's all there is to know about me. Now it's my turn to ask the questions.

撰稿人放下笔，忽然凑了上来。
The editor sets down her pen then leans deep, as if passing along a secret.

空心木：找到了吗？
Verity: Have you found it?

塞梅尔维斯：我不太明白您的意思。
Semmelweis: I don't know what you're talking about.

空心木：哦，看样子是没有。
Verity: Hah. Well, that's a "no," then.

她兴致缺缺地朝调查员摆了摆手。
She waves her hand halfheartedly.

空心木：在你这样一本正经的家伙身上，再有趣的素材恐怕都会变成乏味的档案记录。
Verity: No matter. I'm sure even the most compelling of stories would turn to a dull report when put in your hands.

空心木：再见，祝你工作顺利。
Verity: Goodbye. Best of luck with your work.

调查员干脆地收起笔和文件，然而撰稿人像是忽然想到了什么，再度开口。
Semmelweis closes her pen and files, but the editor, struck by a thought, speaks again.

空心木：不过……看你这么辛苦地忙前忙后，我就投喂你一点儿“小甜点”吧。
Verity: Ah, but since you've been looking so diligently, I suppose I might throw you a bone.

塞梅尔维斯：嗯？
Semmelweis: Yes?

撰稿人凑近身子，诡魅地朝调查员眨了眨眼。
She leans closer still, giving a wink to the investigator.

空心木：听说……之前的乘客总能在夜晚听到哭声。
Verity: Rumor is many passengers aboard this train have heard crying during the night.

塞梅尔维斯：哭声？什么样的哭声？
Semmelweis: Crying? What kind of crying?

空心木：唔……
Verity: Hmm ...

空心木：一开始很轻，后来嘶嘶地、很长很长，像一条线……然后又突然卡住了。
Verity: It starts soft, then turns to a hissing sound, lasting, echoing, and then, all of a sudden, it stops.

她慢慢掐住自己的脖子，朝调查员露出微笑。
She grips her own throat, smiling at the investigator.

空心木：……就像小猫被掐住一样。
Verity: Like a kitten being strangled.

塞梅尔维斯：……
Semmelweis: ...

空心木：怎么样，喜欢我讲的鬼故事吗？
Verity: Well? How did you like my little ghost story?

塞梅尔维斯：哦，还不错。你后面有东西，就悬在半空中……看上去很像那只被掐住的小猫。
Semmelweis: Wait, there's something behind you, hanging in midair. It looks like a strangled kitten.

她面无表情地回击了一个拙劣的玩笑。
Expressionless, Semmelweis shuts down the clumsy joke.

空心木：不，你什么都没看到。
Verity: *chuckle* A good attempt, really. But not nearly enough to work on me.

撰稿人挺直背脊，面带自信的微笑。
The editor straightens but doesn't shed her smile.

空心木：回去忙你的工作吧，“一无所知”小姐。
Verity: Back to your work then, Little Miss Clueless.

登记工作总算告一段落。
The registration is finally done.

调查员略感到疲惫。她踱回自己的座位，翻开来时携带的文件。
Feeling a trace of fatigue, Semmelweis returns to her seat and opens her files to review.

塞梅尔维斯：穿越半岛为数不多的列车之一……
Semmelweis: One of the few trains that travels across the peninsula ...

塞梅尔维斯：来历不明的乘务组成员和闹鬼车厢……
Semmelweis: A crew with as of yet unidentified backgrounds and a haunted carriage ...

塞梅尔维斯：至于乘客……刚才已经登记了一遍，身份都能对上。
Semmelweis: All passengers on the manifest have been registered. No notable discrepancies to be found.

调查员收起文件。
She stows the papers.

一切都无可挑剔地顺理成章，仿佛所有的荒谬都有其存在的理由，但却又隐隐地透露出不对劲。
Everything falls into place too neatly, every absurdity justified, but something is off.

塞梅尔维斯：重塑之手还是没能浮出水面。看来关键还是在于那位列车长……
Semmelweis: And still no sign of the Manus. It seems the key to all this lies with the conductress.

塞梅尔维斯：她到底在隐瞒什么？
Semmelweis: What is she hiding?

塞梅尔维斯：……停车了？
Semmelweis: We're stopping?

乘客Ⅱ：你好，先生……列车怎么忽然停靠了？才刚睡下没多久呢……
Passenger II: Excuse me, sir. Why is the train stopping? I'd just gotten to sleep.

乘务员匆忙穿梭在走廊里，轻言安抚被惊醒的乘客。
The steward hurries through the corridor, calming the roused passengers.

乘务员：各位，很抱歉……列车现在是临时停车。
Train Steward: Apologies for the interruption. I'm afraid the train must come to a temporary stop.

乘务员：由于大雪天气的缘故，铁路暂时无法通行。
Train Steward: The rail ahead is impassable because of the heavy snow.

乘务员：我们正在加紧处理，请各位乘客不要惊慌。
Train Steward: The situation is being dealt with as we speak. Please stay in your rooms and remain calm.

乘务员：现在为诸位提供夜间点心，我们备有莱比锡的云雀蛋糕和东方风情的土耳其软糖，如果您还有其他需要，请随时招手示意我……
Train Steward: The dining carriage will come round to deliver nighttime desserts. We have Leipzig lark cake and Turkish delight. Should you require anything else, please let me know.

塞梅尔维斯：大雪？
Semmelweis: Snow?

调查员悄悄挑开窗帘一角。
She lifts a corner of the curtain.

窗外雪花不时飘飞，吹落在沉默的群山之间。
Snowflakes drift outside, brushed about lazily in the waning storm.

塞梅尔维斯：不错的借口，但这可不足以成为停车的理由。
Semmelweis: Snow indeed, but it hardly seems heavy enough to warrant a stop.

远在列车的另一侧，这场小小的风波并未影响到女孩的好睡眠。
On the other side of the train, the little vampire remains fast asleep.

野树莓：呼……呼……
Rubuska: *gentle breathing*

野树莓四仰八叉地躺在沙发上，呼吸分外均匀。
Rubuska lies sprawled on the sofa, breathing evenly.

她这一天经历了太多起伏，新朋友的倾听与安慰无疑成了她最好的助眠药剂。
The day's turbulence has worn her down. A new friend's comfort was the best lullaby.

艾玛：真奇怪，我还是第一次见到会在夜里睡觉的血食怪……
Aima: How odd. I've never known a vampire to sleep at night.

艾玛：……
Aima: ...

她伸出手，一点点靠近女孩的睡颜。
She reaches out, inching toward the sleeping face.

艾玛：呀！时间到了。
Aima: Oh, it's time.

乘务员摇摇头，整理了一下女孩颊边的碎发。
The stewardess shakes her head, brushing the hair from the girl's cheek.

艾玛：笑得这么开心，一定是在做什么美梦吧。不过……我得暂时离开一会儿。
Aima: Look at the smile on her face. She must be having sweet dreams. It's a shame I have to go.

她站起身，悄悄带上门。
She rises and quietly closes the door.

室外流入的光线被阴影慢慢侵蚀，直至门完全合上，房间陷入一片黑暗。
Light fades into shadow until the room is swallowed in darkness.

艾玛：晚安，小树莓。
Aima: Nighty-night, Rubi.

空气里弥漫着湿木、腐叶、雪和阴谋的气息。女孩在昏暗的树影中穿梭，时隐时现，幽灵般游走于林木之间。
The air reeks of damp wood, rot, snow, and conspiracy. A girl drifts among the trees like a phantom, fading into and then reappearing in the dark.

早早下车的列车长等候在雪地里，捻碎了一片片落在她手心的雪花。
The conductress has been waiting in the snow, crushing flakes in her palm.

告死鸟：你来迟了。遇到意外了吗？
Corvus: You're late. Did something happen?

艾玛：抱歉……我刚把那个血食怪女孩儿哄睡着。
Aima: N-No. S-Sorry, I was just making sure the vampire girl was asleep.

告死鸟：有人知道你下车了吗？
Corvus: Did anyone see you?

静悄悄的森林里，列车无声无息地停靠在铁轨上。
The train, the forest, and the winter winds conspire in gray silence.

雪仍慢慢地下着。
Snow falls calmly but steadily.

艾玛：我走得很小心，没人会发现我的。
Aima: I was careful. No one saw me.

告死鸟：很好，那走吧。
Corvus: Good.

告死鸟：别让他们久等。
Corvus: They're expecting us.

两人一前一后，朝着列车末尾走去，迅速消失在漆黑的雪夜之下。
The two move toward the rear of the train, vanishing into the heavy snow.

雪地上，另一人的脚印远远地跟在后边。
Snow prints follow, another figure trailing them.

塞梅尔维斯：果然……
Semmelweis: Just as I thought.

TMW-09 生人勿近 / Do Not Enter

告死鸟：久等了，各位。
Corvus: Apologies for the wait.

？？？：嘿，伙计们，是咱们的伊格丽卡！
???: Lower your weapons. It's Iglika!

阴影里走出几个年轻人，看清是列车长后，纷纷放下了手中的步枪。
Shadows part, young men emerge. Recognizing the conductress, they lower their rifles.

告死鸟：还是叫我告死鸟吧，我已经习惯这个称呼了。
Corvus: I prefer Corvus. It's more familiar to me.

告死鸟：都是老伙计吗？
Corvus: Are they all our people?

列车长谨慎地挨个看了看在场士兵的面容，确认没有陌生人后，才放下警备。
She checks their faces, easing only when she sees no strangers among them.

“协作者”：跟安排的一样，都是靠得住的人。
Watch Soldier: Yes, no others, just as planned.

“协作者”：鲍里斯安排的人在前面巡逻，没在这儿。
Watch Soldier: Pyrrhos's men are patrolling ahead.

告死鸟：好，我们尽快。
Corvus: Good. Finish this quickly.

告死鸟：临时停车的理由是暴雪封路，车上的人都在等，现在我们应该在“除雪”。
Corvus: The passengers believe we're clearing snow ahead of the train.

告死鸟：鲍里斯那儿也都顺利吗？
Corvus: Is Pyrrhos holding up his end?

“协作者”：没问题，就等列车进站，他会放行你们的。
Watch Soldier: Yes. He'll let you through when the train arrives.

告死鸟：很好，“货”呢？
Corvus: Good. And the "cargo"?

“协作者”：车厢里。
Watch Soldier: In the carriage over there, in the woods.

“协作者”：就在那边的林子里，等我们去把马拽过来。
Watch Soldier: We've got horses to pull it over.

“协作者”：这边走，别让列车上的人发现了……
Watch Soldier: This way. It'll keep you out of sight.

话音落下，几位年轻人便快步跑入铁轨方向的分岔路深处。
At her word, the men hurry down the forked path by the tracks.

“协作者”：嘿，跟上我们！
Watch Soldier: Come on, follow us!

列车长迈开步伐，衣角却被人轻轻拽住。
She steps forward, but her coat hem is tugged.

艾玛：列车长……我……
Aima: Conductress, I ...

告死鸟：……我知道了。
Corvus: Got it.

告死鸟：别担心，我很快回来。
Corvus: Don't worry. I'll be back.

列车长拿出新织好的围巾，笨拙地围在女孩身上，遮住了她大半张脸。
The conductress drapes a newly-made scarf over the girl's shoulders until it has all but buried her face.

艾玛：……
Aima: ...

艾玛：好软……谢谢您，列车长。
Aima: So soft. Thank you, Conductress.

告死鸟：围着它，别冻坏了。
Corvus: I don't want you to catch a chill.

“协作者”：伊格丽卡——
Watch Soldier: Iglika—

列车长拍了拍女孩的肩膀，独自走向阴影深处。
Patting her shoulder, she walks alone into the shadows.

“协作者”：一二——三！
Watch Soldier: One, two, three!

“协作者”：呼……搞定了。这可真是个大家伙！
Watch Soldier: Phew! Done. That was a heavy one.

告死鸟：很好，我们需要再清点一下里面的东西……
Corvus: Alright, time for an inventory check.

塞梅尔维斯：她加挂了一节车厢？
Semmelweis: She's added another carriage?

调查员将自己融入幽暗的树影中，把列车发生的异状都看在眼里。
Semmelweis blends into the dark shadows of the trees, examining the train.

一节新的车厢被秘密挂在了列车长车厢之后，而这一切都发生在“暴雪封路”的掩藏之下。
A new carriage is pulled up and secretly attached behind the rear cabin.

塞梅尔维斯：那些“货”是什么？枪支、弹药，还是管制药品？
Semmelweis: What's it carrying? Guns? Ammunition? Controlled substances?

塞梅尔维斯：还有跟她在一起的军人，不像是塞尔维亚军队……
Semmelweis: And those don't look like Serbian troops.

她又等了一会儿，直到其他人都慢慢离开，雪地里只剩下两人。
She waits until the soldiers disperse, leaving only two behind.

艾玛：……
Aima: ...

乘务员低着头，抓紧了手中柔软的围巾。
Aima lowers her head and clutches her scarf.

下一秒，她忽然跪倒在雪地里。
Then, she suddenly collapses to her knees.

告死鸟：艾玛？
Corvus: Aima?

雪仍然在下着。
The snow falls constantly and heavily.

二人的背影依偎在风雪中，仿佛林木中久久伫立的幽灵。
Their figures lean together in the storm, like ghosts rooted among the trees.

此时此刻，周围的一切都消失得无影无踪，世界只剩下她们。
In that moment, all else melts away. The world is only the two of them.

艾玛：对不起，我……
Aima: I'm sorry, I ...

告死鸟：嘘……我明白，我都明白……
Corvus: Shh-shh. I know. I know.

告死鸟：傻孩子，你不该靠近……
Corvus: Silly girl. Shouldn't have gotten so close.

塞梅尔维斯：她们……难道……
Semmelweis: What are they ... Could it be ...

调查员隐匿在幢幢的树影之中，皱起眉头，极尽眺望。
The investigator, hidden in shadow, frowns as she keens her eyes.

塞梅尔维斯：得再确认一下——
Semmelweis: Need to get confirmation.

？？？：别动。
???: Freeze.

？？？：举起手，背在身后。
???: Hands up where I can see them.

塞梅尔维斯：……
Semmelweis: ...

调查员举起双手。
She raises her hands.

？？？：转过来。
???: Turn around.

两个士兵歪歪扭扭地站在前方，脸色白得几乎透明，像是悬浮在夜空中的两团苍白火焰。
Two soldiers stagger before her, faces ghostly and haggard, like two white flames drifting in the night.

巡逻士兵Ⅱ：很好……别做傻事。
Patrol Soldier II: Good. Don't do anything stupid.

巡逻士兵Ⅱ：刚才你都看到什么了？
Patrol Soldier II: What did you see just now?

塞梅尔维斯：我看到……
Semmelweis: I saw ...

调查员忽然脚尖一勾，将一块石子踢中左侧士兵的膝盖。
She flicks her toe, kicking a stone into one soldier's knee.

巡逻士兵Ⅰ：唔——！！
Patrol Soldier I: Ugh!

士兵发出痛苦的喊叫声，膝盖一弯，重重跪倒在雪地上。
He cries out, buckling to the ground.

调查员迅速俯身，几乎在同一瞬间夺走他手中的枪，枪口毫不犹豫地对准另一个士兵。
She lunges, seizing his weapon in the same instant, turning it on the other.

塞梅尔维斯：现在轮到你们了……
Semmelweis: My turn now.

塞梅尔维斯：举起手，背在身后。
Semmelweis: Hands up where I can see them.

两个年轻的军人卧倒在雪地里，不省人事。
Two young soldiers lie unconscious in the snow.

塞梅尔维斯：这两个士兵看起来不太对劲。动作迟缓、步伐不稳，脸色也很奇怪……
Semmelweis: Something's wrong with these soldiers. Slow movements, unsteady steps, and their faces ... oddly pale ...

塞梅尔维斯：枪里也没有子弹，这可不像是普通的失误。
Semmelweis: Hmm, no bullets in either gun. That can't just be a mistake.

她检查着倒地士兵的状况：没有子弹的枪支、没有刻字的名牌，以及摔落在地的一件令她在意的小玩意儿。
She checks their gear: empty rifles, unmarked tags, and a trinket that draws her eye.

塞梅尔维斯：……！
Semmelweis: ...!

塞梅尔维斯：上次没来得及看清，但从形制大小来看，和列车长递交给那些驻军的东西应该是同一个。
Semmelweis: Same shape and size. This looks to be the item the conductress gave that soldier at the station earlier.

塞梅尔维斯：重塑之手……找了这么长时间，终于浮出水面了。
Semmelweis: Manus Vindictae. Finally, you rear your head.

调查员轻轻摩挲着徽章上熟悉的纹样，拿出口袋里的通讯器，摁下按钮。
She runs her fingers over the familiar symbol, then pulls her communicator from her coat and presses the button.

塞梅尔维斯：塞梅尔维斯，任务编号0073-MV。
Semmelweis: Investigator Semmelweis to Foundation, mission number 0073-MV.

基金会对接员：请讲，调查员。
Foundation Operator: Go ahead, Investigator.

塞梅尔维斯：目前已获取重要线索：贝尔格莱德附近车站的巡逻士兵身上携带了重塑之手的徽章。
Semmelweis: Progress update: I've found a Manus Vindictae insignia on a soldier at a station near Belgrade.

塞梅尔维斯：此外，“多瑙黎明号”列车长行为异常，与当地士兵有可疑交易。她以“暴雪封路”为由，在列车上秘密加挂了一节车厢。
Semmelweis: The conductress of the "Danube Dawn" has undertaken suspicious dealings with these soldiers, stopping the train on the pretext of "the railway being blocked by the snow" in order to secretly add an additional carriage.

塞梅尔维斯：我怀疑列车长已和重塑之手合作。加挂车厢里运送的货物，或许和此次任务目标——血食怪有关。
Semmelweis: I now have reason to believe that the conductress is collaborating with Manus Vindictae. Whatever's in that carriage may be related to our blood-sucking target.

塞梅尔维斯：以及……七十七分队成员已确认失联。
Semmelweis: One more thing: I've lost contact with all members of Squad 77.

基金会对接员：收到，已获悉0073-MV任务进度，将持续追踪七十七分队成员下落。
请继续推进任务，调查员。
Foundation Operator: Mission 0073-MV report received. We will continue our search for Squad 77. Please proceed with your mission, Investigator.

报告完毕，调查员干脆利落地关闭了通讯器。
Report finished, she snaps the device shut.

她望向头顶灰蒙蒙的天空。雪渐渐小了。
She looks up at the dark sky. The storm is easing.

塞梅尔维斯：已经在这里停留了太久。再磨蹭下去，会让某些人起疑心的。
Semmelweis: Been out here a while. Any longer and I might start to raise suspicion.

塞梅尔维斯：该回去了。
Semmelweis: Time to head back.

时间一分一秒流逝。
Time passes slowly.

乘客们陆续从睡梦中醒来，走出各自的卧铺车厢，低声交头接耳。
A few passengers stir awake with the stop; some step out of their cabins, whispering in the darkness.

乘务员：大家不必担心……列车马上就要发车了，不久就将抵达边境检查站！
Train Steward: All passengers, please remain in your rooms. The train is about to depart, and we will reach the border checkpoint soon!

穿行过一节又一节车厢，乘务员尽职尽责地安抚着因停车而有些躁动的乘客们。
The steward moves between cars, calming their unease.

他行至两节车厢间，却发现车门敞开，风掠着雪花吹进来。
Between two cars, he sees one door ajar, wind blowing snow inside.

乘务员：嗯？车门怎么开着？
Train Steward: Hm? Why is the door open?

乘务员：门底下好像有什么痕迹……
Train Steward: Wait a minute, there's something underneath.

生病的乘客：咳……咳咳……
Unwell Passenger: *coughing*

一名乘客倚靠在一旁，接连的咳嗽声拉回了乘务员的注意力。
A passenger leans there, coughing hard, drawing the attention of the steward.

生病的乘客：嗬……请问……我们什么时候能出发？
Unwell Passenger: *cough* Excuse me, when is the train leaving?

乘务员：哦，抱歉！再过五分钟，不……十分钟，列车就能再次启动了。
Train Steward: Oh! Apologies, sir. In about five, no, ten minutes.

生病的乘客：好……
Unwell Passenger: Okay.

他垂下头，不再言语。
He lowers his head with dejection.

待乘务员关上车门离去后，眼珠在他的眼眶转动，嘴唇蠕动着发出喉咙里的一阵怪响。
When the steward leaves, his eyes roll, lips twitching with a guttural rasp.

“咔……咔咔——”
*groan*

沉闷的轰鸣声一阵阵响起，隐去了车内的谈话声、喧闹声以及其他一切不合时宜的声响。
Low rumbles drown voices, shouts, any stray sound in the train.

“多瑙黎明号”满载着乘客，再度于风雪中启动。
The "Danube Dawn" rolls on into the storm, laden with passengers.

TMW-10 墓园里 / Among the Dead

我总是会做同样的梦。梦里的人从不变老，阳光永不消融。
I always have the same dream, a dream where time stands still. People never grow old, and the sunshine never fades.

在梦里，我总能听见母亲的声音。
Because there, I can hear Mама's voice again.

母亲：你的头发已经这么长啦，野树莓。
Mother: My, look how long your hair has grown, Rubuska.

母亲：快坐起来，让我用木梳帮你梳顺……你的头发像我，但小尼古拉的头发像爸爸，总是卷到发根，梳都梳不开……
Mother: Sit up for a moment so I can comb it for you. My hair was just like yours when I was a girl. I do worry when I comb Nikola's, though. His hair's like your father's, all curly at the root.

小野树莓：好嘛，好嘛，妈妈！你一边梳，一边继续给我讲吧……“他们在血色的月光下复生……”
Young Rubuska: Come on, Mама, please keep telling the story! "In the light of the blood moon, they rise ..."

母亲：“他们在血色的月光下复生，永远游走在黑夜的阴影里……”
Mother: "In the light of the blood moon, they rise and stride under the veil of night."

母亲：“他们的世界是自由的，没有死亡，也没有恐惧……”
Mother: "Freely, they live, without fear of death."

母亲：“只需饮下鲜血，他们便将永世长存。”
Mother: "For through blood they live forevermore."

小野树莓：饮下鲜血，永世长存……
Young Rubuska: Through blood they live ...

小野树莓：真不错！那我呢，妈妈，我呢！
Young Rubuska: Amazing! What about me, Mама? What about me?

母亲：你啊……你是我们最最亲爱的野树莓，是家族里最年幼的血食怪之一。
Mother: You, well, you are our dearest Rubuska, one of the youngest vampires in the family.

母亲：春去秋来，你已在沉眠中度过了两百一十四年零四个月两天。
Mother: Seasons changed, years passed, and you've spent 214 years, four months, and two days in a deep, deep sleep.

母亲：如今，绝望的人们正在战火与硝烟中呻吟。为此他们恳请你，睁开血红的双眼，再度回到人间……
Mother: Now, the people suffering from the war cry out, "Rubuska! Awaken! Open up your scarlet eyes and help us!"

小野树莓：呼……嗯？那是……鲜血的味道……
Young Rubuska: Hmm, ah! Is that blood I smell?

小野树莓：很好，血食怪野树莓终于从长长的梦里苏醒了！
Young Rubuska: Now, the great vampire Rubuska has awoken from her endless sleep.

小野树莓：难道有人欺负我的家人？妈妈别怕，我会狠狠地咬住那些坏人，吸他们的血——
Young Rubuska: Does anyone dare hurt my family? Never fear, Mама. Rubuska's here to bite their necks and suck their blood.

母亲：呵呵，傻孩子。
Mother: Hah hah, you silly thing.

母亲：没事的。你忘了吗？身为血食怪的亲族，我们是无惧……
Mother: Have you forgotten? As vampires, we're not afraid of anything. Not even ...

母亲：死亡的……
Mother: ... death ...

母亲：跑！野树莓，快跑——！
Mother: Run, Buska, RUN!

小野树莓：妈妈……不，我不走……
Young Rubuska: Mама! No, no, I, no, no ...

母亲：跑啊——野树莓！
Mother: Buska, RUN!

枪声已经远去，又一个村子在身后燃烧。
I ran and ran, away from the gunshots, away from another burning village.

我逃进了山林，故乡的群山保护了我，然后是墓地。
I ran into the mountains. They protected me—hid my escape. Then I went to the cemetery.

小野树莓：没人追过来，哈啊，哈啊……
Young Rubuska: No, no one's following.

小野树莓：他们找不到我了……哈哈……
Young Rubuska: They can't find me anymore, hahaha.

我找到了一口旧棺材，没人会在乎它，没人会想起它。它就被丢在那里，世界把它遗弃了。
I found an old coffin, cast aside, forgotten, just there, abandoned by the whole world.

我缩在里头，日夜与腐肉、蠕虫和湿润的青苔为伴。
I huddled up inside it, and I lived there. Lived with the worms.

小野树莓：是他们的气味……
Young Rubuska: It smells like them.

小野树莓：是“家人”的气味。
Young Rubuska: Like my "family."

母亲曾说，在这片土地上，逝者不会真正死去。
Mама once said that, in this land, the dead never truly die.

他们的肉体沉入泥土，鲜血渗透进地下，与这片土地的根脉融为一体……
She said that our bodies merged with the earth, our blood seeping into the dirt and nourishing the tangled roots of the trees.

悄悄联结，互相缠绕，永远与世界相联。
And ever so quietly, we'd day by day become one with the world.

于是我不再害怕，也不再挣扎。我安稳地闭上眼，嗅着那股湿气与腐臭，心里却感到很温暖。
So, I wasn't afraid—didn't struggle anymore. I closed my eyes—let the smell wash over me—and a warmth grew in my heart.

小野树莓：爸爸……妈妈……
Young Rubuska: Dad ... Mама ...

此刻，我与他们相依相伴。
We were together again.

相依，相伴……
Together again.

相依，相伴……
Together again, together again.

野树莓：——！
Rubuska: ...!

她从梦中惊醒。
She awakens from a dream.

野树莓：呼……呼……是、是梦……
Rubuska: *panting* J-Just a dream.

野树莓：原来是梦……
Rubuska: *deep breath* Just a dream.

女孩深吸一口气，将郁结的情绪通通咽下肚。
Rubuska takes a deep breath, swallowing her tangled emotions.

环顾四周，车厢内空无一人。
She looks around. The room is empty.

野树莓：已经不记得上次睡安稳觉是什么时候了……
Rubuska: Can't remember the last time I had a good night's sleep.

野树莓：原来已经这个时候了。这样看来……马上就能到边境检查站了！
Rubuska: Huh, I must have slept longer than I thought. Oh, but that means we'll be getting to the checkpoint soon.

野树莓：艾玛也不见踪影……噢！难道说，我已经能离开了吗？
Rubuska: Aima's gone too. Wait. That means I've got a chance to get out of here.

女孩小心翼翼地再次打开门锁，探出头迅速扫视四周，像一只警觉的猫。
She takes no time to pick the lock again, peeking out like a wary cat.

野树莓：很好，外面也没有人！
Rubuska: Yes! No one outside, either.

正欲出门，女孩突然看见了脏污的双手，与身着的漂亮裙子格格不入。
But before she steps out, she notices her dirty hands, a poor contrast with her fine new dress.

它在一路摸爬滚打中沾满了灰尘，女孩想扯下衣袖盖住，却又怕弄脏了洁净的新衣。
Covered in dust from all her scrambling, she tries to pull down her sleeve, then hesitates, afraid to stain the fine fabric.

野树莓：……还是换回原来的衣服吧。
Rubuska: Oh, I'd better change.

野树莓：得把它们都放好……然后……
Rubuska: Just have to put this all back, and ...

洁净的衣裙被整齐叠放在沙发一角。犹豫了一会儿，女孩又在旁边放上了自己的帽子。
Her new clothes are left folded on the sofa. After a pause, she sets her hat beside them.

野树莓：这是我全身上下最贵的东西了……送给你作为礼物吧。
Rubuska: This is the most expensive thing I own. Take it as my gift.

野树莓：再见啦，“小公主”。
Rubuska: Bye-bye, princess.

年幼的血食怪悄悄地行走在车厢之间。
The young vampire slips through the carriages.

乘客们都已熟睡，沉寂的黑夜既让人畅快，却也让人失落。
Most passengers remain asleep. The night is freeing, yet oddly lonely.

野树莓：好安静……
Rubuska: Hmm. Quiet.

野树莓：既然大家都不在，那我只能自己找点乐子咯！
Rubuska: Nobody's around now. Then I can have some fun by myself.

她拿起笛子，用音符为自己作伴。
She lifts her flute, letting notes keep her company.

野树莓：就像以前一样……
Rubuska: Just like the old days.

她轻轻“吹”了一个音符，不惊扰任何沉入梦乡的乘客。
A soft tone escapes, low and sweet.

野树莓：很好……从现在开始，这里是1号车厢。
Rubuska: Right, here I am in carriage one.

野树莓：这里是2号……
Rubuska: Carriage number two.

一个音符落下，又一个音符升起。
One note falls, another rises.

女孩轻盈地穿梭在车厢内，像一阵灵动的风。
She drifts lightly through the carriage like a passing breeze.

野树莓：这是11号……
Rubuska: Eleven ...

野树莓：嗯……？
Rubuska: Huh?

野树莓：算上守车和休息室的话，总共应该是12节车厢不是吗？
Rubuska: Shouldn't there be twelve carriages? Ten for passengers, plus the brake van and the staff compartment. Yeah.

野树莓：这里什么时候……多了一节车厢？
Rubuska: Then how did this extra carriage get here?

风雪吹开，未曾见过的车厢在黑暗中随列车颠簸。
A new carriage, one she's never seen before, rattles in the dark.

车厢连着车厢，似乎永远没有尽头。
But the train stretches long, and in the night it almost feels endless.

空心木：不错，吹得很深情。我几乎都要为那支沉默的木笛鼓掌了。
Verity: Hmm. What a pretty song. I could almost applaud.

声音冷不丁从角落的阴影中传出。
A voice cuts coldly from the shadows.

野树莓：咦，是之前见过的……
Rubuska: Oh, you're that lady from before.

野树莓：我在数车厢一共有多少节。这是计数用的。
Rubuska: I'm counting how many carriages there are. This helps me with it.

空心木：很有趣。这是你家乡的游戏吗？
Verity: An interesting little game. From your hometown, I presume?

女孩摇了摇头。
She shakes her head.

野树莓：是我自己发明的。
Rubuska: No, I came up with it myself.

野树莓：我的家乡……很大，大得漫无边际，就像海一样。
Rubuska: My hometown's big, you see—so big you couldn't even imagine it.

翻过一座山，后面又是一座山。走过一条河，眼前还横着另一条河。
Climb one mountain, and another rises. Cross one river, and another follows.

天空绵延着无边无际的灰色，路远得仿佛没有尽头。
The sky stretches endless and gray, a road without end.

野树莓：不过，我有妈妈留给我的笛子。
Rubuska: Lucky for me, my mother gave me this kaval.

野树莓：我给所有的大山、小河都放上一个独属于它们的音符，这样一来……
Rubuska: So, I used it to name every mountain and river by giving them each their own note.

她握紧手中的笛子。
She grips her flute with pride.

野树莓：我就不会再迷路了！
Rubuska: And now I never get lost!

空心木：你确定吗？
Verity: Are you certain?

撰稿人从沙沙的记录声中抬起头，目光中透露出一丝兴致。
The editor looks up from her scratchy notes, her eyes alight with interest.

空心木：听说这里的列车可是会“增殖”的，哪怕你吹出一整首巴赫B小调复调回旋曲也没用。
Verity: I've heard the carriages on this train can multiply. Even if you played the entirety of Bach's Mass in B Minor, you'd never count them all.

空心木：不信的话，你可以继续往前走。
Verity: Go ahead if you don't believe me. You'll see soon enough.

她露出笑容。
Verity offers a wistful smile.

野树莓：我……？
Rubuska: Oh. What?

女孩看向前方。
She looks down the corridor.

车厢随列车行进的节奏慵懒地左右晃动着，向她发出无声的邀约。
The carriage sways lazily, as if beckoning her forward.

月光倾泻而下，仿佛为它披上了一层苍白而冰冷的裹尸布，将一切秘密掩埋其中。
Moonlight peeks through the clouds, pale and cold, shrouding the scene like a white burial sheet, hiding all secrets beneath it.

他们看见了那节本不该存在的车厢，无数血红的眼睛在尽头的黑暗中交替明灭。
And there, in a carriage that never was, in that place that shouldn't even have existed, blood-red eyes blinked in the darkness.

鲜血遍地流淌，沉睡于黑夜中的怪物们悄然苏醒，静静吞咽那甘甜的热血。
And the blood of those sorry passengers trickled, sweet and warm, into the throats of the red-eyed monsters.

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

野树莓：呃……姐姐，我觉得咱俩最好结个伴……
Rubuska: Uh, ma'am, I think we'd better stick together.

她害怕地退后一步，回过身，却发现背后早已空无一人。
She steps back in fear, turning to find nothing there.

只剩下老旧的木门独自晃悠，吱呀——吱呀——
Just an old iron door, swaying by itself, its hinges groaning, creak ... creak ...

野树莓：姐姐……？
Rubuska: Ma'am?

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

女孩不得不独自面对眼前的黑暗。
The girl has no choice but to face the darkness before her.

野树莓：我、我可是血食怪野树莓！血食怪什么都不会怕的……
Rubuska: C-Come on now. You're Rubuska! The blood-sucking vampire! You're not scared of ... *tremble* ... anything.

女孩深吸一口气，轻轻一跃便跳了过去。
She takes a deep breath and takes a brave leap.

沉重的铜锁扣住了车厢前门，在月光下闪着冰冷的微光。
A heavy copper lock clamps the front door of the carriage, glinting coldly under the moonlight.

野树莓：怎么又锁住了……
Rubuska: Oh. Locked again?

野树莓：好，那我就再开一次！
Rubuska: Fine, then I'll just unlock this one too.

野树莓：开了……！
Rubuska: Open sesame!

只要向前一推，便能进入车厢。
Just one push, and she could slip inside.

野树莓停下了动作。她屏住呼吸，贴近车门，听见里面正隐隐传来呻吟与哭声。
Rubuska freezes. Holding her breath, she presses against the door, catching faint sounds from within.

“在夜里醒来的乘客们，先是听见哭声，然后听见哀嚎。”
"On one such night, a group of passengers awoke to the sound of crying. They followed it. Then the crying turned to bawling, and the bawling to wailing, until they reached it—"

“而当他们朝声音的来源寻觅而去时……”
"A door that wasn't there before."

女孩心中没来由升起一丝恐惧。她转过身去想要离开，然而疾风刮过，车厢门被猛地推开。
Fear creeps over her. She turns to leave when a sharp gust throws the door wide open.

野树莓：……！
Rubuska: ...!

车门那老旧的呻吟声足以唤醒任何沉睡的古老存在。
The ancient groan of the door could wake anyone—or anything—long asleep.

她极慢、极缓地抬起头，直视眼前的黑暗——
Slowly, she lifts her head to face the darkness.

野树莓：啊啊……！
Rubuska: Ahh!

一双双眼睛自黑暗中现出，仿佛黑夜中群聚的苍白鬼火。
Eyes flicker in the dark, like ghostly flames gathering in the night.

野树莓：唔——！！
Rubuska: Ugh, ahh! Mmff.

还未来得及发出尖叫，下一秒，女孩被捂住嘴，拖入深不见底的黑暗。
Before she can scream, a hand clamps her mouth, dragging her into the eclipsing shadows.

TMW-11 十三号车厢 / Carriage No. 13

野树莓：唔唔——放开姆！
Rubuska: *muffled* Mmff. Get off me!

沉重的声音：很好，我摁住她了！大蒜准备好了吗？木桩和盐呢？
Deep Voice: Alright, she's down! Bring the garlic, stake, and salt!

数只沉重的大手死死捂住野树莓的脸，鼻尖传来煤炭的烟熏味，混合着大蒜与泥土的臭气，令人几欲晕厥。
Heavy hands cover her face, coal smoke, garlic, and earth choking her breath until she nearly faints.

野树莓：好臭……姆咬！
Rubuska: Ugh! What're you ... *chomp*

着急的声音：当心，雅科夫！别真被她咬了！
Urgent Voice: Careful, Yakov! Don't let her bite you!

手终于松开了，女孩一骨碌从地上爬起。
Finally, the grip loosens. She scrambles to her feet.

视线逐渐适应了眼前的黑暗。
Her eyes adjust to the dark.

没有血食怪，也没蝙蝠与无尽的长廊，这只是一节寻常的、昏暗而破旧的车厢。
No vampires, no bats, no endless corridors, just an ordinary, if grim, old carriage.

数十个脏兮兮的“乘客”挤在一起。他们衣衫破旧，神色紧张，几乎人人都全副武装：铁棍、锅铲，甚至还有大蒜和盐……
Dozens of filthy "passengers" crowd together, ragged and tense, clutching makeshift weapons: iron rods, pans, even garlic and salt.

雅科夫：原来是个孩子。你……是血食怪吗？
Yakov: Wait, it's just a kid. You're not a vampire, are you, young lady?

野树莓：我可是穿刺公德古拉的末代后裔，当然是血统纯正的血食怪！
Rubuska: Course I am! You're looking at the heir of Dracula the Impaler himself!

乘客们又纷纷举起手中放下的“武器”。
They raise their "weapons" once more.

野树莓：等一下！咳咳，你们应该感到庆幸，本血食怪现在还不算太饿……
Rubuska: Whoa, whoa, whoa! Let's not be too hasty. This vampire's already got a full belly.

野树莓：暂时。
Rubuska: For now.

雅科夫：既然不是来“觅食”的，为什么要撬开车门？你想要什么？
Yakov: Then tell us why you broke in here. And don't go telling lies.

野树莓：我……
Rubuska: I …

女孩心虚地试图后退半步，却被冰冷的铁门堵住了退路。
Rubuska tries to step back, but the cold iron door blocks her retreat.

“偷渡”的乘客：算了，雅科夫。她看起来没有恶意。
Stowaway Passenger: Cut her some slack, Yakov. I don't think she meant any harm.

附近忽然传来女人的劝告声。
A woman's voice calls out, gentle but firm.

雅科夫：哼。你总在关键时刻心软，拉伊哈。
Yakov: Hmph. Reyhan, every time we try to act tough, you go soft on us.

拉伊哈：别忘了我们现在的处境。真闹出动静，咱们一个都跑不了。
Reyhan: Maybe so, but what other option do we have? If anyone hears us and comes looking, we're done for.

野树莓：没、没错！我马上就走。放心，我什么也没看到……
Rubuska: Sh-She's right. Let me go, and I won't say a word. I-I didn't see a thing, promise.

？？？：唔……咳咳……
???: Ugh ... *cough*

一声微弱的呻吟自女人怀中传来。野树莓下意识放缓了离开的动作。
A child whimpers in her arms, and Rubuska hesitates.

女人将孩子抱得更紧了一些，轻声安抚。
The woman hugs him closer, soothing him.

拉伊哈：别害怕，小伊凡。我们都看着她呢。
Reyhan: It's alright, Ivanushka. No need to be afraid. We've got our eyes on her.

小伊凡：我不怕血食怪，姐姐。她看上去一点儿也不吓人，不像那些炮弹……
Ivanushka: I'm not afraid. She isn't half as scary as those whizz-bangs.

男孩乖巧地靠在女人身边，左边的袖管空荡荡的，随列车的行进轻轻晃动。
The boy leans against the woman, one sleeve hanging empty.

小伊凡：姐姐……我们会平安抵达布达佩斯吗？
Ivanushka: How much longer will we be stuck here, Rey? Will we really go to Budapest?

拉伊哈低下头，温柔地摸了摸他毛茸茸的头发。
Reyhan lowers her head, stroking his hair softly.

拉伊哈：会的，我的小天使。
Reyhan: Of course we will, little guy.

野树莓：原来你们也是……
Rubuska: Budapest? Then, you're also …

无需多言，眼前的景象早已说尽了一切。
No words are needed. The scene says it all.

那是太过熟悉的气息，也是她不断试图逃离的、总是如影随形的噩梦——
That scent, too familiar. The nightmare returns, always chasing her ...

小野树莓：小尼古拉，快醒醒……
Young Rubuska: Kolyo *sniffle* Kolyo, don't fall asleep, okay?

枪声仍未远去，又一个村子在她身后燃烧。女孩将亲人揽在怀里，不忍看他血肉模糊的躯干。
Gunfire still echoes. A village burns behind her. She clutches her brother, unable to look back at the ruins.

小尼古拉：姐姐……我，好像感觉不到自己的腿了……
Kolyo: Buska, I can't feel my legs.

小野树莓：这只是暂时的。听着，你会没事的……有我在……
Young Rubuska: They're just a bit numb. It'll pass. You'll be fine. *sniff* I'll get us out of here.

火光划破天幕，又一枚炮弹在他们头顶爆炸。
Flames tear across the sky. A shell bursts overhead.

小野树莓：——！！
Young Rubuska: ...!

小尼古拉：我……我知道，他们把我的腿偷走了……
Kolyo: I think my legs are gone.

Kolyo: It-It hurts, Buska. It-It hurts so bad. I can't—

Young Rubuska: Oh. You'll be fine, Kolyo, alright? Your big sister's here. You're safe.

小野树莓：就像大人们说过的，明天会更好……
Young Rubuska: You'll feel better tomorrow. You'll be better.

Rubuska: ...

Ivanushka: Um, Ms. Vampire, what happened to your eyes? They've gone all red and watery, like a white rabbit's.

野树莓：呃……血食怪回想起开心的事情，眼睛就会像这样……
Rubuska: Huh? Oh, it's nothing. Happens every time I think of a happy memory. It's a vampire thing.

野树莓：嗯？
Rubuska: Hm?

靠近车门的双耳捕捉到了一丝微妙的动静。
She hears a faint sound by the door.

一步、两步……那是由远及近的、安静而耐心的脚步声。
Step by step, quiet and patient.

雅科夫：发生什么了吗？
Yakov: What is it?

女孩摆摆手，示意大伙儿安静下来，随即侧耳贴上车厢门。
Rubuska signals the others to hush then presses her ear to the door.

野树莓：什么都没听见……难道我搞错了？
Rubuska: Strange, I don't hear anything now. Was it just my imagination?

她低下头，见到门缝中隐约透入一抹昏黄的光晕。
She lowers her head and sees a dim yellow glow seeping through the crack.

一个黑影恰巧挡在光晕中间的位置，随列车的摆动一齐轻轻晃荡着。
A shadow blocks the light, swaying with the train.

野树莓：——！！
Rubuska: ...!

她下意识想要后退，转身却撞上了一双无助的眼睛。
She turns in panic but meets the gaze of a helpless boy.

小伊凡：又有人要来抓走我们了吗……？
Ivanushka: Are the bad men coming for us again?

小伊凡：我不想……
Ivanushka: I don't want to go with them.

男孩无助地望向女孩。他的眼睛很蓝，像是晴空的颜色。
His blue eyes look almost clear in the darkness.

曾经在枪声中，有另一个男孩也用这样的眼神望着她。
Once before, in a world of ash and gunfire, another boy had looked at her the same way.

野树莓：小尼古拉……
Rubuska: Kolyo …

她深吸一口气，许下庄重的诺言。
She draws a deep breath, making a solemn vow.

野树莓：别害怕，我可是强大的血食怪……不会有问题的。
Rubuska: … You're not going anywhere. I swear it on my honor as a vampire.

野树莓：交给我吧，我会同你们一起，我们一起去布达佩斯。
Rubuska: Just leave it to me. I'll get you all to Budapest, safe and sound.

女孩坚定地回过头去，面对着车厢门。
Turning back, she faces the door.

野树莓：嘘……
Rubuska: Now, keep quiet.

所有人屏息而待。
They hold their breath.

数十道目光交织起一张无形的大网，牢牢支撑起女孩脆弱的脊背，也阻绝了她全部的后路。
Dozens of eyes weave a net around her, holding her spine steady, sealing every path of retreat.

野树莓：不管你是谁……
Rubuska: Whoever you are …

她颤抖着张开双臂，外套随之扬起，在夜色中鼓荡开来，如同蝙蝠张开巨大的双翼。
She spreads her arms, coat flaring wide, like a bat unfurling its wings in the night.

野树莓：来吧……哈！我可不会让你伤害大伙儿！
Rubuska: Sh-Show yourself! But don't think I'll let you touch a hair on their heads!

一场毫无悬念的战斗，然而战败者却并不轻言放弃。
An effortless battle, yet the defeated refuses to yield.

？？？：唔！快放手……
???: Oh! That's quite enough!

Rubuska: Huh? What are you doing here?

听见熟悉的声音喊出自己的名字，女孩愣愣地松开双手。
Hearing her name called in that familiar voice, the girl slackens her grip.

塞梅尔维斯：这话应该我来问。
Semmelweis: Funny, I had intended to ask you the same thing.

明黄的光柱滑过一张张疲惫而困顿的面容。
The yellow beam falls across weary, half-wild faces.

没有人吱声。眼前这位身手不凡的调查员显然吓坏了不少乘客。
No one speaks. Her speed and skill intimidating the onlookers.

塞梅尔维斯：普通的难民？

调查员思索了一瞬，再度开口。
She pauses for a moment, then speaks again.

塞梅尔维斯：是列车长放你们上来的吗？别急着否认，我看到他们加挂了车厢。

塞梅尔维斯：你们的目的是什么？
Semmelweis: Why are you on this train?

……
...

车厢内一片沉默，人们的目光警惕而不安。调查员知道，她必须亮出更加诚恳的态度，才能打破这堵无形的墙。
Silence. Eyes filled with unease and suspicion fix on her. She knows only sincerity will break through the wall between them.

塞梅尔维斯：我不是边境巡逻，也不是铁路稽察。
Semmelweis: Just listen please, I don't work for the border patrol, the army, nor the railway.

塞梅尔维斯：如果你们只是为了逃离战争、饥荒或者疾病，那我完全理解——这只是一种求生的本能，任何人在这样的境况下都会作出类似的抉择。
Semmelweis: If it's war, famine, or death you're running from, well, who could blame you? In times like these, anyone would do the same.

塞梅尔维斯：我来这里，是为了找一个……血食怪。如果你们与它无关，那我们之间就没有任何问题。
Semmelweis: My business here is with a vampire. If you don't have anything to do with one, then your purpose here is of no concern to me.

乘客们：血食怪？
Stowaways: A vampire?

Rubuska: Could she mean me? Did you come here looking for me?

塞梅尔维斯：是除她以外的另一个血食怪。一开始我还以为它就在这节车厢里，现在看来，我的调查方向似乎出现了一些偏差。
Semmelweis: I can see what you're all thinking, but it's not her. I thought perhaps it could be hiding in this carriage, but it appears I was wrong.

野树莓：哦……
Rubuska: Oh ...

女孩点点头，说不出是庆幸抑或失落。

Stowaway I: So the stories are true. Good thing we came prepared!

“偷渡”的乘客Ⅱ：血食怪……它会找到我们吗？
Stowaway II: That vampire … It won't find us, will it?

人们担忧地交头接耳起来。忧虑与不安在车厢内进一步扩散。

Semmelweis: Look, I'm willing to help you, but only if you give me some information about yourselves. After all, trust is a two-way street, right?

雅科夫：……我明白了。
Yakov: I understand.

雅科夫环视车内一张张憔悴的面容，低声叹了一口气。
Yakov surveys the faces, sighing under his breath.

雅科夫：我们都是从各个地方逃难来的。有人提供了渠道，我们接受，仅此而已。

雅科夫：给的指示也很简单：就在贝尔格莱德车站前面不远，有趟列车会停下来。

雅科夫：至于那个列车长……我们交流不多。她只说出境后有人会接应我们，带我们去治疗，然后在布达佩斯开启新生活。
Yakov: As for the conductress ... She didn't speak much. She said there'd be people on the other side, people who'd feed us, give us medicine, help us start a new life in Budapest.

雅科夫：就这么简单。
Yakov: That's the whole of it.

塞梅尔维斯：带人偷渡可是重罪，要是被当局发现……她有向你们提任何条件吗？
Semmelweis: She's taking a huge risk for you. Smuggling you across the border could put her behind bars. She asked for a fair price, I assume?

乘客们摇了摇头。
The passengers shake their heads.

拉伊哈：只叫我们管住嘴，别让不相干的人知道了。
Reyhan: No, nothing. Only that we keep quiet and never speak a word about it to anyone who doesn't need to know.

野树莓：哇……听上去简直就是做好事不留名的大英雄。
Rubuska: Whoa ... I never would've figured her for something like that.

塞梅尔维斯：……
Semmelweis: ...

塞梅尔维斯：（可她身上带着重塑之手的徽章，甚至把它交给了那些士兵。）

塞梅尔维斯：（还有那些失踪的调查员……）
Semmelweis: And I can't forget that the rest of my squad has vanished without a trace.

调查员望向窗外。雪还在下，没有要停的意思。
Semmelweis takes a glance outside—an unyielding screen of white snow.

她拿出怀表，确认了一下时间。
She checks her watch.

塞梅尔维斯：根据行进的时间来看，我们应该快抵达检查站了。
Semmelweis: We'll be reaching the checkpoint any minute now.

离终点越近，意味着留给她的时间便越少。
Their time is short.

似乎是为了回应调查员的精准推算，话音刚落，列车果真缓缓停了下来。
As if to confirm her calculation, the train begins to slow.

雅科夫：车停了？
Yakov: We're stopping again. What's going on?

雅科夫凑近车门，从缝隙中小心翼翼地看向外面。不一会儿，他的眼睛忽然亮了起来。
Yakov presses close to the door, peeking through the crack. His eyes suddenly brighten.

雅科夫：果然……是边境检查站！
Yakov: You're right. It's the border checkpoint!

雅科夫：好消息，朋友们——我们明早就能出境了！
Yakov: Good news, folks—by tomorrow, we'll be out of the country!

TMW-12 凉水泉 / Kreynero

列车缓缓驶入检查站。
The train glides into a soft brake at the checkpoint.

蒸汽机停止运转，庞大的钢铁巨兽仿佛入睡一般，静静停靠在铁轨上。
The steel beast breathes out a final belch of dark smoke before it stops.

边防士兵Ⅰ：“多瑙黎明号”……
Border Checkpoint Soldier I: The "Danube Dawn" ...

边防士兵Ⅰ：维也纳-潘诺尼亚运输公司所有，登记车厢……十二节。
Border Checkpoint Soldier I: Operated by Vienna-Pannonian Railways, 12 carriages.

边防士兵Ⅰ：于一九一二年十一月三十日抵达尼卡边境检查站。
Border Checkpoint Soldier I: Date of arrival: November 30th, 1912. Location: Nika Border Checkpoint.

边防士兵Ⅰ：登记成员，二百……五十……五十……
Border Checkpoint Soldier I: Persons on board ... 250 ... 50 ...

声音弱了下来，反复打着转，仿佛被困在了数字的囚笼里。
The sound grows faint, looping over and over, as if trapped in a prison of numbers.

告死鸟：先生？
Corvus: Sir?

列车长靠近一步。士兵的面容在月光下显得格外苍白，像是刚从一场漫长的病痛中康复。
The conductress steps forward. The soldier's face, pale as moonlight, looks freshly recovered from a long illness.

边防士兵Ⅰ：噢……！我们会尽快查验放行。
Border Checkpoint Soldier I: Oh, er, just the usual checks. We'll have you on your way shortly.

边防士兵Ⅰ：尼卡检查站向您致敬，列车长。

Border Checkpoint Soldier I: Ma'am, he ...

His eyes drift before finally finding focus.

Border Checkpoint Soldier I: He's expecting you. Said you'd know where to find him.

Aima: Oh, Uncle Pyrrhos. Now I have all five of them. Thank you ever so much!

Corvus: You look exhausted. Has there been trouble?

Pyrrhos: Do I? Perhaps I am a little worse for wear. Dealing with border patrol is always a pain. You know how it is.

他一边说着，眼角的余光不动声色地掠过乘务员。

艾玛：哦……我还得去擦洗一下车窗，你们请继续……
Aima: Oh, yes. I just remembered I still have to clean the windows on the dining car. Thank you again, Uncle Pyrrhos.

艾玛会意地收起新玩具，转身离开。

Pyrrhos: There are eyes on us, and not just some casual suspicion. I believe they may be professionals.

Pyrrhos: I just received word that two of my men were knocked out while on patrol—somehow without alerting anyone. Whoever did it was well trained.

Corvus: I'll handle it.

鲍里斯：看来你见过他们的人了。让我猜猜……现在就在你的车上，对吗？
Pyrrhos: Oh, Iglika. *tut* You've met them already, haven't you? They're on your train as we speak.

鲍里斯：不然我们的人怎么会在森林里倒下。那地方方圆十英里连只兔子都没有，只可能是从你车上下来的人。
Pyrrhos: How else could my men have been ambushed in such an isolated location? You're harboring a snake, my friend, whether you know it or not.

告死鸟：她的目的并非列车本身，你不用担心我车上的人。我说过了——我会处理好一切。
Corvus: She's not after the cargo. As for the assault, I will handle it.

告死鸟：在这个关键节点，我不希望任何事情影响“多瑙黎明号”顺利到达布达佩斯。
Corvus: I won't allow anything to jeopardize the mission. This train must reach Budapest.

列车长摆摆手，示意话题到此终结。
She dismisses his concern with a sharp wave.

鲍里斯：……真叫人怀念啊。
Pyrrhos: *chuckle* Ah, makes me miss it.

鲍里斯：当初你也是像这样，力排众议让我留在了组织里。
Pyrrhos: I'll never forget the day you stood up for me. It's thanks to you that they even allowed me to stay with the guerrilla unit.

军官眯起眼，思绪仿佛又回到了那个遥远的夏天。
The officer narrows his eyes, mind slipping back to a faraway summer.

鲍里斯：那时我们的想法很简单。为了联合……为了建设一个统一的“色雷斯解放阵线”。
Pyrrhos: Things were simpler back then. All we cared about was the cause, about unity, and the Thracian Liberation Front.

鲍里斯：无视血统，无视种族，所有人都一样，我们都在同一个大家庭里。
Pyrrhos: Fighting for a world where, regardless of race or bloodline, we'd all live as one great family.

鲍里斯：白天，我们在山林中穿行，翻越雪线，炸毁敌人的补给线，把那些骑兵吓得连马粪都不敢留在原地。
Pyrrhos: We crossed forests, trudged through the snow over the mountains, and turned the enemy's supply lines to dust, heh. We scared those cavalrymen half to death.

鲍里斯：晚上，我们围着篝火，一起修枪，烤面包，唱那些老掉牙的游击战歌，像一家人那样。
Pyrrhos: And when night fell, we'd gather around the fire, break bread, clean our sights, and sing those songs of war and liberation, like brothers and sisters. You remember, don't you, Iglika?

告死鸟：……那确实是一段美好的生活。
Corvus: It was a good life.

鲍里斯：可惜，不是人人都这么想。背叛、流血，兄弟反目……这些我们都一同经历了。
Pyrrhos: What a shame that not everyone shared our vision. Betrayal, bloodshed, comrades parting ways ... We went through all of it together.

鲍里斯：后来我们先后离开。这么多年过去了……
Pyrrhos: In the end, even we chose to walk away. And now, after all these years ...

鲍里斯：现在，我只想将“多瑙黎明号”当成第二个解放阵线来奋斗。
Pyrrhos: I have a second chance to fight for what we believe in—the "Danube Dawn."

军官的声音很轻。他靠在窗边，沉默地望向漫天飞舞的白雪。
His voice softens as he leans against the window.

每当他侧过头，额角那块暗红的伤疤便毫无保留地展示在世人眼前，仿佛被烧灼的藤蔓。
As he turns, the scar at his temple shows raw and red, like burnt vines.

鲍里斯：我一直认为我们彼此是能互相理解的。
Pyrrhos: I've always felt we were kindred minds, you and I.

鲍里斯：因此，我可以相信你，不过问基金会的事——
Pyrrhos: I trusted you then, and I trust you now. I won't take any action against the Foundation—

他停顿了一瞬。
He pauses.

鲍里斯：但有两个条件。
Pyrrhos: On two conditions.

鲍里斯：第一，列车今晚先停靠在这里，明天一早发车。
Pyrrhos: First, the train mustn't leave until morning.

鲍里斯：我们需要一定的时间来行使“流程”，为巡逻队的事给上面一个交代。
Pyrrhos: We need it here long enough to go through some procedures and put together a justifiable account of the assault.

告死鸟：“流程”？你是指……
Corvus: "Procedures"? You mean ...

鲍里斯：别着急，这就是我说的第二个条件——
Pyrrhos: I'm getting there. Second—

鲍里斯：我需要对整趟车进行一次彻底搜查。
Pyrrhos: I need to conduct a full search of the train.

似曾相识的对话。停靠、登记、检查……简直没完没了。
Same old talk. Stops, papers, inspections ... it never ends.

告死鸟：乘客们已经经历过一次全面登记了，再来一遍除了造成无意义的恐慌，我看不出来有任何益处。
Corvus: The train's already been searched. You'd only raise more concern with the passengers.

告死鸟：如果你需要，我可以提供给你相关文件资料。
Corvus: I can provide you the passenger list if you must check.

军官摇了摇头。
Pyrrhos shakes his head.

鲍里斯：相信我，没人愿意半夜三更来干这得罪人的工作。但那些士兵倒得太蹊跷，报告已经呈上去了。
Pyrrhos: Believe me, my people don't enjoy this any more than yours do. But ... *tut* word has gotten out. It's only a matter of time until people start asking questions about the attack.

鲍里斯：我派人调查，就只是一个简单的表面流程。可一旦公司和政府查起来，这列车上藏了什么、我们都干了些什么……可就全摊在阳光底下了。
Pyrrhos: Besides, better that I do it, rather than getting the government or the company involved. We wouldn't want their prying eyes looking any closer, now would we?

告死鸟：……
Corvus: ...

这似乎是一个令人难以忽视的理由。列车长沉吟片刻，缓缓开口。
His point is made. The conductress carefully chooses her next words.

告死鸟：别动加挂车厢里的人，别惊扰乘客，列车组必须全程陪同。
Corvus: One of my crew members will be with you at all times. And tell your men to stay clear of the "cargo."

告死鸟：此外……列车现在物资紧缺，我们需要更多食物和医疗供给。当然，还有最重要的——列车在布达佩斯的优先通行权。
Corvus: As for the time we're losing, I need compensation: food, medicine, and priority clearance when we reach Budapest.

告死鸟：布达佩斯东站的行政手续一向很繁琐。列车每多停留一分钟，加挂车厢暴露的可能性就会越大。
Corvus: The paperwork there is cumbersome, and each minute the train is stopped risks our "cargo" being exposed.

告死鸟：如果以上要求你都能做到，那么我们可以配合。
Corvus: It's give and take. Do we have a deal?

鲍里斯：……
Pyrrhos: ...

军官的表情空白了一瞬，随即显出淡淡的无奈。
His expression blanks, then yields a faint resignation.

鲍里斯：原来如此。我猜你早就打算好在这里和我谈条件了。你总是知道如何寻找一个巧妙的时机给我添麻烦……
Pyrrhos: Iglika, Iglika ... *tut* I knew you wouldn't make this easy. You never do.

告死鸟：这只是一次双方自愿且完全平等的谈判而已，鲍里斯。
Corvus: This is a fair negotiation, Pyrrhos, for both of us.

告死鸟：我们都需要履行各自的职责，不是吗？
Corvus: We both have responsibilities to attend to, yes?

坐席车厢

紧闭已久的车门缓缓开启。列车长走在前头，步伐稳健，脸上带着一丝罕见的轻松。
The door creaks open. The conductress leads, her steps firm, face lightened by unusual ease.

军官跟在她身后，脸上不见怒意，却也远远称不上愉快。
Pyrrhos follows, neither angry nor content.

艾玛：哈啊……终于出来了。你们似乎聊了很久……
Aima: *yawn* Finally. Is everything alright? That was a long talk.

鲍里斯：放心吧，没有人吵架，也没有人受伤。我还没蠢到跟她硬碰硬——你这位老板可是谈判桌上的刽子手，而我只想尽快签字走人。
Pyrrhos: Of course, sweetheart. I got a little carried away talking about the good old days, and I should know better than to challenge your boss at the bargaining table.

军官抱怨着，忽然弯下腰，压低了声音。
He mutters complaints, then bends low, voice dropping.

鲍里斯：嘿，小家伙。刚才光顾着谈工作，还没来得及和你好好说话。
Pyrrhos: Listen, I'm sorry we haven't had a chance to talk. There's a lot on my plate right now.

鲍里斯：等检查工作做完……我有一份“礼物”要送给你。
Pyrrhos: But when I'm done, I have another "gift" for you.

艾玛：还有别的礼物？是新的裙子吗？可我的衣柜已经满啦……
Aima: Another? But Uncle Pyrrhos, my closet is already bursting.

鲍里斯：嘘……到时候你会知道的。
Pyrrhos: Shhh, this one's a secret. You'll see soon enough.

他眨眨眼，又伸了个懒腰，慢悠悠跟在列车长身后离开了。
With a wink and a lazy stretch, he trails after the conductress, out of sight.

TMW-13 不归者 / The Non-Returnees

车厢外传来沉闷而杂乱的脚步声，紧接着又是一阵不满的喧哗。
Outside the carriage come heavy footsteps, followed by a wave of restless complaints.

雅科夫：……听声音，像是军队的人来了。
Yakov: You hear that? Boots. Sounds like soldiers.

拉伊哈：是那位鲍里斯先生吗？
Reyhan: Could it be Pyrrhos again?

塞梅尔维斯：鲍里斯？
Semmelweis: Pyrrhos?

雅科夫：负责这次“偷渡行动”的军官，听说同列车长是一伙儿的。
Yakov: An army officer. He's working with the conductress to get us out of here.

新的名字，新的麻烦。
A new name, a new problem.

调查员皱起眉毛。
Semmelweis frowns.

塞梅尔维斯：……野树莓小姐，我想我们应该回去了。
Semmelweis: Come on, Rubuska. Time to go.

野树莓：啊？噢，没错！我应该在艾玛的车厢里才对，被发现可就糟了……
Rubuska: Huh? Oh, right! I'm supposed to be in Aima's cabin. I better not be seen here.

小伊凡：请等一下……野、野树莓小姐！
Ivanushka: W-Wait! Ms. Rubuska!

正欲离开的女孩听见了声音，又回过头来。
Just about to leave, she turns back to face the boy.

小伊凡：我只是想说，刚才你保护了我们，谢谢……你很勇敢，希望未来我也能像你一样勇敢！
Ivanushka: Th-Thank you for protecting us. I-I hope I can be brave like you when I grow up.

小伊凡：你是一个好血食怪！
Ivanushka: You're a good vampire!

女孩忍不住微笑起来。她俯下身，摸了摸男孩的脑袋。
She can't help but smile as she leans down to pat his head.

野树莓：你也是个好孩子，小伊凡。
Rubuska: And you're a good boy, Ivanushka.

野树莓：好了，现在你们的好血食怪需要暂时离开，一会儿再回来给你们通风报信。
Rubuska: Now listen, this good vampire has to go up front for a bit. But I'll be back soon with news from the other carriages.

野树莓：有我在，没人能伤害你们——来，伸出手。
Rubuska: No one will hurt you, you got that? Not while I'm around. Here, pinky promise.

她朝小伊凡伸出右手，小拇指轻轻勾起。
She reaches out her right hand to Ivanushka, hooking her pinky.

于是，小伊凡伸出尚且完好的右手，小拇指与女孩的勾在一起。
So Ivanushka lifts his good hand, pinky finger locking with hers.

小小的约定就此落下。
Their promise is sealed.

小伊凡：我们在这里等你。说好了哦……野树莓。
Ivanushka: I'll be waiting for you. You promised, so come back soon, Rubuska.

野树莓：好。接下来……这个我就没收了。
Rubuska: Don't worry, I will. Look, I'll take this.

她拾起脚边的那节木桩，在手中晃了晃。
She picks up the wooden stake at her feet and gives it a little shake.

野树莓：就当作是我们约定的信物吧。放心，我一定会回来的！
Rubuska: As a token of our promise. So you better hold the fort for me until I bring it back, alright?

座席车厢

告死鸟：大家安静，这只是一次例行检查。
Corvus: Ladies and gentlemen, please bear with us while we conduct a routine check.

安娜贝尔：你……你会抓走我们，就像对野树莓那样吗……
Annabelle: A-Are you going to take us too? Like you did with Rubuska?

小威廉：把老大还给我们！不然我就躺在地上，好叫你们什么也查不出来！
Little William: You give her back right now! Or I'll ... I'll lie down right here! I-I'll be an unmovable object!

男孩熟练地瘫倒在地，握紧肉乎乎的小拳头，像一位即将壮烈赴死的志士。
The boy flings himself to the ground, clenching his pudgy fists like a martyr ready to face his fate.

这是对付多萝西女士的杀手锏，男孩从不轻易示人——除非万不得已。
It's his final card to play, a tactic that has worked on the adults before, and one that he's counting on to work now.

告死鸟：你确定吗？我可以让你永远都躺在这里。
Corvus: If you are set on being "unmovable," I'd be happy to stitch you into the carpet.

小威廉：……
Little William: ...

他害怕地咽了咽口水。
He swallows hard.

小威廉：老大回来前……我是不会起来的！你、你死了这条心吧！
Little William: I-I'm not moving! Not until Rubuska's back!

空心木：例行检查？又一次？
Verity: Another search? Again?

空心木：哦，我明白了。你们这是打算每天做两遍检查，以防乘客吃过午餐后就立刻变成了什么别的物种。
Verity: I suppose you can never be too sure whether someone's transformed into a beast over lunchtime.

艾玛：万分抱歉，我们只是想再次确认……
Aima: We're ever so sorry for the inconvenience, but this is for your safety; we just have to check whether ...

索尼娅：好啊，那我也该再次确认你们有没有携带脑子工作。
Sonya: Oh, I have something to "check" too, young lady. Namely, whether anyone on this crew actually has a brain knocking around in their heads!

索尼娅：要我说，你们不是在维持秩序，而是制造混乱——这是列车纪律的羞耻，不是安全保障！
Sonya: You say this is for our safety, but all you've done is stir up chaos. You ought to be ashamed!

车厢内一片混乱。
The carriage is in chaos.

人们离开了各自的座位，热闹地挤作一团，眼看便要引发新一轮的动乱——
People leave their seats, crowding and shouting. The tension seems about to erupt into fresh turmoil.

鲍里斯：好了各位，现在该收起你们不合时宜的幽默感了。
Pyrrhos: That's quite enough commotion, everyone.

军官随手将手枪别回腰间，仿佛只是做了一件无关紧要的小事。
The officer slides his pistol back into his belt as if it were nothing more than a pen—just a tool.

所有人都安静了下来。就在这不安的静默里，另一道被掩藏已久的声音终于得见天日。
In the uneasy silence, another sound breaks through.

“咔……咔——咔咔……”
Hrrrk ... Urrrgh ... Rkkk ...

那是规律的、似有若无的声音，仿佛消化不良的节肢动物正在蠕动腔肠。
A slow, irregular churning, like the rumbling stomach of some terrible creature.

声音低了下来，随后又是一阵猫似的呜咽声。
The noise dips, then rises again into a catlike whimper.

“呜……”
*wail*

人们顺着声音的源头，一同望向角落里面色发白的绅士。
All eyes turn toward the pale-faced gentleman in the corner.

阿不思诺：我……别、别这样看我……
Arbuthnot: I ... W-What're you all starin' for?

阿不思诺：不是我……
Arbuthnot: That weren't me.

脚步声忽然响起。
Footsteps echo.

久未现身的调查员快步向人群走来，身后还跟着本该在车厢里沉睡的野树莓。
Semmelweis strides through the gathered people at a quick pace, with Rubuska trailing close behind.

告死鸟：你们怎么会在这里？
Corvus: What are you two doing here?

塞梅尔维斯：请先让我过去。刚才那个声音……
Semmelweis: Please, allow me through. There's something wrong.

调查员一边说着，大步朝阿不思诺走去，一把拽住他的手腕。
She moves as she speaks, grabbing Arbuthnot's wrist and yanking it away.

阿不思诺：等等！我说了不是我——
Arbuthnot: Watch it! I told you, it weren't me.

她推开阿不思诺，望向缩在他背后的、一直耷拉着头的陌生乘客。
She shoves him aside and looks at the slumped stranger hiding behind him.

塞梅尔维斯：你是什么人？之前做登记的时候没有你。
Semmelweis: Who are you? I didn't see you during the registration.

塞梅尔维斯：方便说话吗，先生？
Semmelweis: Can you speak, sir?

生病的乘客：……
Unwell Passenger: ...

乘客以一种极慢、极缓的速度仰起脸。
The passenger can hardly lift his face to meet hers.

他的脸色很白。瞳孔外，菌丝般的红色正延展向眼眸中央。
His face is chalk-white. Red streaks score outward from his pupils.

随后他张开嘴，里面荡漾着一片粘稠到发黑的血色海洋。
Then he opens his mouth, revealing a thick, black sea of blood swirling inside.

生病的乘客：咔……咔咔——
Unwell Passenger: Chk ... Chklga—

喷血特效

众乘客：啊啊啊啊——！
Passengers: AAAAHHHH!

生病的乘客：救……救我……
Unwell Passenger: H-Help ...

男人倒在地上，喉咙里不断呕出血来，又被他“咕噜咕噜”咽了回去。
He collapses, choking on the blood, gurgling as he swallows it back down.

调查员蹲下身，掀开他的眼皮。
The investigator kneels and pries open his eyelids.

塞梅尔维斯：……感染种？
Semmelweis: An Infected?

塞梅尔维斯：但和文件里描述的感染种症状……很不一样。是发生异变了吗？
Semmelweis: But this looks nothing like the usual symptoms. A mutation, perhaps?

告死鸟：——！！
Corvus: ...!

乘客Ⅲ：能不能讲点我们能听懂的话？感染种，感染什么了？
Passenger III: Hold on! Hold on! Would anyone care to explain this? What's an Infected? Infected by what?

空心木：重感冒，沙门氏菌，肺结核。你以为呢？
Verity: A pinch of cold, a dash of salmonella, and a spoonful of tuberculosis—what do you think?

空心木：当然是血食怪感染种。
Verity: He's been bitten by a vampire.

乘客Ⅲ：血！血食……
Passenger III: Va-Vampire?!

倒下

接二连三遭遇惊吓，乘客白眼一翻，终于晕了过去。
Overwhelmed with shock, the passenger faints.

乘客Ⅰ：上帝保佑……血食怪？我还以为那只是传说……
Passenger I: My goodness. A vampire? On this train? I figured those were just old stories.

鲍里斯：这里混进了不该有的东西，伊格丽卡。是那个血食怪女孩儿，对吗？
Pyrrhos: Oh, dear. Looks like we've got an unwelcome guest aboard. Iglika, did that strange girl do this?

他看向野树莓。
He looks toward Rubuska.

鲍里斯：刚才我听孩子们一直吵着说什么没有影子的“血食怪老大”。
Pyrrhos: I overheard the children talking about some shadowless "vampire boss."

多萝西：噢……我一直以为这只是孩子们的玩笑话！
Dorothy: Oh my. I thought it was just a silly game!

人们默不作声地打量着女孩。失去毡帽的遮掩，暗红色的双瞳再也无处遁形。
Everyone turns to Rubuska in a convicting silence. Without her hat, there is no hiding those ruby eyes.

于是，所有的恐惧都有了可以解释的根源。
Their fears find a cause.

乘客Ⅳ：我从一开始就觉得她不像是买了票的乘客，吵吵闹闹的。
Passenger IV: I knew there was something wrong with her the moment she came on board. All that shouting and running about.

乘客Ⅱ：嗯……仔细一看，她的皮肤也太苍白了一些……
Passenger II: And look, she's awfully pale, too.

野树莓：不……不是我干的。
Rubuska: No. No, it wasn't me.

鲍里斯：很遗憾，这里不是法庭，我也不是你请的律师。我们只负责一件事——清理麻烦。
Pyrrhos: This isn't a courtroom; there's no use pleading your case. You're going to have to leave the train.

鲍里斯：虽说血食怪不是我们的首要任务，但放任你在车上溜达？封闭车厢，一群毫无防备的活人……
Pyrrhos: After all, we can't have a vampire wandering free on a train full of ordinary people now, can we?

鲍里斯：小朋友，这里可不是你的专属豪华晚宴。
Pyrrhos: You'll have to find your next bite elsewhere, kid.

军官朝身后挥挥手。
Pyrrhos signals to his men.

TMW-15 云雀蛋糕 / Lark Cake

脸2特效

记忆中只剩下一张女人的脸。

And I buried the screams. Buried the gunshots. Buried her face deep in my memory.

女孩也躺了下去，小心翼翼地蜷缩在“母亲”身旁，让她早已僵硬的手臂环绕到自己的胸前。
She lies down with them, curling close to her mother, pulling a stiffened arm around her chest.

小野树莓：好暖和……妈妈，你要像小时候一样抱着我哦，还有还有，给我梳梳头发吧……
Young Rubuska: This is nice, like when I was little, and you used to hold me, Mама. When we wake up, will you comb my hair?

断指缠绕在她的发间，那轻微的触碰使她安心。
Cold fingers tangle in her hair, yet in her mind it feels like comfort.

小野树莓：妈妈，给我讲睡前故事吧。血食怪的故事，你已经讲了很多很多遍啦……没关系，我还想听……
Young Rubuska: Mама, tell me a story, would you? Please? I know you've told the vampire story a hundred times, but just once more, please.

小野树莓：“他们在血色的月光下复生，永远游走在黑夜的阴影里……”
Young Rubuska: "In the light of the blood moon, they rise and stride under the veil of night."

小野树莓：“他们的世界是自由的，没有死亡，也没有恐惧……”
Young Rubuska: "Freely, they live, without fear of death."

小野树莓：“只需饮下鲜血，他们便将永世长存。”
Young Rubuska: "For through blood they live forevermore."

闭眼
Her breath is shallow. Consciousness slips away with whispered stories as her eyes close, and she falls into slumber.

关闭眼

她闭上双眼，呼吸越来越轻。意识在模糊的呓语中悄然松弛，然后坠落，再坠落——
Because blood is life.

鲜血即是生命。
小野树莓：鲜血即是生命！
Young Rubuska: Because blood is life!

小野树莓：对，没错！血食怪只要吸食了鲜血，就能从墓穴里复生……
Young Rubuska: That's right! As long as they drink blood, vampires can rise from their graves and live forever!

女孩猛地坐起，惨白的脸染上了奇异的光彩。
The girl bolts upright, pallid face glowing with a strange light.

她咬破手指，将血液轻轻抹在母亲的嘴唇上。
She bites her finger and smears the flowing blood over her mother's lips.

那一瞬间，奇迹似乎发生了。
For a moment she believes in miracles.

鲜血在母亲的唇间微微溢出，犹如红色的玛瑙石般闪烁着，点亮了她那张原本晦暗发青的面庞。
The blood beads on cold lips, glowing like red agate, lighting up death's grim mask.

小野树莓：——！！
Young Rubuska: ...!

女孩惊喜地扬起嘴角。
The girl smiles with delight.

小野树莓：太好了，太好了，妈妈……
Young Rubuska: Yes, good, Mама!

小野树莓：我也要给爸爸、尼古拉都来上一点儿……
Young Rubuska: A little for Dad, too, and for Kolyo.

小野树莓：搞定啦！
Young Rubuska: All set!

她在每个家人的唇上都抹了一层厚厚的、浓郁到几乎有些滑稽的鲜血。
She smears thick, almost comical streaks of blood across her family's lips.

小野树莓：是的，我想起来了。就像故事中说的那样……
Young Rubuska: Yeah, we're just like the story!

小野树莓：爸爸、妈妈、小尼古拉，还有我——野树莓，我们本来就是血食怪一家呀！
Young Rubuska: Dad, Mама, Kolyo, and Rubuska—a vampire family!

小野树莓：难怪妈妈以前喜欢涂口红。红红的，像血一样美的口红。
Young Rubuska: That's why Mама likes to wear lipstick. It's just like blood.

小野树莓：别担心，妈妈……我重新为你涂上了。
Young Rubuska: Here, have a little more, Mама.

她温柔地抚摸着家人的脸庞。
She caresses their faces tenderly.

小野树莓：我已经猜出了身份的谜题。所以，你们快醒来吧……
Young Rubuska: Am I a clever girl? I figured it out. Now, we'll all wake up soon, right?

小野树莓：我知道，血食怪的复活需要很长、很长一段时间。
Young Rubuska: I know it might take a while, but I'll wait.

小野树莓：放心吧，在你们醒过来之前，我会一直等着你们、保护你们。
Young Rubuska: Don't worry. I'll be right here, watching over you.

一阵风轻轻吹起，呜咽一般的鸟叫声自天边响起。
A breeze lifts. A bird's cry drifts in from afar.

女孩看向如血的晚霞，吸了吸鼻子，朝天空挥舞着稚嫩的拳头。
The girl looks toward the scarlet-red sunset, sniffs, and raises her tiny fist to the sky.

小野树莓：你们别想伤害我的家人！
Young Rubuska: Don't even try to touch my family, you hear me?!

小野树莓：我、我可是德古拉的末代后裔，强大的血食怪野树莓！
Young Rubuska: I'm Rubuska the vampire, descendant of Dracula himself!

小野树莓：我在血色的月光下复生，永远游走在……走在黑夜的阴影里！
Young Rubuska: I'll rise in the light of the blood moon and stride under the veil of night!

小野树莓：我的世界是自由的，没有死亡，也没有恐惧。
Young Rubuska: I'll live freely, without fear of death!

小野树莓：我将保护我的亲族，直到永远的永远的永远的——
Young Rubuska: I'll watch over my blood forever and ever—

小野树莓：永远！
Young Rubuska: —forevermore!

斩钉截铁，掷地有声，来自一个孤独而激情、幼小但强大的血族后裔。
Her vow is sharp and unyielding, the fiery voice of a young but powerful child of an ancient and noble vampiric bloodline.

？？？：假的。
???: Liar.

小野树莓：咦，是谁在说话……？
Young Rubuska: Huh? Who's there?

她循着声音低下头去。不知为何，刚才鲜活的家人们此刻却变为了腐烂的尸体，红艳艳的嘴唇却一齐弯成了诡异的弧度。
She looks down again, and the illusion breaks. Cold blood dries on rotting faces. Their mouths bent into grotesque smiles.

小野树莓：你们……是谁？
Young Rubuska: Who are you?

小野树莓：呀！小尼古拉，你的衣服弄得太脏了……这样会挨妈妈骂的！
Young Rubuska: Kolyo! What happened to your clothes? Mама's going to be mad at you!

尸体双眼浑浊，浓重的死气环绕着躯体，面部已经溃烂，只剩下衣着还能依稀辨认出昔日身影。
Their eyes are milky and puckered dry, bodies cold and sagging, gray faces gaunt—blood-soaked and tattered clothes the last vestiges of their identities.

小野树莓：妈、妈妈……妈妈……别这样！妈妈，你抱抱我……你快醒来抱抱我呀……
Young Rubuska: Mама, Mама, Mама, wake up. Please, please hold me.

小野树莓：不要！不要！不要！
Young Rubuska: No! NO!

小野树莓：爸爸……妈妈！
Young Rubuska: Mама! Dad!

她尖叫着撕下一片衣服，用力地擦拭亲人溃烂的脸庞，只换来阵阵更加鲜明的腐臭。
She screams, ripping cloth, scrubbing furiously at their faces, but the flesh gives way like ripened cheese.

小野树莓：不……我们是血食怪……你们是不会死的，不会的……
Young Rubuska: No! You're not dead. We're vampires! We can't die!

她擦拭的力道牵扯着他们的嘴角，使那沾着鲜血的嘴唇展露出诡异的微笑。
Her rough wiping tugs at their mouths, baring smiles soaked in blood.

？？？：哈哈哈哈……
???: Hahahaha ...

笑声开始膨胀，从血色的嘴唇、无边的天幕与尸云中倾倒而出，哀号着、回荡着，如万千钟声齐鸣。
Laughter swells, spilling from red lips, from the sky, from the corpses, howling, echoing, like a thousand bells ringing at once.

？？？：假的！所有的一切——
???: Lies! All of it.

？？？：鲜血、红眼睛、尖牙、亲族的复生——都是假的！
???: Red eyes, fangs, the resurrection of our family—all lies!

小野树莓：不……
Young Rubuska: No ...

她害怕极了，转身奔跑在无尽的血日下。
Terrified, she runs toward the distant red sun.

然而无论她跑到哪里，这笑声却不打算放过她，像是奔涌在她体内、永不停歇的冰冷血液。
No matter how far she goes, the laughter seems to chase her.

？？？：跑！哈哈哈……
???: Off you run! Hahaha.

跑啊，野树莓——
Go, run, Rubuska!

跑啊！！
Run!

野树莓：——！！
Rubuska: ...!

女孩从深沉的梦中睁开双眼。
Rubuska jolts awake from a deep sleep.

野树莓：不是……假的……
Rubuska: It's not a lie.

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

心跳慢慢回落，视线逐渐适应眼前的黑暗。
Her heart slows. Her eyes adjust to the dark.

身旁弥漫着熟悉而又令人作呕的气息——死亡的气息，混杂着淡淡的燃油和烟草。
The stench beside her is revolting and bitterly familiar—death, mixed with fuel and smoke.

她转动眼珠，却与另一张膨胀发青的面庞四目相对。
She turns her gaze and meets another face, swollen and bluish.

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

那是一具早已发硬的尸体。青黑色的血管狰狞地缠绕在半透明的皮下，仿佛苍白古木那不断孽生的枝蔓。
A corpse, stiff and cold. Black veins coil beneath its pale skin like twisted branches of a dead tree.

眼神沿着躯干缓缓上移，最后定格在那张熟悉的脸上——她曾见过他，就在风雪纷飞的车站里。
Her eyes follow the body upward until they freeze on a face she knows—one she has seen before, back at the snowbound station.

回忆
渐入

乘客Ⅰ：类似的故事没有几百也有上千啦。血食怪吃人、狼人吃人、野兽吃人……
Passenger I: No, no, not precisely, but many like it. Vampires, werewolves, wild beasts, and monsters.

乘客Ⅰ：说到底，本质都是人吃人罢了，还非要安上一个名头。这些写故事的人呀，就喜欢这么弯弯绕绕。
Passenger I: It's always the same story about the powerful consuming the common folk. Heh, storytellers have always been good at making their points one way or another.

消回忆

野树莓：渐出
Rubuska: It's that old man from the train station.

野树莓：是车站的那个老爷爷……

老人的生命定格在了毫无意外的结局之中。
The irony of his warnings is a bitter mix of comedy and tragedy.

？？？：你醒了。
???: You are awake.

角落的黑影动了动，慢慢长成一个高大的人形。
A shadow in the corner stirs, taking the shape of a looming man.

鲍里斯：渴吗？
Pyrrhos: Thirsty?

野树莓：你是刚才的那个军官……这些都是你干的？
Rubuska: You-you're that officer. What is all of this? Did you ... Did you kill these people?

军官置若罔闻，仿佛压根儿没听见女孩说话。
Pyrrhos ignores the questions.

破抹布在地上发出沉闷的拖拽声。最终，它被随手扔在野树莓面前。
The rag drags across the floor with a heavy scrape, tossed casually to Rubuska's feet.

鲍里斯：很遗憾，这里没有别的食物和饮用水了，但血和肉一定管够。
Pyrrhos: I'm afraid I haven't been a very good host, and alas, our water supply has run dry. Blood, however? Well, we've got plenty of that.

鲍里斯伸出手，长长的、发黑的指甲情人般轻拂过尸体的手腕。
Pyrrhos extends his hand, long blackened nails stroking the corpse's wrist with a vile tenderness.

流血

鲍里斯：喝吧，“小血食怪”。
Pyrrhos: Drink up, Little Miss "Vampire."

血沿着野树莓的头发向下流淌，先是睫毛、眼睛，再是鼻子……最后是嘴。
Blood runs down Rubuska's hair, lashes, eyes, nose, finally her mouth.

野树莓：咳咳……唔呕——！！
Rubuska: *cough* Blrrrghh!

鼻尖满是腥臭的血气，她再也支撑不住，半趴在地上疯狂呕吐。
Her nose fills with the stench of blood. She collapses halfway to the floor, retching violently.

肉菜烩饭冰冻果子露果仁蜜饼云雀蛋糕……
Stew, frozen berries, honey bread, lark cake ...

所有她吃过的好东西全都顺着肠胃的痉挛一并呕出，和地上那些污秽的血水以及组织器官紧密交融，不分彼此。
Everything she's eaten pours out with each spasm, mingling with the foul blood and shredded organs on the ground.

鲍里斯：……真是狼狈啊。真正的血食怪可不会这样。
Pyrrhos: Not so demure at the table, are we? *tut* How embarrassing. I knew you weren't one of us.

野树莓：呼，呼……你……
Rubuska: *pant* You ...

她仰起苍白的脸，看向眼前男人的双瞳。
She lifts her pale face and meets the man's horrid gaze.

那是不同于她的、完全没有掺杂一丝杂质的纯净血色，仿佛月光下静静流淌的鲜血海洋。
His eyes are pure crimson, flawless, like a sea of blood flowing under moonlight.

毋庸置疑的血脉，毋庸置疑的身份。
An undeniable bloodline. An undeniable identity.

野树莓：你也是……血食怪？
Rubuska: You're a vampire, too?

鲍里斯：当然。哦，纠正一点，没有“也”。
Pyrrhos: Through and through. But you? It seems not to be so.

鲍里斯：哈哈……还没清醒过来吗？可怜的小冒牌货。
Pyrrhos: Still lost in your dreamland, little imposter?

野树莓：不……我不是冒牌货……
Rubuska: Don't call me that.

野树莓：我的亲族……他们不久就将从墓穴里醒来，与我重聚……
Rubuska: My family—my blood—they'll rise from the grave soon, you'll see! We'll be together again.

她挣扎着吞咽着流淌的鲜血，直到满脸满身都是血迹。
She chokes and swallows the blood until her face and body are smeared with scarlet.

假的。那一天永远也不会来。
A lie—that day will never come.

车站仓库

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

鲍里斯：哈哈哈哈……
Pyrrhos: Hahahaha ...

男人开怀地笑了起来。
The man cackles.

Pyrrhos: Aren't you a sorry little thing? It almost stirs something in this useless old heart.

鲍里斯：不错，你让我很满意。所以，我可以给你一个实现愿望的机会。
Pyrrhos: In fact, I've almost come to like you. Tell you what, I could make your wish come true.

野树莓：实现……愿望？
Rubuska: My wish?

军官血色的双瞳闪烁着不可捉摸的危险。

Pyrrhos: You heard me. I can help you ...

鲍里斯：成为一名真正的血食怪。

TMW-16 雪与惊魂夜 / Winter Fright Night

小威廉：不——我是不会跟你们走的……绝不！
Little William: No. I'm not going with you! NEVER!

小威廉死死抱住列车座椅的扶手，发出足以杀穿列车层层钢铁外壳的尖叫声。
Little William clings to the seat rail, screaming loud enough to pierce steel.

“隔离条令”发布后不久，乘客们被打乱、分离，而其中部分乘客转移到了列车长车厢。
After the quarantine order, passengers are scattered, some herded into the conductress's cabin.

边防士兵Ⅰ：松手。
Border Checkpoint Soldier I: Let go.

Soldiers pry open the boy's stubborn fingers one by one.

Semmelweis: Officers, with all due respect, you've taken a dozen passengers already.

Semmelweis: May I ask where you're taking them?

Her words and any vital intelligence she could share are stranded with her.

一切本应安静摆放的物品，如今乱作一团，又因血迹的点缀而显得分外诡异。

塞梅尔维斯：这是……

???: Aaahahah!

边防士兵Ⅱ：嘶……到底怎么回事？
Border Checkpoint Soldier II: What the—Everything alright?

Border Checkpoint Soldier II: Ah. Idiot. Better go check on him.

看守的士兵提起枪，急匆匆离开了。
