塞梅尔维斯：整件事都是鲍里斯设计的一个幌子，所谓的隔离只不过是变相软禁罢了。他们口中的“隔离”可不像是在预防血食怪感染。
Semmelweis: No food, no water, no radio signal. I don't believe they're doing anything to protect the passengers from infection. This isn't a quarantine; this is a cover-up.

告死鸟：看样子你的调查工作有进展了。
Corvus: What are you suggesting?

调查员不再掩饰，而是拿出先前从巡逻队身上拾起的徽章。
The investigator reveals the badge in her hand.

塞梅尔维斯：如果我没记错的话，你手上也有一个。
Semmelweis: This insignia. I believe you have one just like it.

告死鸟：所以这才是你一直在找的东西。
Corvus: That's what you were sniffing around for.

塞梅尔维斯：这不是眼下的重点。它是我一直在调查的组织——“重塑之手”的信物。
Semmelweis: It belongs to an organization I've been tracking—Manus Vindictae.

告死鸟：重塑之手？
Corvus: Manus Vindictae?

塞梅尔维斯：我猜你应该不是重塑之手的一员，不然鲍里斯不会如此提防你，你也不会和我们一起被关在这里。
Semmelweis: At first, I thought you were one of them. Yet here you are, locked up like the rest of us. Perhaps Pyrrhos doesn't trust you all that much.

列车长困惑的表情使调查员进一步验证了她的猜测。
Corvus's look of confusion—certainly genuine—serves to confirm her suspicion.

塞梅尔维斯：重塑之手，一个危险的极端神秘学家组织，以引发混乱为乐，每个成员都是不折不扣的疯子。
Semmelweis: The Manus are a group of extremist arcanists that take pleasure in chaos and despair. Heartless bastards, every last one of them.

告死鸟：……这原本是鲍里斯提供给我们的、方便大家识别自己人的信物。
Corvus: Never heard of them. The badge is Pyrrhos's, some kind of identifier for his men.

塞梅尔维斯：根据我登车前所掌握的情报，再结合眼下的状况……鲍里斯很可能与重塑之手投放在列车上的血食怪有关。
Semmelweis: When I took this mission, our intelligence suggested that the vampire I'm after may be associated with Manus Vindictae. If Pyrrhos is working with them, he could be working with the vampire aboard.

塞梅尔维斯：甚至有可能就是那位血食怪本尊。
Semmelweis: It's possible, indeed, that he could be the vampire himself.

告死鸟：……
Corvus: ...

告死鸟：鲍里斯是血食怪。
Corvus: Pyrrhos is a vampire.

列车长不再回避，平静地宣读了真相。
No more evasions and equivocal answers, the conductress calmly reveals the truth.

告死鸟：我们曾经并肩作战，他为组织贡献过很多力量。他聪明，冷静，总是能在关键时刻做出最理性的判断。
Corvus: We were comrades-in-arms once. One of the most capable fighters we had—clever, composed, he always made the right decisions when it counted.

告死鸟：因此我从未想过他会和什么“极端神秘学家组织”扯上关系。
Corvus: I would never have thought he'd be involved with such an organization.

塞梅尔维斯：那么，几乎可以肯定了——他就是重塑之手安插在列车上的血食怪。
Semmelweis: I'm afraid it's almost certain that he's the vampire Manus Vindictae had sent to this train.

真相终于浮出水面。调查员长长吐出一口气，背后的重量终于卸下。
At last, a lead. Semmelweis breathes a long, drawn-out breath, letting the weight fall off her shoulders.

塞梅尔维斯：既然彼此已经挑明，那么我想请问，我的队友们……
Semmelweis: Now that things are out in the open, do you have any idea what happened to my squad?

列车长摇摇头。
The reply comes with a resigned shake of her head.

告死鸟：很遗憾，我确实从未见过你的队友们。
Corvus: No. I haven't seen any of them.

告死鸟：曾有基金会的成员搭乘过列车，又和车上的神秘学家们起了一点小冲突。因此我对他们有印象——很显然，不是好的那一种。
Corvus: I'd know. As I've said before, this isn't the first time we've had the Foundation aboard. Last time there was a confrontation between them and some other arcanists.

塞梅尔维斯：抱歉。很多时候，惹人不快也是我们工作的一部分。
Semmelweis: Hah. Sometimes, I think causing trouble might be our primary mission.

塞梅尔维斯：重塑之手，我不清楚他们真正的目的，但恐怕……
Semmelweis: But let's return to our vampire. I'm still not certain what Manus Vindictae is up to, but ...

告死鸟：恐怕和刚才被感染的乘客有关，是吗？
Corvus: That vampire infection couldn't have been a coincidence. Someone meant for it to happen.

列车长冷笑一声，轻轻摩挲着银制手枪上的雕花。
The conductress sneers, her fingers tracing the silver engraving on her pistol.

告死鸟：我认识鲍里斯很多年了，他最近的行为虽然很异常，但只要不干涉列车的正常运作，我对他的私事不感兴趣。
Corvus: I've known Pyrrhos a long time. But lately he's been strange. I usually wouldn't attempt to interfere with his business.

告死鸟：但这一次……他越界了。
Corvus: But these are my passengers—my train.

塞梅尔维斯：既然如此……身为“多瑙黎明号”的列车长，我猜你应该有办法帮助我们脱困？
Semmelweis: Glad to see we're finally on the same page. So, Conductress, can you get us out of here?

告死鸟：耐心，调查员。现在只剩最后一块拼图了。
Corvus: Haste makes waste, Investigator. There's a loose thread I'm waiting for, then we can pull all of this together.

塞梅尔维斯：我必须说，这已经不是耐心的时机了——
Semmelweis: We're long past the point for patience, if you ask me.

血手印
现场

安娜贝尔：啊——！！
Annabelle: Ah!

惊叫打断了二人的沟通。一只血手猛地贴上车窗，拖出一道道蜿蜒的血痕。
A bloody hand slaps the window, smearing crimson streaks down the glass.

？？？：呜……
???: Oh ...

塞梅尔维斯：是被感染的乘客。
Semmelweis: Another Infected!

塞梅尔维斯：现在你觉得我们还需要耐心吗，列车长女士？
Semmelweis: What was that about "haste makes waste," Conductress?

告死鸟：……
Corvus: ...

感染的乘客：过去……让我过去。
Infected Passenger: Through. Let me through.

咚。咚。
Thud. Thud.

他面无表情地嘟哝着，用头一下一下撞着车窗玻璃，直到额头鲜血淋漓。
The man mumbles flatly, headbutting the glass again and again until blood pours from his brow.

感染的乘客：让我。过去。
Infected Passenger: Let me through.

安娜贝尔：啊啊啊——！！
Annabelle: Ah!

安娜贝尔：他，他就要进来了……
Annabelle: He's ... He's breaking in.

感染的乘客：让我过去让我过去让我过去让我过去让我过去让我过去——
Infected Passenger: Let me through, let me through, let me through, let me through.

塞梅尔维斯：列车长女士，现在我们可用不了神秘术。
Semmelweis: Conductress, there must be something muting arcane skills on this train.

告死鸟：调查员，到我身后去。
Corvus: Arcane skills aren't everything.

她将乘客们护在后方，掏出别在腰间的手枪，将枪口对准车门。
She pulls the passengers behind her, draws her sidearm, and takes aim.

震屏

感染的乘客：呃啊——！！
Infected Passenger: Uggh!

尚未来得及开枪，被感染的乘客忽然被一股强大的外力拽离了人们的视野。
Before the shot fires, the infected passenger is yanked away by an unseen force.

震屏

更多血沾在了车窗上。鲜红的液体沿着窗框流下，留下一条条不规则的血痕。
Another splash of blood smears across the window.

塞梅尔维斯：……外面打起来了？
Semmelweis: What was that? Another Infected?

声音安静下来。不一会儿，门外又传来窸窸窣窣的响动。
The sound dies. Then comes a faint rustling outside the door.

一个毛茸茸的脑袋从车窗外缓缓升起。
A familiar face rises into view beyond the glass.

艾玛：是我……
Aima: No. It's just me.

塞梅尔维斯：如果我猜得没错……这就是你刚才所说的，最后一块拼图？
Semmelweis: Is she what you were waiting for, Conductress?

告死鸟：没错。艾玛，刚才引走驻军的人也是你，对吗？
Corvus: Exactly. Aima, you drew that soldier away, yes?

艾玛：嗯，我等了好久才找到机会……
Aima: Mm-hm. I waited for just the right moment.

告死鸟：做得好。现在外面情况如何？
Corvus: Well done. What's our situation?

艾玛：走廊上、车厢里到处都是……感染种，都是从仓库里跑出来的。现在整趟车都已经……
Aima: There are Infected everywhere—the cabins, the hallways—all through the train. They seem to be running out from the station warehouse.

乘务员面色发白，向大家诉说自己一路上的见闻。
The stewardess goes pale, recounting everything she saw outside.

艾玛：墙上、餐桌上、座椅下全是血，我一眼都不敢看……
Aima: There's blood everywhere, too, on the walls, on the floor ... I tried my best not to look at it.

塞梅尔维斯：真叫人意想不到。刚才那个被感染的乘客……是你杀的？
Semmelweis: Was it you who killed that Infected just now?

艾玛：嗯……
Aima: Well …

女孩有些害羞地拽了拽自己右侧的眼罩。
She tugs shyly at her eyepatch.

告死鸟：身为“多瑙黎明号”的乘务员，会点儿防身的技巧并不是什么稀奇事。
Corvus: I ensure all crew on the "Danube Dawn" are trained in self-defense. It's hardly surprising.

告死鸟：艾玛，继续说。
Corvus: Go ahead, Aima.

艾玛：好……
Aima: Oh, yes.

乘务员低着头，握成拳的手轻轻颤抖着。
She lowers her head, clenched fist trembling.

艾玛：刚才在外面的时候，我看到了那些士兵。我本以为他们会忙着安抚乘客，或者清理感染源，保护大家……
Aima: I saw those soldiers in their carriages. I thought they'd be caring for the passengers or removing the Infected, but ...

艾玛：可他们什么也没做，就像是……就像是在任由这一切发生。
Aima: They did nothing, as if it were of no concern to them whatsoever.

艾玛：乘客们被带去临时拘留室“检查”，然后又一个个被带去了仓库，紧接着一切都开始失控了……
Aima: They took the passengers, one by one, to some kind of detention room for inspection, then sent them to the warehouse. But then they started coming back out, like that.

乘务员一边说着，手指擦过脸上的点点血迹，放在嘴里含了一瞬。
She wipes a smear of blood from her cheek, then slips her finger briefly into her mouth.

艾玛：鲍里斯叔叔……我不知道他身上发生了什么，总之我们得先找到他。
Aima: Uncle Pyrrhos ... I don't know what's happened to him, but we have to find him.

告死鸟：我明白了。那些驻军呢？
Corvus: I see. How many soldiers remain aboard the train?

艾玛：有不少去临时拘留室看守关押的乘客了，车上剩下的数量不多。可、可以对付！
Aima: Not many. A few were sent to guard the detention room. I-I think we can handle the ones that are left!

乘务员小心翼翼地挥舞起小拳头。
The meek girl pumps her fist in an uncommon gesture of confidence.

告死鸟：很好。现在人已经到齐，没必要再等了。
Corvus: Good. Everything is in place; let's move.

艾玛：嘘……外面有脚步声。
Aima: Wait, shh. I hear footsteps.

艾玛：刚才我已经被人看到了，被发现可不好……
Aima: They saw me just then. I can't be seen here again.

乘务员迅速环顾了一圈，躲进了窗帘背后。
Aima's eye darts around before she ducks behind the curtains.

下一秒，车门被大力扯开。
Then, the door is opened forcefully.

边防士兵Ⅱ：见鬼……这下全失控了……
Border Checkpoint Soldier II: Damn it. This is getting out of hand.

处理完“意外事故”的士兵急匆匆跑进来，站定，再度将枪口指向没有抵抗能力的乘客们。
Soldiers, having dealt with the "unexpected occurrence," rush in, weapons raised at the frightened passengers.

边防士兵Ⅱ：不好意思，刚才耽误了一会儿……让我们接着下一个……
Border Checkpoint Soldier II: Where were we? On to the next passenger.

枪口漫不经心地左右晃荡着，最终落在安娜贝尔身上。
The muzzle drifts left and right, finally settling on Annabelle.

边防士兵Ⅱ：就你吧。小朋友，麻烦跟我们走一趟。
Border Checkpoint Soldier II: You. Little girl. It's your turn.

安娜贝尔：我……？不，我不要过去……
Annabelle: Me? I don't want to go!

边防士兵Ⅱ：行了，少废话——
Border Checkpoint Soldier II: Come now, be quiet.

摇晃的枪管被死死扣住。
The muzzle is locked in place.

告死鸟：她说了，她不想过去。
Corvus: You heard her.

告死鸟：听不懂吗？
Corvus: She said: No.

争执间，两发子弹不偏不倚地射在车厢的金属顶棚上。
In the scuffle, two shots ring out, each slamming into the metal ceiling.

士兵试图拽回步枪，然而枪管依旧被列车长牢牢握在手里，动弹不得。
The soldier tries to wrench back his rifle, but Corvus's grip is unyielding.

边防士兵Ⅱ：你……放手……！
Border Checkpoint Soldier II: You! Let go!

告死鸟：她不想过去。
Corvus: She's not going.

边防士兵Ⅲ：嘿。你们在做什么？都给我退后——
Border Checkpoint Soldier III: What's going on? Stand down, all of you!

又一个士兵出现在众人身后。他一手举枪，另一只手则颤抖着掏出一枚口哨。
Another soldier appears behind them, gun in one hand, whistle in the other, his fingers shaking.

告死鸟：去吧，艾玛。
Corvus: Go, Aima.

艾玛：噢……好的，我明白了！
Aima: Y-Yes. Understood!

乘务员摘下眼罩，露出另一只暗红如血的眼睛。
The stewardess tears off her eyepatch, revealing her other blood-red eye.

哨声还未来得及吹响，她便从阴影中一跃而出，以惊人的速度飞扑到士兵身上。
Before the whistle meets his lips, she leaps from the shadows, slamming into him.

边防士兵Ⅲ：滚、滚开！
Border Checkpoint Soldier III: Aargh! Get off me!

下一秒，她抡起胳膊，环住士兵的脖颈。
In a second, her arm snakes around his neck.

边防士兵Ⅲ：呃啊——！！
Border Checkpoint Soldier III: Uggh!

艾玛：很抱歉，枪和口哨我都没收了……！
Aima: Apologies for the shock, but thank you for the gun and whistle.

士兵们被轻松放倒在地。
The soldiers collapse.

乘务员将他们拖到角落，长舒一口气，又拉下了眼罩。
Aima drags them to the corner, exhales, and pulls her eyepatch down.

艾玛：这下没有人会被带走啦，暂时安全！
Aima: No one will take you away, Annabelle, at least for the time being.

艾玛：嗯？怎么都不说话……
Aima: Hm? Why is everyone so quiet?

乘客们默不作声，纷纷朝她投来讶异的目光。女孩惊喜地迎了上来，拉住她的裙角。
Passengers stare in slack-jawed silence. The girl runs up, tugging excitedly at her skirt.

安娜贝尔：红眼睛，还有尖牙……乘务员小姐，你……你也是血食怪吗？
Annabelle: Red eyes, fangs ... A-Are you a vampire too, Stewardess?

艾玛：抱歉，我不是故意隐瞒。不过放心，血食怪的身份不会影响我为大家服务的。
Aima: Oh. Well, yes, I am. But don't worry. It won't affect your service in any way whatsoever!

安娜贝尔：奇怪……你的另一只眼睛虽然像湖水那样美，却一点儿也不红。难道也是染红的吗？
Annabelle: But your other eye is all clear and blue, like a lake, not red at all. How did you do that?

艾玛：我……我不是纯种的血食怪。
Aima: I-I'm not a pure-blood vampire.

小乘务员轻轻摇头，并不打算就这个话题展开太多。
She shakes her head quietly before looking away; she has no intention of going any deeper into the subject.

塞梅尔维斯：想不到列车上的血食怪传说都是真的。只是……我以为它至少会高一点，或者凶一点，不是会端茶递水的那一种。
Semmelweis: I have to say, I didn't expect the stories of a vampire train to actually hold any truth. Though I doubt any of the stories had our vampires pouring tea and fluffing pillows.

告死鸟：部分是真的。艾玛从未伤害过任何人。
Corvus: There was never any truth to them. Aima may be a vampire, yes, but she's never done anyone harm.

塞梅尔维斯：我明白了。那么之前在树林里的时候，你们……
Semmelweis: Then, earlier, in the forest ...

回忆
渐入

她回忆起俩人在风雪中依偎时的场景。
She recalls the night in the snow, with the two of them pressed close together.

那时雪下得太大，她费力伸长脖颈，也只看见白雾、树影，以及一条在雪中飞舞的红色围巾。
The storm was so thick she could barely see, only mist, trees, and a red scarf whipping in the wind.

消回忆
渐出

告死鸟：是渴血症犯了。我将我的血给了她，就像以前无数次做过的那样。
Corvus: It was bloodthirst, so I gave her mine. It's an arrangement of ours.

列车长一边说着，轻轻整理了一下小乘务员因战斗而稍许松开的围巾。
Corvus adjusts the scarf around the small stewardess's neck.

塞梅尔维斯：先是加挂车厢，现在又是血食怪……你很擅长隐藏，列车长女士。
Semmelweis: First a secret carriage, now a vampire stewardess. What else might you be hiding up your sleeve?

告死鸟：放心，我们立场一致。起码在这次事件中，我们已经成为同伴。
Corvus: Nothing of your concern. We share a common interest, so let us treat each other as comrades.

告死鸟：同伴手握底牌，并不是什么坏事。观察、等待，然后一击致命。这是我的做事习惯。
Corvus: There may be tricks up my sleeve, but for now, we watch, wait, and then strike.

塞梅尔维斯：原来您还是一位出色的猎人。那么，下一步，您打算怎么做？
Semmelweis: You surprise me more and more, Conductress. Comrades it is, but what's our next move?

告死鸟：……
Corvus: ...

告死鸟：我本不想对老友动手。
Corvus: I wish there were some other way, old friend.

她吐出一口气，眼里闪过冰冷的光。
She exhales, a cold light flashing in her eyes.

告死鸟：艾玛，车上还剩多少乘客？
Corvus: Aima, how many passengers are left on board?

艾玛：我没数过，但士兵们把很多乘客押去了车站的临时拘留室。
Aima: I didn't count precisely; there were already quite a few that were taken to the detention room.

艾玛：哦！列车长，您难道是要……
Aima: Oh! Conductress, are you going to ...

列车长穿过人群，走到一个高大的橱柜面前，狠狠一拉——
Corvus pushes through the crowd to a tall cabinet and yanks it open.

告死鸟展示军火库

告死鸟：基金会的，你开过枪吗？
Corvus: You there. Ever handled a gun before?

乘客们：哇……
Stowaways: Whoa ...

墙壁上挂满了整齐排列的各式武器，在灯光下闪闪发亮。
Weapons line the wall in neat rows, gleaming under the light.

每一根枪管都被精心地擦拭、抛光，仿佛在默默等待战斗的号角。
Each one meticulously polished and ready, as if awaiting their call to battle.

塞梅尔维斯：……
Semmelweis: ...

塞梅尔维斯：所以你背地里还是个军火贩子？这数量要是放在某些国家，足以发动一次政变了。
Semmelweis: Yet another surprise. I don't think I ever would have expected you to be lugging an armory around with you.

告死鸟：一点小小的收藏爱好罢了。接着。
Corvus: It's a hobby. Take this.

她将一支悉心养护过的手枪取出并丢给调查员。
She takes a pistol down and tosses it to Semmelweis.

告死鸟：对付血食怪和感染种时，银色子弹比神秘术好用。
Corvus: Silver bullets are more effective than arcane skill when dealing with vampires and their Infected.

告死鸟：各自装备好武器，伙计们。接下来等着我们的……将是一场恶战。
Corvus: Anyone old enough to handle a weapon, arm yourselves. We have a fierce battle ahead.

TMW-17 睦邻 / Friends in Need

枪声四起。从守车离开不过半小时，车厢内早已成为硝烟弥漫的战场。
Gunfire erupts. In less than half an hour, the train turns into a battlefield.

塞梅尔维斯：见鬼……！
Semmelweis: Damn!

塞梅尔维斯：枪声把它们都吸引过来了。门——我们得把门关上。
Semmelweis: The gunshots are drawing them in. We've got to close the door!

告死鸟：你们先离开，我去关门。
Corvus: Head to the next carriage. I'll close the door.

告死鸟离开座椅的掩护，径直冲向那聚集了无数鲜血与哀号的危险禁地。
Corvus leaves cover and charges straight into the carnage.

安娜贝尔：列车长……不……
Annabelle: Conductress, don't!

告死鸟：别回头！！
Corvus: Don't look back!

被凝视的感觉实在太过强烈。安娜贝尔没有忍住，缓缓转过头……
The weight of unseen eyes is unbearable. Annabelle turns her head.

感染种扒车门

安娜贝尔：——！！
Annabelle: ...!

安娜贝尔：我……我想回家……
Annabelle: I-I want to go home.

告死鸟：……
Corvus: ...

告死鸟：都说了别回头了。

塞梅尔维斯：不行，这些家伙数量太多，我们根本对付不过来。
Semmelweis: There are too many of them. We can't do this alone.

感染的乘客：嗷啊啊……
Infected Passenger: Aaaargh ...

从列车外涌入越来越多的感染种。他们穿梭在各个车厢间，如同癌细胞一般增殖、扩散。
From outside, more Infected swarm in, spreading like a plague of locusts through every car.

号哭一声接着一声，仿佛永远都不会停歇。
Cries of panic and bloodlust rise and fall.

塞梅尔维斯：弹药还够，但很明显，我们人力不足。
Semmelweis: We have enough ammunition but not enough hands to fire them.

告死鸟：眼下只剩下一个办法了。
Corvus: There is still one option left.

告死鸟：我们的火力无法突破感染种的防守，应该去其他车厢争取尽可能多的乘客。
Corvus: There are more passengers. We can rally the people to fight.

塞梅尔维斯：来的路上，我们所见的车厢都被士兵占领了。或许存在尚有理智的乘客，但我对此不抱过多期望。
Semmelweis: The other carriages are still under guard; I doubt we'll find many willing passengers who are still fit to join us.

告死鸟：还有一个地方……就在守车后面，鲍里斯曾答应过我不会动它。
Corvus: Hm. I know where to go. Pyrrhos gave me his word he would leave them be.

塞梅尔维斯：所以你相信重塑之手成员的承诺？
Semmelweis: And you still think he'll stand by it?

告死鸟：很遗憾，我们没有更好的选择。至于他的承诺是否为真……
Corvus: It's our best chance. As for whether he has kept his promise ...

她呼吸平稳，枪口对准因撞击而愈发脆弱的车门。
She steadies her breath, aiming at the door buckling under the assault.

告死鸟：去看看不就知道了。
Corvus: We're about to find out.

枪声仍未停歇。
Gunfire still rattles.

此刻，又有新的声音加入战场——一连串散乱而密集的脚步声。
Another sound joins in—scattered, heavy footsteps.

拉伊哈：一个、两个、三个……不，远不止三个。
Reyhan: One, two, three ... No, there are more. Many more.

她的声音逐渐颤抖起来。
Her voice trembles.

拉伊哈：脚步声很杂乱，听上去不像是鲍里斯他们的人。怎么办，雅科夫？
Reyhan: They don't sound like soldiers. What do we do, Yakov?

雅科夫：……
Yakov: ...

雅科夫：大家备好武器，听我指挥。
Yakov: Ready your weapons, everyone.

脚步声越来越近，沉重的铜锁被再度拽起。
The steps draw closer. The lock strains.

人们纷纷拿出手中的“武器”，数十道目光落在那扇缓慢开启的车厢门上。
Passengers grip their makeshift weapons, every eye fixed on the opening door.

雅科夫：好……都给我上！
Yakov: Hold. Now! Attack!

人群一拥而上，毫不留情地将手中的武器往来客身上狠狠招呼。
The mob surges, raining down blows without mercy.

气急败坏的声音：见鬼，别打了——我们是来帮你们的！
Agitated Voice: Stop, damn it! We're here to help!

稚嫩的声音：娃娃……我的娃娃不见了……
Young Voice: My dolly ... I can't find her.

哭声、咒骂声和抱怨声此起彼伏，足以出乎所有人的预料。
Cries, curses, and wails crash together in a storm.

雅科夫：嗯？女人……还有孩子？
Yakov: Wait, wait! I heard the little girl! And-And a woman?

车厢内的小小战争终于停歇。
The little skirmish finds a belated end.

一支临时组建的军事小队出现在“偷渡”的乘客眼前，就连老人都配备了锃亮的装备。
A makeshift militia appears before them, young and old bedecked in piecemeal gear.

塞梅尔维斯：请大家放下手中的武器。
Semmelweis: Everyone, please lower your weapons.

塞梅尔维斯：谨慎是好事，但我想我们没必要每次一见面就兵刃相向。
Semmelweis: There's really no need to be at each other's throats each time we meet.

拉伊哈：是刚才的那位调查员女士，还有……列车长？！
Reyhan: It's that investigator. She's back. And the conductress!

列车长上前，将在冲突中被挤歪的帽檐轻轻扶正。
Corvus steps forward, adjusting a tilted hat brim.

告死鸟：不错，看来你们已经具备了组织和武装自己的能力。
Corvus: Excellent, you're already prepared to protect yourselves.

告死鸟：长话短说。这趟列车被血食怪感染种包围了，我们需要在座各位的帮助，不然列车将无法启动。
Corvus: I'll make this short. The train is surrounded by vampire Infected. We need your help to defeat them and get moving again.

告死鸟：为此我们准备了一些武器。大家挑把趁手的，然后……我们一起杀出去。
Corvus: Take a weapon if you're able. We'll fight together.

乘客们面面相觑，杂乱的车厢里短暂沉默了一瞬。
The stowaways and the passengers glance at one another. Silence holds for a moment.

“偷渡”的乘客Ⅰ：可……这一切和我们又有什么关系？
Stowaway I: But, why us?

“偷渡”的乘客Ⅰ：都是那些有权有势的贵族、军人搞出来的祸事，我们只是一群手无寸铁的偷渡客，为什么要为此买单？
Stowaway I: Look around you. We're just a bunch of regular folk—refugees who've probably never even touched a gun. The army's here, isn't it? Shouldn't they clean up this mess?

“偷渡”的乘客Ⅱ：没错。就算我们费尽心思救了他们，那些家伙会拿正眼瞧我们吗？
Stowaway II: And say we risk our lives to save other people from these Infected, what would stop them from reporting us if we try to cross the border after?

乘客们你一言我一语地议论起来，质疑一声高过一声。
Then voices rise again, questions sharp and insistent.

“偷渡”的乘客Ⅰ：没错！要我说，干脆把那几节车厢都卸了，我们剩下的人还能继续前往布达佩斯。
Stowaway I: She's right. I say we unload the carriages with the Infected inside, and the rest of us keep going to Budapest.

拉伊哈：你觉得呢，雅科夫？
Reyhan: You're quiet, Yakov. What are you thinking?

一声轻柔的询问声后，人群安静下来，所有人都看向他们的领袖。
A single soft query hushes the noise, all eyes turning to their leader.

雅科夫：……
Yakov: ...

雅科夫：我的意见是……
Yakov: I'd say ...

坐席车厢

另一侧的隔离车厢则要显得“安静”许多。
The other isolation car is quieter.

除了偶尔从外面传来的、堪比战争前线的枪炮轰鸣声以外。
Only distant gunfire breaks the silence, like the front line of war.

索尼娅：我感觉似乎不太对劲……
Sonya: This is all getting rather unnerving.

老妇人颤抖却仍旧不失仪态地放下手中精致的骨瓷茶杯。
The woman sets down her porcelain cup in a rattle. Yet she maintains an utter state of composure.

阿不思诺：难道是法国佬又攻进来了吗？！
Arbuthnot: Gunshots? Not another bleedin' war!

阿不思诺：我的枪……该死，我该带上……
Arbuthnot: Hell. I knew I should've brought my gun.

绅士警惕地四处张望，瞳孔不住颤动着。
The gentleman scans around them, his pupils twitching.

空心木：很好。看来我即将从一名杂志编辑转职成为战地记者。
Verity: So this is it, my career's turning point—magazine editor turned combat correspondent.

撰稿人终于舍得将头从笔记本中抬起。她走到车厢门前，朝外头瞟了一眼。
The editor finally closes her notebook, moving to the door for a peek.

血手印

一只血手忽然从窗外贴了上来，留下暗红的手印。
A bloody hand slaps against the window.

感染的乘客：呜呜……
Infected Passenger: Oh ...

乘客Ⅳ：哦！我的上帝啊，这是……这是……
Passenger IV: Oh, my! What on earth is that?

还原

空心木：是刚才见过的“感染种”？我倒不知道这还是可以量产的东西。
Verity: More of those Infected? Wasn't aware you could mass-produce such a thing.

编辑走到身侧的窗前，望向驻军扎营的方向。
The editor peers out further, toward the soldiers' camp.

士兵们匆忙地来回进出，不时高声喊叫和挥舞着什么。
Men rush back and forth, shouting, waving, losing all sense of order.

视线飘到更远的一栋灰色建筑。从那里正不时跑出来一些人影，他们尖声咆哮着，在雪地上留下一连串的暗红血迹。
Her eyes drift past them to a gray building. Figures burst out, shrieking, trailing blood across the snow.

一部分融入了远处幽暗的树林中，另一部分则向着列车的方向奔来。
Some wander into the forest; others charge toward the train.

空心木：看样子像是驻军的仓库……感染种都是从这里跑出来的？
Verity: That must be the station warehouse. Is that where these Infected are coming from?

空心木：从隔离到现在已经过去了将近两个小时。这期间究竟发生了什么……
Verity: It's only been two hours since the quarantine began. What's gone wrong?

撰稿人暗自思忖着，耳畔又传来一阵高亢的尖叫。
The editor frowns; another scream rings sharp in her ear.

感染种扒车门

乘客们：——！！
Stowaways: ...!

Arbuthnot: Ah? Oh.

感染的乘客：进来。进……

Passenger IV: The door won't hold for long. Get something to block it!

玻璃碎裂

Stowaways: Ah!

Verity: What are you all standing there for? Get out of the way.

从硝烟中走出一群人影。他们荷枪实弹，神情疲惫，脸上沾满了血迹。
Through the smoke, armed figures emerge, faces pale and bloodied.

塞梅尔维斯：嘶……肩膀似乎拉伤了。
Semmelweis: Ah. Think I strained my shoulder.

告死鸟：我早就警告过了，霰弹枪不适合你。
Corvus: I did warn you. Someone your size can't handle a shotgun.

塞梅尔维斯：呵……对付成堆扑来的感染种，手枪的威力还不够让我足够优雅地死去。
Semmelweis: Well, you can hardly expect me to take them down one by one with a pistol.

空心木：各位是打算抢劫吗？丑话说在前面，现在我身上一分钱都没有。
Verity: If this is some kind of robbery, then I'm afraid you'll be disappointed. A writer always travels light.

告死鸟：不，我们是来向各位请求协助的。
Corvus: It isn't. We want your help.

告死鸟：……事情就是这样。边境站的驻军已经被血食怪感染了，军队带走了不少乘客。
Corvus: That is all we know. Most of the soldiers stationed here have been infected. Many passengers have become their captives.

告死鸟：多亏了他们的鼎力相助，我们才能突破感染种的包围，来到这里救出你们。
Corvus: It's thanks to their help that we made it this far.

她向身旁的难民乘客们颔首示意。
She nods toward the refugees beside her.

雅科夫：我们只是为了还列车长一个人情。
Yakov: Just repaying a favor. Think nothing of it.

雅科夫：她不求回报地帮助许多同胞抵达布达佩斯。光凭这一点，我们愿意帮她。
Yakov: She's helped so many people get to Budapest and asked for nothing in return. She'll have our support no matter what.

乘客Ⅲ：嘶……竟然加挂了车厢……
Passenger III: An extra carriage.

乘客Ⅳ：看上去真可怕……他们是刚从战壕里出来的吗？
Passenger IV: They look like they just climbed straight out of the trenches or something.

人们不安地交头接耳。眼前扛着枪的不速之客在他们眼里几乎就是贫穷与危险的代名词。
They whisper uneasily. To them, these unkempt and unruly strangers with rifles look no less monstrous than the creatures they had vanquished.

索尼娅：不管怎么说……感谢诸位的帮助。
Sonya: Well, in any case, we appreciate you rescuing us.

索尼娅：等列车靠站后，我一定会安排我那粗心大意的管家为各位送上一份厚礼……
Sonya: Once we arrive, I'll be sure to arrange for gifts to be sent your way.

雅科夫：厚礼就不必了，一会儿注意跟紧点儿，别乱跑——现在我们可都是一条船上的人了。
Yakov: That won't be necessary, ma'am. Just stay close, and we'll get out of here together.

索尼娅：抱歉，我不明白您的意思。我们需要转移去别处吗？
Sonya: Pardon my confusion. You mean to say we're to leave this carriage?

告死鸟：没错。离开之前我们得先去车站的临时拘留室，救出被关押的其他乘客。
Corvus: Yes. We need to see if any of the passengers are still alive.

乘客们：什么？！
Stowaways: What?!

乘客Ⅲ：我们只是一群手无寸铁的旅客，和军队干架？你们是在开玩笑吧……
Passenger III: You're not seriously asking us to fight those soldiers, are you? Infected soldiers, even!

吵闹声未见停歇。混乱中，一个孩子小心翼翼地从人群的缝隙中钻了出来。
The noise doesn't stop. In the chaos, a child squeezes out from the crowd.

小伊凡：列车长女士，您提到其他乘客……这也包括野树莓吗？我一直没有见到她……
Ivanushka: Um, Ms. Conductress, is Rubuska there, too? I still haven't seen her.

还没等告死鸟回答，又一个声音从背后响起。
Before Corvus can reply, another voice cuts in.

乘客Ⅳ：野树莓……你是指那个假血食怪吗？恐怕也被关起来了，她是最早被带走的乘客。
Passenger IV: Rubuska ... You mean that fake vampire? She was one of the first ones they took away.

小伊凡：假血食怪？可她明明有红眼睛和尖牙……
Ivanushka: Fake vampire? But she has red eyes and pointy teeth.

安娜贝尔：别听他们的！野树莓……她、她在我心里就是真正的血食怪！
Annabelle: Don't listen to her! Rubuska is a real vampire!

安娜贝尔：你认识野树莓。所以你也想和我一起救出她吗？
Annabelle: Are you one of her familiars too? Come on, let's rescue her together!

小伊凡：当然！
Ivanushka: Yes, let's!

小伊凡：她保护我们，还和我许下了约定……我们不能看着她身处险境。
Ivanushka: She protected us. I have to pay her back. We pinky promised.

索尼娅：哼。天真的孩子，你们不害怕外面的怪物吗？
Sonya: Hmph, children. Aren't you afraid of those monsters outside?

小伊凡&安娜贝尔：不怕！
Ivanushka & Annabelle: Never!

迫切而稚嫩的回答出乎所有人意料。
The bold, if childlike, answer surprises everyone.

拉伊哈：呵呵。瞧见了吗，就连孩子都比你们勇敢。
Reyhan: Haha, see? Even the kids have got more guts than you.

索尼娅：呃……
Sonya: You ...

阿不思诺：我、我们并非不能接受合作，可没有武器怎么行，总不能指望我们拿着刀叉冲锋吧？
Arbuthnot: It ain't that we're tryin' to get out of helpin', but we ain't got no weapons. What d'you expect us to do, fight 'em off with knives an' forks?

告死鸟：放心，我们早有准备。
Corvus: No need to worry about that.

列车长侧过身，让出一条路给身后的同伴。
She shifts aside, opening a path for her ally.

乘务员走上前，利索地解开身上携带的沉重麻袋，亮出里头乌泱泱闪着光的长枪短炮们，仿佛一位在市集向往来顾客们展示新鲜鲱鱼的渔民。
Aima steps forward, loosening a heavy sack, which pours out rifles and pistols into a motley assortment like a fisherman displaying his catch.

艾玛：大家可以按照自己的喜好挑一把武器！我带的都是方便上手的……
Aima: Take any you like. All the guns here are quite easy to handle. I picked them out myself.

阿不思诺：这……勃朗宁M1910！莫辛-纳甘！毛瑟C96！
Arbuthnot: An FN Model 1910! And this is a Mosin–Nagant! And a Mauser C96!

绅士兴奋地扑在麻袋前，贪婪的眼神一一舔过里面的存货。
The gentleman lunges into the pile with boyish glee.

阿不思诺：嗯，这把火力稳定，精准度高……不对，这把泵动流畅，射击更快……
Arbuthnot: This one's excellent—consistent firepower. But this beauty, she's got a smoother pump cycle—lovely for follow-up shots.

索尼娅：唉，这同那些时候又有什么变化？一个个的，都忙着送死。
Sonya: *sigh* Will the fighting ever cease?

老妇人发出一声哀叹。下一秒，她冷下脸，眼神是前所未有的冷酷。
The old woman sighs, then hardens. Her gaze turns ice-cold.

索尼娅：给我也来一把！重火力的！
Sonya: Alright, just pick one for me. Something with some punch!

TMW-18 吾血之血 / Blood of My Blood

枪
Against the rattle of gunfire outside, the warehouse seems unnervingly quiet.

与外面丝毫未见停歇的枪声相比，仓库则安静到近乎诡异。
The vampire's invitation still awaits a response. The girl bows her head, staring at her shadow.

车站仓库

血食怪的邀约尚未得到答复。女孩低着头，沉默地看着自己脚下的影子。

鲍里斯：我想我必须提醒你，血食怪的耐心远不及他的寿命来得要长。
Pyrrhos: Let me remind you that, although my life may be everlasting, my patience is not.

鲍里斯：而你此刻的犹豫……实在令人失望。
Pyrrhos: I have to say, your hesitation is disappointing.

野树莓：……
Rubuska: ...

野树莓：代价是什么？
Rubuska: What's this going to cost me?

她直视军官的双眼。
She looks into his crimson eyes.

野树莓：我一直是个很倒霉的人。
Rubuska: Every time I've been offered any kind of gift in my life, every time I've even come close to something ...

野树莓：通常落在我头上的好运，要么会被立刻收走，要么就是彻头彻尾的骗局。
Rubuska: It's either been taken away from me or turned out to be a complete fraud.

野树莓：先生，你的是哪一种呢？
Rubuska: So, sir, which one is it?

鲍里斯：都不是。我提供给你的，是血一样纯粹的现实。

塞梅尔维斯：这是，七十七分队的人，我的……我曾经的同僚们。
Semmelweis: Squad 77. All of them.

鲍里斯：是啊。我嫌他们碍事，早在他们上车前就一次性解决了。
Pyrrhos: Indeed. I worried they'd prove irksome if not dealt with, so I handled them before they even boarded the train.

暗红的眼眸轻描淡写地掠过调查员。
Dark red eyes sweep past her with casual indifference.

鲍里斯：没想到还漏了一个。
Pyrrhos: Though it seems one managed to slip her way on board.

告死鸟：为什么？
Corvus: Why, Pyrrhos? I need a reason.

鲍里斯：……
Pyrrhos: ...

鲍里斯：因为我对这一切都感到厌倦了，伊格丽卡。
Pyrrhos: If you must ask, Iglika, it's because I've run out of patience.

鲍里斯：无尽的战争、流浪、痛苦……那些愚蠢的人类和他们无休无止的征伐游戏。
Pyrrhos: People and their endless games, wars one after another, and following it—exile and despair.

鲍里斯：你知道这一切的根源是什么吗？
Pyrrhos: And do you know where it all began?

他拎起垂在身侧的一只柔软无力的手臂，任由鲜血顺着肌肉的弧度汩汩流下。
He hoists a limp arm; blood streams down it like a red river.

鲍里斯：血。我们脚下的土地流淌着太多不同的血液。
Pyrrhos: Blood. Too many bloodlines are bound to this land, each serving their own desires.

鲍里斯：无法融合，无法消失，只能相互侵蚀、撕咬，彼此仇恨，在这片被诅咒的土地上生生不息地纠缠着。
Pyrrhos: For centuries, they have nipped and snapped at each other, unable to cooperate, unwilling to unite, never satisfied with peace.

鲍里斯：为了打破这一切，我尝试了各种方法……包括加入解放阵线。
Pyrrhos: I tried to break them free from this cycle—did everything I could, including joining the Liberation Front.

告死鸟：你本可以选择告诉我这些。
Corvus: You could've told me this. We could've talked about it.

鲍里斯：这没什么好说的，伊格丽卡。
Pyrrhos: Oh, I could have, Iglika, but why use words when it is already clear to see?

鲍里斯：你只需要站在那里，闭上双眼，感受着脚下土地哭声一样的脉动，就什么都明白了。
Pyrrhos: Don't you hear it? When you close your eyes at night, don't you feel the distant tremors of their cries?

鲍里斯：后来，在你离开之后……在曾经的同志们都不再活动之后。
Pyrrhos: After you left the Liberation Front, after all others had forgotten how to even speak of our cause ...

鲍里斯：那位来自远方的歌者听到了我的祈祷，为我指引了一条新的道路……
Pyrrhos: A voice came to me. A voice from the heavens. She heard my prayers and showed me a new path.

他一手指向身后堆叠的尸体们，眼神炽热。
He gestures toward the mound of bodies, eyes blazing.

鲍里斯：一条让我们血脉相连的道路！所有人都成为血食怪，没有隔阂与冲突，只有彼此的理解与共鸣——
Pyrrhos: A path of unity! Where all would share the same blood, the same interest, the same goal.

“砰——！”

枪声响起的瞬间，军官原地消失，子弹只来得及击中几只蝙蝠的虚影。
At the crack of gunfire, Pyrrhos vanishes, the shot clipping only a few fluttering bats.

蝙蝠冲脸

下一秒，他又悄无声息地出现在告死鸟背后。
In only a heartbeat, he reappears soundlessly behind Corvus.

鲍里斯：第二枪。这可真叫人伤心啊，伊格丽卡。
Pyrrhos: Another bullet. You wound me in more ways than one, Iglika.

告死鸟：你错得离谱，鲍里斯。你以为血脉真的能终结一切冲突？
Corvus: You've lost your way, Pyrrhos. Do you truly think blood is to blame for all of this?

告死鸟：人与人之间冲突永远不会结束。它不仅来自血脉，也来自误解、恐惧……甚至是爱。
Corvus: It's one cause of conflict, yes, but so are misunderstanding, fear, even love.

告死鸟：血脉只是其中很小的部分。将一切都归结于此，这是彻头彻尾的逃避。
Corvus: To blame everything on bloodlines means choosing a simple lie over a complicated truth.

鲍里斯：呵呵……你还是那么容易被表象迷惑。误解，恐惧，爱——这一切都源于我们内心的本能。
Pyrrhos: Haha, you haven't thought deeply enough then, dear Iglika. Look at these causes, examine them at the root, and what do you find, hm? Human nature.

鲍里斯：而驱使这本能的钥匙，正是血脉。
Pyrrhos: And our nature, old friend, is set by our blood.

血食怪站在血肉铸就的山丘前，张开双臂，眼神也变得炽热。
The vampire spreads his arms before the hill of flesh, his maddened eyes ablaze with baleful violence.

鲍里斯：想象一下，伊格丽卡！想象一个没有流血的世界。
Pyrrhos: Listen to me! Imagine a world with no bloodshed,

鲍里斯：当所有人都摆脱了自己的肉体局限，平等地生活在永生之中……
Pyrrhos: where everyone is free of mortal weakness and given infinite time to enjoy the pleasures of this earth.

鲍里斯：每一滴血都将是彼此之间的纽带，所有的心跳与呼吸，将为同一个目标而存在。
Pyrrhos: Our shared bloodline serving as a bond, not a line of division, so that all our hearts might beat as one.

鲍里斯：无论你身在何方，肤色如何，血脉都会将我们连成一个庞大的家族，永远不再有敌人。
Pyrrhos: Race, color, creed—all would melt away in the face of this great family we will create.

鲍里斯：而这，不正是我们所希望的吗？
Pyrrhos: Was that not your vision once, Iglika?

告死鸟：一个没有流血的世界？这里的血已经够多了。
Corvus: You want a world without bloodshed? Hah. Ironic. Your methods tell a different story.

告死鸟：看看这满地的狼藉吧，鲍里斯。你正在创造另一种形式的战争，而非终结它。
Corvus: Look around you, Pyrrhos. You're starting a war, not ending one.

告死鸟：你根本不在乎所谓的“理解与共鸣”。你只是一个吃不到糖，就想拉它一起坠入地狱的孩子。
Corvus: Unity, really? Things didn't go your way, so now you'll drag us all to hell along with you.

鲍里斯：……
Pyrrhos: ...

月光驱散了所有华丽的矫饰，在血食怪脸上降下苍白的帷幕。
Moonlight strips away all pretense, casting a pallid veil across his face.

鲍里斯：你永远都知道该怎么伤害我，并对此毫无顾忌。
Pyrrhos: You always did know how to use those words like a scalpel.

鲍里斯：我不该对你有所期待的，伊格丽卡。
Pyrrhos: *sigh* I was a fool to think you'd stand with me again.

他轻叹一口气，眼神落在另一侧的乘务员身上。
He sighs, turning his eyes with strange softness toward the stewardess.

鲍里斯：艾玛。
Pyrrhos: Aima.

鲍里斯：来吧，到我身边。接下来会是一场恶战，你是我的血亲，我不想伤到你。

塞梅尔维斯：血亲？原来……
Semmelweis: His blood? She's ...

调查员的目光在乘务员和列车长之间流连，离散的线索在她脑内串联了起来。
Semmelweis darts her eyes from face to face, loose threads knitting in her mind.

被唤及名字的乘务员下意识向前一步。所有人的目光都集中在了这个从来都只会默默跟随的女孩身上。
Aima steps forward as every eye turns to her.

艾玛：鲍里斯叔叔……
Aima: Uncle Pyrrhos ...

野树莓：艾玛……！
Rubuska: Aima!

听见身后的呼唤，女孩停下脚步。

她回望身后的人们，红色围巾毛茸茸的触感划过她的脸颊。
She looks back, the woolly red scarf brushing her cheek.

于是她攥紧围巾，缓慢而坚定地直视军官的眼睛。
She grips it tight, slowly and firmly locking with her uncle's eyes.

艾玛：对不起，叔叔。你是我的血亲，是我一直心怀感激的人……但我不能过去。
Aima: Forgive me, Uncle. I love you dearly, and I'm grateful for all you've done. But I can't.

Aima: You know how much the "Danube Dawn" means to me. Please, stop. I don't want anyone else to get hurt.

她回到了属于她的人群中间。
She steps back to stand proud and defiant among her people.

鲍里斯：我的血亲……连你也要背叛我吗？还有你们……
Pyrrhos: Blood of my blood. Of all people, you choose to stand against me. And you ...

男人、女人、老人、孩子……人们隔着不远不近的距离看着他，眼里充斥着恐惧、厌恶和鄙夷。
Men, women, the old, the young ... each stands ready from a measured distance, brimming with fear, disgust, and scorn.

这些眼神砌成一堵沉默的高墙，将他隔绝在外。高墙之下，是一道不可逾越的鸿沟，一切解释和辩驳都将在其中湮灭殆尽。
They build a silent wall, cutting him off. Beneath it yawns a chasm no words could ever cross.

鲍里斯：呵呵……你们看着我的眼神，就好像我是什么不可理喻的怪物一样。
Pyrrhos: Hahahahaha. You look at me like I'm some kind of monster!

他神经质地笑了起来，随后深吸一口气，又恢复了以往的平静。
He laughs with a twitch, then inhales deeply and resumes his malevolent composure.

鲍里斯：我早就明白了，根本不存在所谓的“理解与共鸣”。
Pyrrhos: Well, I tried, but I always knew preaching would only get me so far.

鲍里斯：暴力、宗教、和平谈判，甚至血脉……一切手段到最后都会显得滑稽又可笑，根本撼动不了这片土地与生俱来的、无可救药的分裂与堕落。
Pyrrhos: Violence, religion, politics, marriage ... Our predecessors sought every means to unite us, but greed has always been stronger.

鲍里斯：我也曾幻想过，某一天我们能抛开仇恨，联合起来。但是，历史和今天给了我们什么？
Pyrrhos: Still, I was naive enough to hope we'd finally put aside our differences.

鲍里斯：废墟、血染的战场，在故乡的每一块石板下，都埋着无数的悲剧与血债。呵呵……呵呵呵……
Pyrrhos: Ruins, battlefields, countless headstones, and beneath every one, a blood debt unpaid. Hah ... Hahaha ...

鲍里斯：伊格丽卡，有一件事你说对了。
Pyrrhos: Perhaps, in the end, you were right, Iglika. If I can't have what I want ...

他低下头，慢慢抽出裸露在胸口外的那截木桩。
He reaches to pull out the wooden stake lodged in his chest.

肉色的蝠翼从他的背脊破裂而出，缓缓张开，遮住了窗外朦胧的月色。
Fleshy bat wings sprout from his back, spreading wide to block out the hazy moonlight outside the window.

鲍里斯：现在我只想拉着这片土地，还有这片土地上的人们一起……
Pyrrhos: Then I will drag every single man, woman, and child.

鲍里斯：坠入地狱。
Pyrrhos: To hell.

怪物“鲍里斯”发出一声尖锐的鸣叫，赤红的双目血流如注。
The monster lets out a shrill cry, eyes streaming blood.

叫声如同一道致命的信号，在夜空中扩散开来，吸引了无数在外游荡的感染种们。
The sound spreads through the night like a deadly signal, drawing hordes of the Infected in from the dark.

感染的乘客：血流如注……血流如注！
Infected Passenger: Gushing, seething!

Infected Soldier: Nevermore!

Semmelweis: The Infected are swarming. He must have called for them.

告死鸟：拿起武器，作好迎战准备！
Corvus: Incoming! Weapons ready!

告死鸟：鲍里斯……今天，我会亲手用子弹贯穿你的心脏。

血色墓园

村民Ⅰ：喂，还活着吗？
Villager I: Is the beast still breathing? Hey, you!

青年鲍里斯：……
Young Pyrrhos: ...

村民Ⅰ：这家伙可真邪门儿啊。被钉在木桩上晒了一个星期太阳，血都快流干了，还是没死。
Villager I: Devil take him, he's still twitching, even after we staked him and left him under the sun for a week. He ought to be dust by now.

村民Ⅰ：不愧是纯种的血食怪，上一个才三天就没了。
Villager I: The last one didn't last but three days. This one must be of purer blood. They say those are stronger.

青年鲍里斯：为……为什么……

村民Ⅱ：人在剿灭害虫的时候，还会一个一个区分它们的好赖吗？
Villager II: What, so we've got to wait until you've drained someone dry before we put you down, do we?

他被阳光刺得再也抬不起眼，只能徒劳地缩着脖子、低着头。
The sunlight burns him until he can no longer raise his eyes. He shrinks his neck, attempting to turn his head in vain.

血食怪的狩猎向来血腥。人类的、牲畜的、血食怪的血在地上杂乱地流淌着，又在末端合成了一条小小的溪流，洇湿了他的足趾。
A vampire's hunt is a bloody one, as always. Human, beast, vampire—blood spills in a tangled mess across the ground, merging into a stream that soaks his toes.

一阵风轻轻吹起，捎带来遥远的歌声。
A breeze stirs, carrying a distant song.

歌声空灵而缥缈，仿佛从一个庞大而无垠的空间内飘来，再编织成复杂的网，温柔地上下起伏着。
The song is ethereal and light, as if drifting from a vast, boundless space, weaving into a comforting net that rises and falls.

如歌的声音：绝望。
Sing-Song Voice: Despair.

如歌的声音：这是最纯粹的情感。它剖开你的防备，将你从庸常的束缚中解脱出来，让你变得更加……完美。
Sing-Song Voice: The purest of emotions. It lifts the weight of fear, frees you from the constraints of mundanity, and brings you one step closer to perfection.

青年鲍里斯：谁……？
Young Pyrrhos: Who ...?

他闻到、听到干净而凉爽的风声。

如歌的声音：帮你实现愿望的存在。

Sing-Song Voice: I shall help you achieve greatness, and you will be surrounded by family and friends, never to be alone again.

如歌的声音：而这一切，是为了让你变得更加完美——完美的绝望，完美的激情。

青年鲍里斯：家人……没错，我希望……

<speed=2>Not on the battlefield, nor in a field of slaughter, nor in hollow declarations. It lives in every moment, here and now.

Its painted smile is unchanged, as if it still remembers the winds along the Danube, the swaying of the train, the murmurs and laughter of her journey.

如今，它的旅程终于结束了。
Now its journey has come to an end.

它该回到属于它的地方了——一个没有隔阂、没有流离的世界。
It should return to where it belongs, a world without walls, without exile.

或许，它会在那里找到属于自己的答案。
Perhaps there it will find its answer.

Little William: Oh, me too! Me too!

多萝西：随意向他人索要礼物，这实在太失礼了……都给我回来！
Dorothy: Such naughty children! Who taught you it was appropriate to demand gifts from others like that?

家庭教师严厉的呵斥很快被淹没在孩童一声高过一声的欢呼中。
The governess's stern scolding is drowned out by their joyous shouts.

多萝西：实在抱歉。是我没有教导好他们……
Dorothy: I do apologize. I don't know where their manners have gone.

野树莓：没关系！我愿意送礼物，他们愿意收礼物，这样岂不是皆大欢喜？
Rubuska: *chuckle* No need to worry, ma'am. I'd love to send them some things. It would make me more than happy.

多萝西：……
Dorothy: ...

多萝西：感谢你，野树莓小姐。我们也一定会准备回礼的。
Dorothy: You're very kind, Ms. Rubuska. I'll be sure they prepare something for you in return.

送别了叽叽喳喳的云雀们，女孩长舒一口气。
Bidding farewell to the chattering children, Rubuska lets out a long-held breath.

野树莓：这下必须得努力打工了，不然光是每年的礼物钱就能叫我破产……
Rubuska: Right, now I really need to work hard. Ruby eyes and fangs don't pay for themselves.

塞梅尔维斯：如果你有兴趣，我可以介绍基金会的派遣工作给你。
Semmelweis: I may have some errands from the Foundation that would suit you, if you're willing.

塞梅尔维斯：虽然不能保证工作内容符合心意，但百分之百报酬丰厚。
Semmelweis: I won't say they'll be easy, but they pay well.

野树莓：呜哇，真的吗！
Rubuska: Y-You mean it?

塞梅尔维斯：当然。三位都已经在基金会做过登记了，按照条约，我不会限制你们的行动自由。
Semmelweis: Of course. Now that the three of you are registered with the Foundation, you're free to lead your lives as you wish.

塞梅尔维斯：包括你们愿意替谁工作。
Semmelweis: That includes deciding who you'll work for.

告死鸟：就这么简单？没有别的流程了？
Corvus: Is that all? Your procedures were quicker than I expected.

艾玛：是、是呀……我差点儿以为你要把我们都抓起来呢。
Aima: F-For a moment, I thought you'd take us away to the Foundation and lock us up.

塞梅尔维斯：我的确有这个想法。
Semmelweis: I admit I did toss the idea around.

女孩们：嗯？！
Girls: Huh?!

塞梅尔维斯：不过随着调查的深入，我必须遗憾地通知大家……
Semmelweis: But after a thorough investigation, I regret to say ...

调查员眨眨眼，露出一个神秘的微笑。
She blinks with the flash of a secret smile.

塞梅尔维斯：是我的情报有误。
Semmelweis: That our intelligence was faulty.

塞梅尔维斯：“多瑙黎明号”上不存在血食怪，那只是一个传言，以讹传讹的传言。
Semmelweis: There are no vampires aboard the "Danube Dawn." It's safe to dismiss the reports as no more than a rumor.

野树莓：“头儿”，你可差点儿又吓坏我们啦！
Rubuska: Oh, real funny, "boss." You nearly gave me a heart attack!

女孩们的笑声轻轻飘起，又消散在如潮水般的人流中。
The girls' laughter drifts up, then scatters into the tide of people.

塞梅尔维斯：好，那我的任务到此就结束了。
Semmelweis: Right then, it looks like my mission ends here.

塞梅尔维斯：下一站你们要去哪里？
Semmelweis: Where are you headed next?

告死鸟：进城去。我们进城去，去伊斯坦布尔。
Corvus: To the city. Istanbul.

塞梅尔维斯：你说的是……伊斯坦布尔？你们还要折返回去吗？
Semmelweis: Really? Heading back so soon?

列车长顿了一下，脸上难得露出笑意。
Corvus pauses, amusement softening her battle-scarred face.

告死鸟：这只是个玩笑。好吧，我们其实是要去维也纳。
Corvus: But our next stop is Vienna.

告死鸟：准确的说法是，“回”维也纳。有些乘客在维也纳下车。
Corvus: We have some passengers who need to get off there.

塞梅尔维斯：那这趟车还会再去东方吗？
Semmelweis: Any plans to head east again from Budapest?

告死鸟：在战争结束之前都会的，还有很多人需要我们的帮助。
Corvus: As long as these wars rage on, there will be people who need our help.

塞梅尔维斯：愿你一切顺利，列车长。不管是你们的“秘密行动”，还是未完的理想。
Semmelweis: I wish you all the best, Conductress, with your "secret operation" and with the dream you're chasing.

告死鸟：谢谢。一定会的。
Corvus: Thank you. I intend to see it happen.

告死鸟：我手下现在有两个血食怪伙计，我们离胜利又更近了一步。
Corvus: And we're making progress. Especially now that I can count on not just one but two vampires to assist me.

她指向一左一右两名“血食怪伙计”。
She points toward the two "vampires" at her side.

塞梅尔维斯：既然这样，那我就放心了。
Semmelweis: Haha, indeed. I can only conclude that things will improve from here.

塞梅尔维斯：再会，如果真的还有那一天的话。
Semmelweis: Perhaps we'll meet again, if we're lucky.

她微笑着朝大家挥了挥手，转身离去。
She smiles, waves to the crowd, and turns away.

野树莓：呼……我还以为她真的要绑走我们呢。
Rubuska: Phew. I honestly thought she meant it when she said she'd lock us up.

野树莓：血食怪可不是什么要被收容进监狱的危险目标！
Rubuska: Vampires aren't meant to be locked up in a cell.

艾玛：但是，如果再给你一次机会的话……小树莓，你会想成为血食怪吗？
Aima: I'm curious, Rubi. If you were given another chance to become a vampire, would you take it?

血红色的眼珠转了又转，最后落在艾玛身上。
Ruby eyes dance around and find their rest when they meet Aima's face.

野树莓：成为？为什么要成为，我现在不就是吗～
Rubuska: Given a chance? Mm. I don't need "a chance." I am a vampire!

野树莓：血食怪野树莓，可是“多瑙黎明号”上最最可怕的生物！
Rubuska: Haven't you heard of me? The nightmare haunting the "Danube Dawn," the terrifying monster—Rubuska the vampire!

野树莓：别看她毫不起眼，如果有谁敢欺负车上的乘客，野树莓会让他们见识到什么是真正的恐惧……
Rubuska: She prowls the train, looking for anyone who might cause trouble. And if they do, she'll see them punished.

野树莓：调查员？神秘学家？列车长？统统不值一提！
Rubuska: Investigators? Arcanists? The conductress herself? Hah! She can take them all single-handedly!

野树莓：野树莓的影子伙伴会将他们通通吃进肚子里……
Rubuska: And her shadow friends will gobble up anyone who dares stand in her way!

野树莓：哈啊——！
Rubuska: Ah-ha!

野树莓：欸啊啊啊啊啊——
Rubuska: Aaaah—

野树莓被拎起

告死鸟：不值一提？
Corvus: "Single-handedly," you say?

告死鸟：现在，不值一提的列车长命令你去打扫第五车厢的车窗。
Corvus: Let's see how our "monster" manages her chores first. The fifth carriage windows need wiping.

野树莓：打、打扫？这怎么行……
Rubuska: Ch-Chores? How could you do this to me!

告死鸟：是谁说自己什么都愿意做，只要肯让她留在“多瑙黎明号”上？
Corvus: Funny; I recall someone saying they'd do anything to stay on the train.

野树莓：那、那也不能让尊贵的血食怪干这种事，不能……！
Rubuska: Well, yeah, but, we can't have a noble vampire scrubbing windows. We just can't.

一束阳光穿透晨雾，温暖地照在车站每个人的身上。
A beam of sunlight pierces the morning fog, warming everyone at the station.

列车长沐浴在金色的晨光中，神情也变得柔和。
Bathed in gold, the conductress's scarred features soften.

告死鸟：好了，这只是个玩笑。但我必须强调，“多瑙黎明号”上的工作可不是闲差。
Corvus: Jokes aside, I must be clear—working on the "Danube Dawn" is no easy task.

告死鸟：我给你的那本《员工手册》必须牢记于心。先从第一条背起，我会随时抽查……
Corvus: You will learn the service manual by heart. And I will be testing you, so you'd better start reading.

车站人流如织，乘客们行色匆匆，无人在意眼前三人的小小互动。
The station bustles; soon-to-be passengers rush past, oblivious to the small exchange.

列车长和她的乘务员们刚刚经历了一个血腥的夜晚，又开始准备并期待着未来的旅途。
After a night steeped in death and violence, the conductress and her crew brace themselves for a renewed journey.

她们依然憧憬着那些金色的、洒满晨光的日子。
Still, they dream of these days painted gold by the morning sun.

基金会客房

塞梅尔维斯：我于一九一二年十一月三十日登上“多瑙黎明号”列车，结识了神秘学家乘客野树莓与列车长“告死鸟”等人。
Semmelweis: On November 30th, 1912, I boarded the "Danube Dawn" and encountered a young arcanist named Rubuska and the conductress of the train, Corvus, among others.

塞梅尔维斯：在尼卡检查站，与之共同挫败了投靠重塑之手的血食怪军官鲍里斯的阴谋，阻止了感染种危机扩散，并协助列车顺利驶入奥匈帝国境内。
Semmelweis: At the Nika checkpoint, we stopped Pyrrhos, a vampire and army officer affiliated with Manus Vindictae, and foiled his scheme to infect the greater population, after which the train successfully entered the territory of Austria-Hungary.

塞梅尔维斯：血食怪。
Semmelweis: "Vampire" ...

她停下笔，看着自己写下的似是而非的报告记录。
She stops writing, staring at the report before her. Half-truths have become a specialty of hers.

塞梅尔维斯：把真话说一半，呵呵，那就不算是假的咯。
Semmelweis: It hardly counts as "forging reports" if I simply leave out a few details.

塞梅尔维斯：至少我可以保证，这些事情是真实发生过的。
Semmelweis: All that I've written is true. It just "didn't occur to me" to include some minor details.

基金会职员：塞梅尔维斯小姐。
Foundation Staff Member: Ms. Semmelweis.

塞梅尔维斯：请放心，我今天一定能写完这份材料。
Semmelweis: No need to worry. I'll turn in the report by the end of the day.

基金会职员：啊，我不是来催你的。
Foundation Staff Member: Oh, I'm not here for the report.

塞梅尔维斯：嗯？
Semmelweis: Hm?

基金会职员：从维也纳出差回来的同事带了礼物，托我给你送一份。
Foundation Staff Member: Our office in Vienna received a gift. They were asked to pass it along to you.

职员小姐把一份小小的礼物盒挂在门口，随即悄悄离开。
The young clerk leaves a small gift box by the door and slips away.

塞梅尔维斯：这是……一份礼物，难道说？
Semmelweis: A gift? Could it be ...?

她放下笔，走向门边，用指甲划开信封，取出信纸。
She slices the letter open with her fingernail.

歪歪扭扭的字迹，右下角滴着如蜡印般的、浓稠的两滴血点。
The scrawl is uneven, the corner stained with two thick drops of blood like a wax seal.

塞梅尔维斯：“致圣洛夫基金会的塞梅尔维斯女士。”
Semmelweis: "Dear Ms. Semmelweis of the St. Pavlov Foundation."

接着，她看向冗长而调皮的落款。
Then her eyes fall on the illustrious, overlong, and entirely playful signature.

“瓦拉几亚大公阿诺德五世的末裔，初代埃杰什公爵萨瓦诺维奇及多瑙河畔埃杰什城堡之唯一继承人，阿诺德六世之女……”
"The youngest descendant of Arnold V, Voivode of Wallachia; true heir of Savonovic, first Duke of Arges; rightful lady of Castle Arges, daughter of Arnold VI ..."

“本世纪最最勇敢的血食怪，野树莓，从布达佩斯向你问候！”
"... and the bravest vampire of the century, Rubuska, sends her regards!"
